O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You noble sons, I have completed this book which is the last of the science of medicine along with its contents, and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it has come into my vision that I complete this for you with the treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is entirely lost everywhere, so that the science has perished and been destroyed, and nothing remains except for the small descriptions in books of the ancients which hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed up, and knowledge is removed.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Now it seems to me that I will bring it to life along with the organization of this treatise according to the way of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will also come along with the forms of cauterizing instruments and other tools of work with the joining of declaration and preparation of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because of this reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who undertakes this to ascend in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the joints of the members, and their forms, and conjunctions, and separations, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and veins, and the number of them, and their movements and rest, and the place of their origin.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because of this, says Hippocrates that a name with its name is much, and with the work is little; and likewise in the art of hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction to this book that whoever is not aware of the things previously said, should beware that he does not fall into error and harm men; thus as I have often told many others who undertake this science and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a foolish surgeon who cut out, that is to say, an abscess of the scrofula or neck of a woman, and cut the arteries of the neck; wherefore so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I have seen another surgeon who treated a stone from an old man's bladder, and the stone was large; so he carried off with him a part of the bladder, and the man died within three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I had already been called to treat him, and I saw the condition of the sick man and the largeness of the stone, and knew well that if he was cut for it, he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I have seen another surgeon who took on the care of a duke from our land who had a broken leg, and with the break, there was also an open wound; and the ignorant surgeon sewed up the break over the wound with very loose stitches, and did not leave any space for drainage, and left it in this way until the leg became mortified and the foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to come to him, and I hurried to come to loosen the leg; and when I had it untied, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But in all ways the corruption was already confirmed in the member, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to progress through the member until the entire limb had been lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I have seen another surgeon who burst an infected abscess, and then it inflamed through the malice of his treatment.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	When the chancre is pure of melancholic humour, it is not necessary to touch it with iron if it is in such a place that everything that is corrupted can be completely removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And therefore, dear son, it is necessary for you to know that manual work is divided into two divisions: that is to say, the work in which there is danger in various dispositions; and I will show in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	Why it is necessary that you take care of yourself, so that the foolish speaker will not speak ill of you If you take up arms in defense, and begin to treat your patients lightly but firmly, and use the best method, so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised; and leave frightening diseases with their bad health; and remove from yourselves what makes you doubt, and be strong within yourselves, so that you can come into this world with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The Galen says in one of his warnings: "Do not take on the treatment of a bad disease, lest you be called a foolish physician.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have composed this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about cauterization with fire and medical cauterization, and it is the chapter organized from head to toe; and of the forms of instruments, and the cauterizing irons, and of all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and venous bloodletting and wounds, and extracting arrowheads, and similar things; and it is the chapter that includes the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is organized from head to toe, and includes the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Therefore, so that we remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of the help and harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the qualities of aid and its usefulness are the longest word and most subtle science and secret answer; and many of the wise spoke about these things and agreed with them; and I suffice for my words, for I am wary of their length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that universal aid is to every temperament or body, whether it has matter, except for two temperaments: namely hot temperature with matter, and dry temperature with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry temperature with matter combined, they disagreed and said that cauterization is great aid; and the others said the contrary: that cauterization is not worth for diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be used to cure hot disease by heat, nor dryness; and those who said the contrary say that cauterization does great aid for hot and dry disease that comes into the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man and its moisture to the heat of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it to be true once before through experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And in any case, no one should intervene except for those who have proven it through experience and who know from long usage the recipe of cauterization, and the diversity of human temperaments, and their dispositions and causes of illnesses, and remedies and the pace of time; we are not afraid of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the physicians assembled and agreed on cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, my son, that fire used in cauterization is a secret of remedies, and of greater virtue than cauterization with burning medicines.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and it does not affect any other member except the one that is cauterized, and it harms no other part if you know how to name its place.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines spread from member to member by alienating them, and bring diseases with bad health to the afflicted member; and perchance they kill the patient. The fires, due to their height and the goodness of their substance, do not make those things happen, unless there is a superfluity.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experiment and the length of my service and study that I have devoted to this art, and it was on the truth of things; and because of this, I excuse myself for the length of my speech, for I do not like to take away from you the secret which is inherent in fire, and the quality of its work, how it beats back diseases of the body, as the philosopher says when he demonstrates it; so receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, my son, that they agreed on the time when cauterizations should be done, and chose patients.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is advisable in all times, because the ensuing harm is brought under control by the aid of cauterization; and indeed if the cauterizations are for necessary, urgent pains which cannot wait until more serious harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think that, dear son, what foolish doctors say; for the illness that is cured by cauterization has no relapse; and they say so themselves. But it's not true as they believe, because cauterizations are not just medicines that change the complexion, and dry out the humors that cause pain, but rather it's a medicine that moves quickly, because of its value, and because of the virtue of its work and its power.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And it's a great thing that the illness comes sometimes according to the complexion of the sick person and the place of the disease and its nature; and the superfluities are gathered in him through the consumption of meats and similar things, unless cauterizations are administered at the place where there is a lot of superfluity and moisture, such as cauterizations for dens pain and similar things, and that kind of pain does not come back. But it's true in some cases.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people don't understand why cauterizations are called the last resort of medicine, and that's true; but they don't think that cauterization is worth it after medicine, but their intentions are false. And I say that cauterization is the last resort of medicine because this: when we administer other methods of treatment for a disease and they fail to work, then we administer cauterization, and it succeeds.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Then it is clear that cauterization is the last of medicine, not according to the intention of foolish healers.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that a cauterizer made of gold is more poisonous than one made of iron, and they did not say this out of ignorance but due to the quality of gold and its high substance; and they said that the wounds from cauterization do not become putrid, but it's not true because I have experienced it, and I have found that it is true in some people; and a gold cauterizer is worth more than an iron one, as they also said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And besides, when you heat up an instrument made of gold, you don't know when it has heated enough because of the color of the gold, and it cools down at once; and if one heats it too much, it gets broken at the fire; and thus there is a lot of hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And because of that let's use iron cauterizers which we have made more suitable to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Now I have ordered this chapter from the top down to the bottom, so that it may be easier for you to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive cauterizer.
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These cauterizers are useful for moistening and cooling the head, and there are two of them that we use because of diseases called "soda", and because of many humors that descend from the head to the temples, ears, and throat, and because of a multitude of dreams and pains in the teeth and throat, and similarly for all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cauterizer is that the sick person should be purged by a medicinal solution that clarifies the head, either three or four times, depending on what virtues, age, and habit of the sick person can tolerate; and then reheat the head of the sick person.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit cross-legged between your hands, and put his hands on the balance scale; after that, place the root of your palm on the root of his nose, between his two eyes. Let your fingers come together so that he may bleed from the nose, then heat up the cauterizer called "olive" which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put him on the place marked with ink, and do in descending and stretching your hand little by little and twisting it around; then lift up your hand suddenly, and reward the place if you see the bone .i. a small piece of gold; and if you don't see it, then repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take .i. small handful of wool, and put in soft and moist cotton inside, and put on the place, and let him stay for .iij. days; afterwards put on damp cloth soaked in butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed; afterwards cure the wound with ointment called "tetrafarmacium", until he is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said the old man, that the longer stays open the wound, the more it purges itself; and because of this he advised him.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said one of them that you should burn the cautery so long that part of the bone is burned, and then redo what has been burned from the bone, and be healed.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And said the other that you should burn the cautery so long and put it so hard that it brings out of the bone as wide as a spindle that women put in their distaffs, so that the humors come out; and one should leave the wound open for a long time; then it should be cured and sewn.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of cauterization do not seem to me entirely good in all cases, except that they are used in some people who have access to fear; and it seems to me that I should leave them alone. For the bones are weakened by continuous natural solutions, as we witness in other members; and likewise when the bone of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first sign of cauterization is more safe and gentle for me, and I will use this method until a good recovery.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When pain in the head comes constantly and lasts long, the patient should use herbs and pills called "cochie", and purges of the head, oils, and plasters; and if one makes him the cauterization that we mentioned before, it is not worth it.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care if the patient's head is of strong constitution, and it is not too cold; then cauterize under that a small amount of what we said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After that, make cauterization on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we said before, and make one cauterization on the place called "vasselz"; and it is one place where you put a poultice; and hold your hand so close to the bone that you don't see anything: the patient feels a much greater pain in this cauterization than in the others, and I will speak of it later; and the cauterizations on the horns should be finer than those on the middle part of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	From the cauterization of the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When a sudden pain comes from one part of the head and the disease is spread to the eye and the head is purged by medicinal purges and all the other treatments that I have said in the division of diseases have been done and none of these things help: then he makes cauterizations in two ways, namely with hot medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with hot medicine is that you take a dose of almond paste (alz), remove the skin and recollect it into one small amount for two eyes, then pour the almond paste into the temple where the pain is located in such a way that you can place it under the skin; and when it has been placed there, tie and bind it well and leave it thus for 12 hours; then untie it and let the almond paste ooze out of it, and let the wound be left thus for two or three days; then put on a cotton cloth dipped in oil so that it oozes.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After that, apply a poultice until it is healed; and if you see fit to make any of the purging medicines that I have written about or to treat with purging medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron cautery is thus done.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it is the shape:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And it is called "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a nail or small hook, and in the middle has a slight appearance; and you put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, until the midpoint of the burn is scorched; and lift your hand so that the vein does not burn, which is far away, and there flows an abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	Then put cotton on top of the silk thread, and leave it for three days; then I put wet cotton in the burrow, and then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery called "cultellare", do so at all points, and be careful not to cover the artery in this migraine which is not ancient.
de emigraine	migraine headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you cure migraine as we have said before in the divisions of diseases, and it does not help, and you see that the cauteries from medicine and iron do not work for it, then it is necessary that you heat up the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and then sign over the painful place a line of half a finger in length, and take your hand away once, and pull back so that you do not hit the artery and get close to the bone; and be careful of the jawbone that moves when one eats, and the nerves do not get damaged so that spasms do not come to the patient, and be careful of the bleeding from the artery when it is cut, or if there is great fear or especially in someone who does not know what they are doing and has no experience; and leave the work to those more skilled. But I will tell you how to stop bloodshed when the artery is cut, and I will show you where to find this in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not help the disease, and the patient is suffering, then cauterize in the head as well, just like we have said, and cure the wound until it is healed; and if you want to, administer the cautery that we have mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery, with the cautery that has two blades; and this cautery is better and more helpful than the previous one.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	Dolor des oreilles (ear pain) due to cold or chill.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When in the ear comes pain from cold, and we have worked on it with medicinal solutions and other cures that we have said in the division, and the pains do not move, then warm this cautery which is called "point", because of its form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, point the entire circumference of the ailing ear, or around both if the pain is in both, and take out one spot above the root of the ear after you have marked its place; and make ten points on each ear; after cure the place as much as it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Torture which must be cured by cautery is none other than those that move with foam, such as we have said in the division of diseases; and do not make a cautery for appearances that come from scorched and spume of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture that moves with foam of yellow and purging of head and gurgling, and it is not effective, then it is necessary for you to cauterize the ailing person with three cauters: one in the root of the ear, and another a little behind the temple, and the third at the joining of the two lips; and put the cautery on the part that appears healthy, and make the cautery near the top of the head of the ear above a little below the horn of the head, and another in the temple as long as a finger's breadth; and leave the cautery so high up that the middle of the burn is charred; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the shape of the knife that we have placed before, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the blade be a little thicker; after that, cure the place as I have said before, until it is healed.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in the way that we have said, and it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauters: two on the two horns of the head, and one in the middle of the head, and one at the place which is called "vasselz" as we have said before, and the last cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured as we have said before.
de litargie	of lethargy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	To this disease it is necessary to give the ailing person great doses of purging pills for the brain; after that, rinse the head of the patient thoroughly, and put on the occipital bone an ointment of mustard which is written in the treatise on plasters; and this is the form of the cautery: if one makes it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healed in this way, then it is good; and if not, then make three cauters inside the head descending just below the neck, with a span of two fingers between each cautery; and cure it as the others, and if you see that it needs to be joined, and the patient is suffering, then make one cautery in the middle; and if necessary, two others on the two horns, and cure them until they are healed; and this is the form of the cautery which is called "olivare", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the coldness of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be purified with years and with what we have said before; after that, rinse the head of the patient, then make cauters inside the head and on each horn, and one last one and three on the spine of the neck; and if you think it needs more, and the body is moist and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, then make four cauters on the spine of the back; and leave them until the most of the burn is charred, and lift your hand; after that, cure them until they are healed, and this is the form of the cautery which is called "olivare" that we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should not use cauterization unless the person is phlegmatic, and it is necessary to purify the brain first with years and other remedies that we have said in the section on how to treat a patient who is old and suffering from strong medication.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer [the cauterization], then make them gargle and chew on a purifying remedy for the brain often with good meats; after that, rinse the head in the middle, and I will make one cautery according to what we have said before, and one cautery on the vassel (a type of vertebra), and on each horn; and if the patient is severe and suffering, then make cauterizations as I said to someone who has paralysis and softening of the body, on the spine of the back and of the neck, and this is the form of the olive cautery according to the manner that I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is an infant, then make one subtle cautery in this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When because of melancholy the superfluities or moistures are corrupted and there is great phlegm, then the caustic of thread cautery as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if because of melancholy the superfluities decline to melancholy, and the body of the patient is moist, then he should drink something by which the brain will be cleansed, according to what it was before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then wash the head of the patient; then make one cloth of flax well made, also like a circle, if he puts it on the head; and the patient should be crossed and held tightly from all sides; then present the liniment, and wait a few hours until the balm of old thyme hardens; and heat it with temperate fire, so that the dough can bear to have it poured in; then empty the circle inside the head and let it cool; and do this for the patient once a week with another good government, as long as they are cured.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	Or if you wish to cauterize him, make several pointed marks all over the cautery.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterizing moistens the brain equally; and then put on damp cotton in lard and goose fat.
de l’awe des eulz	Il semble que la phrase se termine là ! "De l'eau des eulx" est une expression qui signifie "d'une eau pure et saine", mais je n'ai pas trouvé de texte complémentaire pour continuer le passage. Si vous avez d'autres phrases à partager, je serais ravi de les lire !
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	Quant awe vient premierement as eulz... Ah, merci ! C'est comme ça que continuaient les phrases !
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After commanding the patient to rear their head, and doing a fire cautery in the head, and making two cauteries on the two temples if the descent of the humour is at both eyes together, or in one if it is at one; and cut through all the veins and arteries that are under the skull, and make the cautery long according to the breadth of the temple; and beware of bloodshed, and if you see too much blood come out, stop with such power as you have.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you how to stop the bleeding in the extraction of arteries and in the incision, and never make a cautery or hot iron below the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	from the eyes' sockets.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears from the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or near the arteries that are in the appearance of the head outside; and one sees that it is a cold, foolish, watery superfluity, then he makes the cautery that I said at the beginning of the humour descending to the eyes: one cautery in the head, and two cauteries on the two temples, and two cauteries or hot iron below the two bones; and if there is need for more, then he cauterizes carefully above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	from within the sockets of the eyes.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	If you treat him according to what we said in the division, and it does not help, then give the sick person to drink three ounces of old vinegar; after that, rinse his head, and make a cautery on the middle of the olive-sized cautery; and make two cauterizations of the cautery which is called "clavilis" above the eyebrows, one on each side; and beware not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the shape of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the membrane of the eye is softened by illness and moisture, then cauterize it with this cautery which is called "olivare".
de coi ci est li forme:	In what shape does it consist:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you make two fire cauterizations on the two hairs as long as the hairs are; and do not leave your hand off until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the manner that I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	two eye hairs that stick out (or possibly: "eyebrows" or simply two eyelashes)
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	At no time has it happened that the hairs of the eyes are turned into burners, and they pierce the eye, and one makes a cauterization according to two manners: that is to say by fire, or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	Or the fire cauterization commands the patient to let the hairs be as long and equal as they are; and if they pierce at their birth, then he binds them so that they do not move until they have born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are equal, then the patient puts them in their place; afterwards he signs on the paper of those a figure that is as much like the berry of the myrtle as it is; and this is the beginning of the sign near the hairs; then he puts damp cotton soaked in egg-glue and muskellunge fish scale on the eye, then heats the cauterization until it forms:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, cauterize on the figure that you have signed a little and a little many times, until the burn is burned away in that place; and the sign of health of the work is that you see the paper shrink back, and the hairs raised to the tip of the eye; then lift your hand, and let it be like that for three days, then put damp cotton in butter so that the scalding is removed; afterwards apply ointment until they are healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that the hairs come again and the paper is softened then start the cauterization again on those very same ones, just as you did first; and if the hairs are scattered, then cauterize until the paper rises to its natural height and is equal, and does not pierce the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The cauteries of burning medicine are that you command the patient to let the hairs grow as long and even as possible; then make a parchment in the shape of the leaf of myrtle; then take French soap and hot oil, each one-third, and grind them together well; and do this quickly, so it does not cool down, then sprinkle on top of the shape that you have made like the leaf of myrtle, and place on paper above the eyes; and if the disease is in only one eye, you should work with one, and also in both; and put cotton wool soaked in egg under the eye; and the patient's head be in your hands and place your two fingers showing on the medicine, and press one poultice and squeeze out all the times when the patient feels a prickling of the medicine, because he feels as if it is burning like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a long time, then take away the medicine from your fingers.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the mordication has passed, then lift up the place of aching, and reward if you see the membrane lifted in the same way as if it had been lifted by constriction of fire or by cutting; and if so, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, so put again of the medicine on the place or the medicine has no effect, as long as your works are equal and your eyes are set in point; then put on damp cotton wool in a burrow until the burned parts are cooled, after cure the place with the ointment that is called "dyafenis" and others, as long as it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to be careful in your work for great care that the medicine does not fall into eyes.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes damp afterwards and the hairs prick in the eye, then start again with the medicine on that place which is made damp with clean paper properly, just as you did before; after cure it as long as it is healed; and this is the shape of the leaf of the myrtle tree:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in greatness and smallness, and according to these you should adjust your constraints. And do not claim the right way for him whose study is this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	From the treatment of a fistula by cauterization.
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not help, then it is necessary that you cauterize it according to this manner.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Command the patient to put his head in your hand; and take the servant's head in your hands in such a way that it does not move or leave its place; after putting damp cotton on an egg yolk or persimmon juice over the eye; then heat the cauterizer which is like this: and shape the end so that it looks like a goose feather, together with the handle being the cauterizer itself; if you see that it is pointed from one head to another, and if you see, it is also like a tent; but nevertheless, what is shaped in this way will be worth your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After press the fistula if it is open, and take out the putrid matter, and dry it; and if it is closed, then work on it, and take out the bowels; after place on top of the cauterizer which is hot in shape, and hold your hand to the cauterizer at the part above the eye, so that your hand does not make a mistake; and put the cauterizer into the fat of the eye, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterization just to the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then repeat the cautery again once, and other if you need it, and let it be 3 days; afterward put on moistened cotton in a ball, and apply the treatment of drying ointment until it is healed, and if 40 days pass without being healed, put on corrosive bitter medicine until the bone is exposed; and the rite according to what it would come to his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing a fistula that none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand it as a fistula, and make an incision in its place; afterward put into the incision 1 subtle camomile that is in this shape:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and they make a quantity like that of a pea; and hold your hand or cloak firmly, and let the patient not move until the blistered spot runs its course to the eye; and it is necessary to put cotton soaked in eggs or vinegar on the patient's eye: the blister soars to the fistula, and the vein by marvelous sanitation.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is healed by the cauterization that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer poultice to the neck, and bring the fistula back into its proper place in the neck.
des crevaices en levres	cold sores on the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times happen blisters on lips that are called "pox", and just as well on the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these blisters with what we have said in divisions, and the treatment does not benefit, then heat a small cauterizing iron according to this shape:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it immediately into those blisters as hot as you can, until it comes to a head; after that dress the place with ointment until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of an abscess on the face (goule)
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess comes to the root of the face (goule), or to the eye, palate, or roots of the teeth, after it has done its purulence and become a boil and is inflamed and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we said in divisions, and it does not benefit: then it is necessary that you have a cauterizer according to the size of the fistula. After this, you should plug or poultice the fistula, and hold your hand so that the iron burns until the boil comes to a head and finishes its course; and do this once or twice, after which cure it as we said in cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it's good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the place and remove the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your chapter.
dou movement des dens	of a toothache (douvement des dens)
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines and it doesn't work, then put the patient's head in your healthy one; after heat a cauterizer so that when you apply it to the tooth, it will come out like a rod. Put hot cautery inside immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; after lift your hand and repeat the cauterization according to your pleasure. After fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and let them spit for an hour and rinse well.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is confirmed, and the softened gums are restrained, and the corrupted moisture dries up.
de la dolor des dens	of a toothache (dolor des dens)
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache pain comes from cold or if there is frostbite or water in the mouth, and medications do not work, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways: with a candle (cauterer de burre) and with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with a candle is done as follows: take some wax from a candle and shape it into the tip of an iron or metal spoon; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a thread, and moisten it in melted wax. Put this on the painful tooth immediately and hold until it cools down; and do this often until the virtues of the cauterization reach the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The iron or bronze cauterizer assembled with fire is such that you take a hot dog of metal and it's thick so the fire doesn't reach the mouth of the patient; after heating the cauterizer, in which shape will it be formed afterwards, place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cauterizer cools down; do this often, because the pain will be removed that same day or the next.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it's necessary that the patient fills his mouth with good butter in the pressing of this cauterizer, and then pulls away strongly; and this is the shape of the cauterizer.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauterizer for whatever part of the head you want, and according to your ability; and this is the shape of the cauterizer:
des scrophules	from swellings.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulas are from wet and cold moistures, and are not obedient to digestion by medicines, then heat the cauterizer shaped as it comes afterwards, and have two openings for the vapors to issue into the other part; and put the hot cauterizer on the abscess once, or twice if necessary, until it reaches the core of the abscess; and if the abscess is small put the cauterizer according to the size of the abscess, and leave it so for three days; and put on moistened cotton in butter until the swelling is removed; after that heal the place with ointments and bandages until it is healed.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the canina:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moistures prevail over the channels of the body and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then you must first purge the patient with soluble medicines; afterwards do a cautery at the root of the throat, and take care not to come up as far as the throat, and burn only with a small spark.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that you do another cautery at the joint of the neck at the tip of the spine, and the cautery is called "clavicule" by which we have shown the shape before; and heal the place as we have said before until it is healed.
de la toust	from the head of the breast (or chest)
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and every illness of the womb are caused by cold moistures, and the patient does not have a fever or a sweat, and it is an old illness, then make two fire cauteries on the navel in the skin; and another cautery between the two breasts; and let the cauteries be called "clavile" according to the form which has been said before.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, do a cautery to the entire point called "point" by which the shape is like that shown before in the disease of the ears; and the points should be up to thirty, or around there.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treatment, restore the joint according to what is said before; and have the cautery for three days according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And because of that they are the cauteries lighter, because you make them three at one strike.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the shoulder blade is dislocated due to moisture and it is put back in its place, but it cannot stay that way and it keeps coming out again with slight movements that happen, as we have proven, then you must reduce the initial dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After that, make a poultice on the patient's back and side; after lift up the skin which is inside the little bone at the shoulder joint with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated inward, then heat up the cautery that has two nails of douqueil (a type of iron or metal nail). This is the form:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the skin until it perforates all the way to the side, and the pus from the cautery will come together with four cauterizations; and because of that the cautery is made with the cautery that has three nails, because the figure of cauterization shows six cauterizations; and the nerves are according to the subtlety of a tent, and this is the form of the cautery that has three nails:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And at no time is it joined on top of that one nerve, because it has eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After that, put on the cautery a poultice of broth with cloth; after make the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated above, which of this thing happens often, then make a cautery on the thick part above the cautery nail, or many cauteries pricking there.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is refilled, and moisture is removed, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and much moisture come into the stomach and drain out until it returns to its natural condition, and many cathartics are multiplied for him, and in the accustomed ways of treatment he does not benefit at all, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back, and stretch out his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	From that time on, make three cauterizations one below the edge of the rib under the quantity of an egg, up to the full cautery nail, and two cauterizations behind the two sides as much so that the figure of the cauterizations be at three angles, and have such space between one and the other that they do not join together when they exude pus; and be the cauterizations so deep that they reach the two parts of the spleen, and be the figure of the cauterizations according to this form without juncture:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	If you see that one must cauterize with a great cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who has fear of this cautery, cauterize him in pricking and marking on the stomach i point according to the quantity that you see of ink; then cauterize him with the whole cautery which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the care of the care that we have had before them, as long as they are cured.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes pain of cold and moisture and great windiness, as long as it is strongly out of its natural complexion by superfluities; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and it does him no good, then you must have the patient sit on his haunches; and make a sign of three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, outside the hypochondrium, where the ribs of the man come; and there be space between each cautery the size of an egg; and the cauteries be as long as the length of the body, and do not press very hard with your hand on the whole cautery; and it burn only the middle part of the scab, and the patient must sit straight up on his feet; and if he cannot, then have him lie down, stretch out his legs, and lift up his arms; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is so, then cauterize these cauteries with the cutellary, if you are skilled and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all the flesh through; for you would dry out the whole body; and let it not come as far as boiling, for the flesh is very subtle at that place, and you know well enough.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When he has an abscess on the liver, and you wish to know if it is in the flesh of the liver or in the membrane: if it is in the flesh, the patient feels pain that is not too strong; and if it is in the membrane, he feels excessive pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure should be done on the eyes, it is necessary that the patient be seated over a basin; and then sign him to touch the place where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizing iron which resembles the sunbeam, of which this is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize with fire as long as the cautery is burned and becomes like sulfur so that the ulceration is completely gone; after the cure according to the treatment of scabies until it is healed; and it is not necessary for anyone other than he who has studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whose hands these diseases have been cured at some point.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can boldly undertake it, and it seems to me that it is more valuable to let him alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	of the cauterization for pleurisy (an inflammation of the lining surrounding the lungs)
