Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancients said that one should make cauterizations with the roots of Aristolochia for pleurisy, in this manner: Take a long root of Aristolochia, as large as you can find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your arm; and soak it in oil, and then take it to the fire, and cauterize one cautery between the ribcage and the neck, and two small cauterizations a little below descending in the part that is under the beard; and two cauterizations between the sixth rib and the lowest one, declining behind a little; and one cautery in the breast, and another on the stomach, and one between the shoulder blades, and two at the sides of the breast behind the cautery that is between the shoulder blades; and do not press your hand, but rather do it openly as in anointing.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they said some old man that someone uses the fire cautery similar to a razor, and heats it up and puts it between the ribs, so long as it comes to the abscess; and the pain is completely gone, just as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear that the patient dies now, or a fistula comes which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mumps (inflammation of the salivary glands)
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mumps in the manner that we have said in the sections on treatments, and it does not benefit, then there are three ways of cauterization that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of which one manner is such that you make III cauterizations, or IIII, in a row according to the length of the vein, according to the figure of the liver cauterization that we have said before; and do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient sit up straight over his back; and another manner of cauterization is such that you apply the cauterization which has II nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the key which is at the vein, or the wound of the patient comes towards the left, and let the elevations that you lift the key according to the key, according to the length of the body, and the cauterization be according to the width of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Then place the two nerves inflamed so that the key is pierced from the other side, and then take out the cauterization, and thus there will be four of them. And if you see, cauterize all the cauterization with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when it has grown by long time, and this is good that the other treatments before said.
de ydropisie	Diarrhea.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cautery does not help in dropsy, unless it is done in the manner called "asclytes".
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you cure it according to the manners that we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not help, then it is necessary that you do four cauterizations around the mouth, and one on the stomach, and one on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two behind the back on the spine, and one near the navel; and let the cauterizations be well close to the fatty part of the kidney.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterwards, let the cauterization remain open for a long time to allow corruption to be removed over time, and do not remove the patient's cure after the cauterization; and sanitation will hasten its way, and both inclinations (i.e. the treatment and the body) will come together with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The shape of the cauterizer for the belly should be a key (as we have shown before), and that for the back should be an olive leaf, as it is placed here before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the inflammation of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet are swollen in one who is dropsical and are full of clear yellow water, it is necessary that you cauterize on the back of the foot between the ring finger and the middle finger; and lift your hand with the cautery without turning.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too deep at once; thus the fire will soon turn yellowish-green, and the cauterize should be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After that make two cauterizations on each leg, one at the tip of the cutlery and another in the middle of the leg; and let the cauters be left long without scabbing until they dry out; after which cure the other cures that we have said.
de la menoison	Of the mensooning (or perhaps "dislocation")
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When the bloating of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, so much that the retentive and digestive virtues which are in the stomach and intestine are debilitated, and cannot be cured by ways of cures; and you see the sick person very suffering and of great virtue, then make one large cauterization on the stomach according to what has been spoken about here before or the cauterization of the stomach, to cauterize; and four small cauters around the mouth subtily each a thin cauter, and two cauters on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the sick person suffering, then make a cauterization on the elbow, and one small cauterization on each armpit, and two small cauters on the stomach next to the large one, because the cure is profitable when there is good aid.
de la cure des emorroydes	Of the treatment of hemorrhoids.
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the fundament, or one or more, and are old and of cold and moist corrupted humors, and are treated as we have said in divisions, but do not benefit, then make cauterizations: III on the spine of the back, that which is all apart from under the navel piece by piece in triangulating, and I cautery below the lip II tos; and if you think that the stomach has been chilled, and the meat does not cook, and one sees the face swell, then the face one great cautery on the stomach, as it was said before, and another on the liver, and another on the spleen with all the cautery tongs; and leave the cautery open for a long time.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment let the place heal until it is healed.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the scrotum which is called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you cut on the scrotum, if you heat a cautery which looks like a razor, and then put it all aflame on that scrotum cut; and leave your hand so long until the cautery comes to the fold of the groin, from where the skin covers; do this once or twice, and if there is much of the scrotum, cauterize each part as we have said; after cure with salves helpful as long as they are whole; and if you cauterize a great cautery on the testicles, it will have greater help.
de plaie mal curee	Of uncured wounds
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure cutting or opening, which we will tell about in its place, this illness comes that can not be healed except by cauterizing.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When to anyone comes a fistula, and it is swollen and spews forth putridity and corrupted moisture, then you must try to determine the depth of the whole opening and take care that you know how deep it is throughout.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which seems the hottest, and put it in the fistula according to the size that the opening is entered, and reheat the cautery as long as the corrupt and corrupted body parts are burned, once, or twice, or three times, according to the quantity of need; and be careful not to burn the nerves which are nearby, and the main veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes into the bladder and to the intestine, then beware of those places, and do not do this fire except in a place that is charred, and think it is not healed; after treatment let the place heal until it is healed, and if the place is sealed, and the matters are removed over a long time, then know that the place is completely healed; and if the matters are not removed, know that the place is torn, and corrupted with the bone to the core; and thus as one of these which we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet. Voici une tentative d'interprétation du texte :
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra .iij. cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When pain from cold comes to the joints, and from great swelling, and it does not take on a female complexion, then you must cause a cautery over the joints in one place and an iron cautery that we have spoken of before in another; and if we cauterize him with oil, he will have three cauteries in line, and they will become greater help.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et .i. a destre et .i. a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais .i. cautere defuers le dos, ou .ij. se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak from cold and moisture, so that the patient retains urine, then you make a cauterization on the part in front of the bladder, where the pubic hair begins, and one to the right and one to the left, and each cauterization be as long as the nail of a thumb; and you make one cauterization behind the back, or two if you need it; and the iron cauterizers be shaped according to the form spoken of before.
de la marris	of the kidneys
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the kidneys are cold and moist, and do not allow conception to occur for that reason, and the flowers are corrupted and their endings are delayed; and when they come, you feel great pain: then it is necessary to make three cauterizations around the waist, as we have said about the cautery of the bladder, and two cauterizations behind the back; and the iron cauterizers be shaped, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hip joint
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous humors descend to the hip joint, and because of this he is unable to stay in one place, and the sign is that his thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and the patient's usual position is disturbed, then you must cauterize him on the back of the hip joint at a single cautery resembling a circle, and mark ahead of the usual position around the back as it turns, so that the back is inside the circle; and let the cauteries be such as those with which we have cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if these cauterizers are not available to you, then make three large cauterizers of olive wood, and let the cauterizers be as deep as all the kernels; and continue treatment until he is cured.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip joint
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes to the joint of the thigh, and it's due to cold or moisture, and the patient has been treated according to what we have said in the division, and the treatment is not working, and the disease is old: then you must purify the patient with foul-smelling pills or other good-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After the fire cauterization; and the manner of the cauterization is in two ways: that is to say together burning medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is in many ways, one of which is: that you cauterize on the buttock skin three triangular cauters according to this shape, and I make good depth and great, and there should be between each cautery the size of a thumb, and the cauters olive-shaped; sometimes one has made a cautery in the middle on the chief of the buttock, for which it is IV according to this shape:
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cauterized area is too small in comparison to what we have said before about the dislocation of the thigh; but make it so that the circle contains all of the thigh, and all the fat of the knee is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And that is the manner in which one does it in sciatica, when the pain stays in the buttock and does not reach as far as the thigh or as far as the leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes as far as the thigh and leg, then you make two cauters there where the patient says that the pain is located, and one cautery on top of the ankle four fingers deep, to the left side a little; and the cauters should be knife-shaped, and be charred the thickness of a key; and if the patient feels that the pain extends as far as two or three inches below the foot or very near, then you cauterize there where he feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if necessary, you make even more; and if it seems that the pain is under the knee towards the thigh, then you make a cautery at the knife-shaped or circular cauter, and take good care in all your cauterizations that you do not burn so deeply that you damage the nerves and large arteries, and that you do not cause the patient more great harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had a fire cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they were left so that the leg would be completely swollen, and the feet as well, and was pierced and corrupted all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a purging from the belly by which he got his death.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pains are in two parts together, do a cautery in one and in the other, in this manner.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the wise ones said about the buttock cautery, of which this is the manner, make such an iron and it should be at its head as thick as a walnut shell, or a little less, and it should have handles and be from one handle to the other in length the quantity of a pea; and the handles should be two parts wide, and they should also be like pebbles, and there should be an iron well made; and this is the shape:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it should be scalded until it is completely red and smells of sulfur, then put on the backrest of the sick haunch and turned over to the healthy side; and cauterized once with a cautery stone and left for three days; then make a poultice with wax, and leave the wound open for a long time; after the ointment cure until it is healed.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use a poultice of this cauterization for the fear of its gaze, and if we see one who uses it; and nevertheless these are good cauters which can bear it, and where it affects.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The fiery cauterization of medicine is such that you make the instrument between the hands in which it descends the edge of the door, and is made of brass or iron with a long handle, and in its height has two loops, and between each loop is the quantity of the thickness of an index finger; and they are open at both ends, and join together as this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After put on the board of the arse to the patient lying on his side with his back towards you, and quickly lift your hand up over the board of the arse; after throw between the two circles of the hot iron which is heated in the fire at one pot, and let it be an hour from then, and bear the pain and burning of it to the patient.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it also finds cauterization similar to fire; and when the cauterizations are past, then lift your hand with the instrument and lift off the arse from the hot iron, and leave thus three days, and put on ointment so that what is black from the burning is scraped away; and let him be for three days until purging goes out of it; and this would be the last aid after the cure of ointments as long as he is healed.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain has spread up to the thigh or up to the leg, make an instrument that touches it in the same way as you have done with the hip; and this is the manner of hot application, and I have written it in the treatise on medical correction.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and live coal, as much of one as the other, and grind them together, and put them in a new pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Or if there is a small hole at the back so that the point of a razor can enter; and put on top of this pot another pot well weighted down, and put on top of the alkali and coal and sweet ash above, until you have two layers of powder above it which you will then have very firmly stuck to your hand; and leave it thus until the hot water and juice trickle down into the weighed-down pot, then take all this liquid and pour it over coal and alkali as before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And then it will be very swollen and will be managed in various works of medicine and cauteries of other members. For it makes a similar work as fire, and if one cauterizes well the area with honey, thus with mustard and anacardium and soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a treatment from which one man was cured of the pain in his groin and sciatic vein, and he greatly praised it, saying that no other treatment was done to him, and that he was healed once when this cure was made, and he had himself bathed just as he teaches here afterwards.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he says in the same manner that you take a handful of fresh and dry verdigris and grind it very well with one part of fat, and put it on the groin and on the thigh and on the leg where the pain is, and bind; and leave him for three hours, or as long as the patient does not feel the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then make him enter into a bath until his body be somewhat heated up, and make him enter into bed, and the pain will go away entirely and he will be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use a cautery for such medications unless it is after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when a vein is scarred with the fire of a goat's hair, it helps a lot; and the cautery should be done in this manner.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take linen and soak it in old oil, and place it on the cleft which is between the thumb of the foot and the other one that is called foscile.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take dry goat hair and burn them over the fire until they are charcoal, and place it on the linen, and let it stay as long as it takes to become cold; and do this again in the same way, and do not cease from doing it thus as long as you think by reason that it will come up just to the hip, and that the pain will be ceased; and this manner of cautery is called "cautere de chievre".
de la dolor dou dos	of the pain in the back (or) of the spine
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, either from falling or by percussion or from too great evacuation, or from signs of cold spread matter, none of these signs is worth cauterizing, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after these things that the sick person be freed from foul pills or other similar things, so that one makes on their back, at the place where the pain resides, three lines marked with ink, and in each line five cauters or more according to virtue and quantity that the sick person can bear; and make the cauterizing according to the cautery called "point"; and if you see, do three cauters or four on the middle nail-shaped cautery according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This illness often comes to small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have a narrow anal passage when they urinate, and pain; and you find it in the last vertebra of the back and on the appearance that comes over the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you think it can be cured, then cauterize it at the "point" cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery is applied to every part of the spine equally.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you wish, then cauterize around the spine with the red-hot cautery at two or three lines, and let the points be close to one another.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After the cure, leave it so that it is sound according to what we have said, and beware that you do not bring a cautery into a hollow place where there are nerves.
de la dolor des jointes	of pain from the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When the pain from joints is due to humors that are spread throughout each member of the body, and when the pain comes in the feet, which doctors call "podagre" properly, and when it comes from a cold cause and medicines cannot cure it, then it is cured by cauterizing in this manner: make a ball of cauteries around the joint of the foot, and let the cauteries be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you prick on the face of the foot, then let the face cauterize completely with the red-hot cautery which we call "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knee and other joints, and this often occurs, then let the cautery be applied over each knee three or four times on each part, with the whole olive-shaped cauterer; and if you need more, then do it, but hold your hand no longer than until the flesh of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend just to the knee and to the back, administer the cautery that we have said in its chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make points around the boil II lines; and if there remains no pain in the arms, make points above each joint and above the hair of the hand; and if the pains come just to the ribs or just to the shoulders, cauterize each part, and do good governance to the patient and give medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do good governance and purge phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	from a rupture of the scrotum (or testicles)
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the hernia comes in angles, and the intestines descend to the scrotum and it's new, so you should instruct the patient that when you see them cure, do not harm him on that day; and he should use things that empty the belly, so that the intestines descend from his belly. Then have him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to pull his intestines out as long as the hernia is repaired, and hold them at your sides, and make a sign below the hernia over the bone of the elbow, and in all one sign that is similar to half of a circle above the body. Then apply the cautery with which it is shaped:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	as long as he is white and emits fetid vapors.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the intestines to their place; and the ministers bind his hand so that they do not return behind; and take good care of the thighs of the patient, and put under him a cushion and a servant on the thighs, and another on the chest which binds his hands; then put the cautery on the sign of the finger over your whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it so long as you reach the bone, and if you do not touch it at first time, repeat it again another time until you feel the bone; and be careful subtly that the intestines do not burst when you make the cautery, that you do not burn him; and that by this the patient does not die, or suffer another evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not reach just to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery of children be subtle according to their measure, and for great people also great according to their measure; then cure the place of the cauterized fat as long as the scalding is removed; then cure other ointments until they are healed, and let the patient lie on his back 40 days so that the wound may be well closed; and it is necessary that his dressings be left for a long time, so that the boil do not burst when he will get up in bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after 40 days, when he wants to get up, give him a well-made bandage and wear it for another 40 days; and have good rest, so that he does not strain himself too much and take care of excessive drinking and eating, and high breathing; and when he has followed this teaching then is completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say afterwards the treatment of cutting in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the twisting of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come to other areas and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, then apply the fire cautery according to its quantity, and let it be burned the third part of its depth; after cure according to what we have said; and any of the ancients has said that one must cauterize with a cautery at III angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of the head and make a line across its width above the ulcer, and another below it, and hold your hand inside all over the cautery nail.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and more subtle.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any limb, from falling or striking, and that pain lasts for a long time, and the cure of medicine is not worth it, then it must be cauterized with the cautery which is called "points", and let the cautery be according to the length of the limb, its weakness, and its fragility, and its strength and its location of torsions and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is cleansed by the first cauterization, it is well; if not, recommence the other cauterization on him, because such a custom is that it must move to the member that lies nearby, for which reason you should do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	of surgery (or surgical procedures)
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The abscesses are helped at times by cauterization with great help, and similarly the diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see it being cauterized, be on the lookout if the disease is at its beginning, and if it has been cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not spread or remain, and you doubt that the corruption will contaminate all of him, then do five cauteries over the head: I inside the head now, and the other towards the forehead by the end of the eyebrows; and II on both horns, and I behind on the nape; and leave your hand there so long as the cautery comes up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the thick humors can issue forth; and cauterize over the nose according to what it is in front.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the surgery is spread throughout and it's evident that the patient will die, then it's necessary to cauterize with the cauterizations we've mentioned on the head, and 1 cauterization in the neck, and 2 cauterizations on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauterizations on the spine of the back, and 1 large one on the navel and another next to it, and 2 on each shoulder, and 2 on the sides of the breast, and 2 on the tendons of the hips, and 1 on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands. And be careful not to burn the nerves that are behind the calcaneus. At times make a cauterization on the bone of the wrist, and another on the bone of the stomach, and another on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I do in cauterization, the more it helps you, and increases your benefit; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cauterization as much as the healthy person feels, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After the cure rub the place with flour and honey several times and do other cures until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a swelling comes to any member and is treated by medicines and oils and poultices, and it is not healed, then make cauterization on the member according to its size and smallness; and let the cauterization be one part going into the fat of the skin; then treat with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And at any time one makes a cautery on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that moves the member, and thus if it is removed the swelling; and nonetheless no one intervenes who is not knowledgeable about the members and the exits of the moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	of ulcers
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "ulcer" is deep-rooted, and no medicine can do anything about it, then cauterize it with a blister one inch deep, according to the depth of the flesh, until the ulcer is removed and its color changes; then cure it with flour of poppy seeds and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and vinegar from gall and red wine, each in equal parts; and mix everything together, and bind it with a cloth, and air it at the fire until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the treatment of syphilis by blistering
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a carbuncle comes at the beginning, and you see it arrest its course, if you cauterize it with a cautery that seems like a circle, all around the border of the carbuncle.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And nonetheless the wise men said that one also makes a cautery in the middle of the carbuncle; and nonetheless this does not seem to me good, because I fear it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen sometimes; and more properly is that it should be cauterized around, with the cautery which is called "circule", as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of swelling that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When some has an illness called "adubelati", and it delays in dying or because of the superfluity that it makes, or for the age of the sick person when he is decrepit (that is to say too old) and he has pus of blood, or for the heat; and you see it hastening to die: then cauterize around him with many small cauteries that prick; afterwards leave him thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it piercing through the entire cauterization, then heat the cauterization until its form is changed:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the midst of that illness called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the core, and be such that the patient feels it elsewhere in just such a manner that the course of the putridity is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards care for him until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cure with fire by iron (or, possibly) the surgical cure by iron (i.e. surgery performed with a hot iron or cautery)
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another manner of illness is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing other than a consumption of the member, for it eats the members just as fire consumes dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can tolerate cautery together with fire, then heat the cauters small and large, as is fitting to the place where the disease is; after cauterizing all over so that you eradicate all corruption, and nothing remains of it, so that everything that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized places a poultice with oil as long as the scalds from fire are being removed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cream of ointments has generated flesh.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after three days that healthy flesh does not grow, it is good; and if not, then repeat the cauterization on what remains of the places corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this medicine is sometimes cured in place of cauterization with fire; but nonetheless cauterization with fire is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicament in its division: take what you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	The spurs which come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often times happens that at the feet by departure a disease appears which is called "clos" according to our intention, and it is a thickened thing that wounds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the fire cautery for this disease is in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This means fire cautery and water hot cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is that you heat a cautery handle as well as an iron pen of vinegar, and it should be made of good iron to its measure that it can pierce the tumor from all sides, and that there are subtle edges; afterwards put it hot on the tumor, and turn your hand entirely around the tumor until it reaches the temperature of the tumor; and leave it thus for three days so that it begins to emit pus; then make a poultice with bitter wild savin crushed with oil, and leave the poultice over the whole night, and the tumor will fall out and be uprooted from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the place with ointment by applying salve until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if it is converted into a boil on the body, and occurs often in hands and feet, then you should bring a cauterization of hot water; and do it thus: take a tin or iron tube, or a horn spoon, and place it on the boil and the surrounding area, that is to say, porcupine warts; and put the tube on so that it covers everything around, then put in a bit of hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand turning so that the edges of the tube reach to the root of the boil, and allow the hot water to penetrate deeply to the root; and let the patient endure the scalding of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will dislodge itself completely with all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Do this after another like this, until you have removed all of those that are in the body, then treat them with salves that remove flesh.
li cure dou trembler	It seems like you're sharing a medical treatment from an old text. Here's my attempt to translate and summarize:
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some person shivers from cold or from quartan fever or another, it is necessary that you make him four cauteries or five on the spine of the back, one cautery between each spine; and one on the navel, and one on the stomach at the olive cautery; he will let out the tremble, and hasten to health from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	boils that pus
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	At times appear on the outside of the body blisters or festering boils that come from thick corrupted matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	It is necessary at first when they appear that one makes a cautery on the top of each boil: a subtle cautery from hazel wood, whose tip is seized by fire, or from the root of Aristolochus longa, or with a lentil-shaped cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at times when one has cauterized them at first when they appear in this manner, and they cannot grow any further forward, but the superfluous things from which they come are ruptured and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Often there are great outflows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes from the outside, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the member, and suchlike things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet when this happens to someone, if you hasten to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and press hard until the blood is calmed under your finger, and no more comes out; then take olive cauteries, both small and large, as many as they are red, and then catch one, either great or small according to the wound and its place where the artery runs, and put the cautery on that vein where you hold your finger, and hold the cautery so long as the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bursts out again when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cautery cools down, then take hastily another one of the cauteries that are on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing these one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is nearby, and that no other evil comes upon the sick person. And know that when blood spurts from an artery, it cannot be well stopped directly if the artery is large, except by one of the four ways we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not tied off, or by strongly tying a thread, or by medicines applied which have power to stop bleeding; and it should be tied and strained properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who would remind of the danger of stopping bleeding with tightly tied strings or by applying hot things on top, or similar things, if they did not have some effect?
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to someone and they do not have a physician or medicine present, then they should put their index finger on the wound of the vein as we said, and press hard until it is stopped above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move their finger, but moisten it with cold water frequently so that it is very cold, until the bleeding is congealed and thickened and stopped. And make inquiries in front to get what they need of cauteries and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	The second book of surgical remedies begins here.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter all the diseases in which one must cautery with fire, or with a burning medicine, and the instruments and causes and the forms of cauterization; and I put that chapter at the head until now, and I will go into this chapter by the same way so that you may find more easily what you want.

And thus that I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of cauterization, and therefore it is necessary to be on greater guard.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter there are many times evacuation of blood at opening the vein, and at incising above an aposteme, and at dressing wounds, and at extracting splinters, and at incising on the bone, and similar things; or there is danger and fear, and death comes to many.

si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come of those who have so great faith in their disease that they will die easily because of the foolishness that they find in their illness, and from the great wickedness of their malady; and of these one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are who give you their reason, and say: "Wait, I am cured"; and the illness is spiteful.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It does not behoove you to consent to those who come to you with this manner, but put more great care in your honor than in your greed, and do not act foolishly but wisely of those of whom you are certain, and of whom you can take and have profit; and use prognosis and indication in the treatment of your patients for whose salvation may be converted; and those will help you to gain good reputation, and glory, and memory of praise.

And the treatment is such that if the swelling is between the cheekbone and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you make a cut in the head of an incision wide; and it should be as long as two fingerbreadths, so that the pus can run out. (This appears to be a detailed medical description, outlining a specific condition known as hydrocephalus or "water on the brain", where fluid accumulates in the cranial cavity, causing swelling and potentially life-threatening complications.)

And another manner of incision is that you look where the greatness of the abscess opens up and the gathering of the water; because it never faces forward, never faces backward, never faces to the right, and never faces to the left.

Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone a disease called "catarre" in the groin or in the thigh, and the disease is ancient, and the treatment of medicine does not help, then the last resort cure is cauterization with something that will close off the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief. Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see, place the spatula under the artery and cut above it, cutting also like two threads across. (This instruction is likely intended to help a surgeon carefully cauterize an area without damaging the underlying artery or other vital structures.)

And if the artery does not open to the feeling, so it is necessary that you measure the quantity of the space of III (the) twelfths, then sign up and do just to the bone; and what has to be put out of blood so is VI [parts], and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can endure, and the refilling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone point of the syphac, so cut that swollen things do not come in, then strain the wound and tie, and cure with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	It seems like another section title "de emigrainne". This may be a heading for a discussion on treating or managing migraines, which were considered a type of "head pain" or "pain in the head" during medieval times. The text may provide some description of symptoms and possible treatments for this condition.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient migraine comes, and old-fashioned headache appears, due to the moisture of tears and heat in the temples and an old-fashioned frenzy and similar things, and it has been medicated with various medical treatments and all those things do not help it, we would cut out the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have said before.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of their extraction is that the patient must hold back the hairs on their temples, and listen to the artery which beats in the temple, because it beats very well, and its pulse is not far from being visible in some people who are too cold; and if it is visible, then tie off the end of the artery with a cloth, and scrape the area with an asperous cloth, and clean up the area with hot water until the artery appears manifestly; then take a spatula which has this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then strip the skin lightly until you come to the artery, then draw it up with forceps and separate well the veins that are under each part; and if the artery is fine, so turn it to the point of the lancet, then cut off that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	If she is not cut, then the blood will not flow out completely.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out the blood from .vj. cups, down to .iij.; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it in .ij. places with a double thread of strong silk, so that there may not be any infection before the union of the wound, and there will gradually come out blood; then cut off the superfluity which is between the .ij. threads at the same time, and then, if you see fit, do the cautery of the fire cautery with a cauterizing knife down to the bone until the head of the artery is cut; and this is the main work, if the patient has no fever and he is of hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizing is a help to finish off the hemorrhaging: for this reason it is of greater aid to the patient.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary to fill the place with old cotton and put on good bandages; and when you untie them, take care of dry medicaments that make flesh grow, and bandages, until he be healed; and if blood flows from the artery so long as you work, hasten to cauterize by cautery, or fill the place with vitriol and strain on your hand so that the bleeding may cease; and if you do not have this at hand, put on the place your duty as much as the bleeding may congeal, and rise the place with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and be strained as much as it is necessary; and what is chief and more easy in the extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the back part of this cutting cautery with a trenching of .ij. parts, but the trenching must be well thick to withstand longer their heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instruments are too thin, they hold less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two knives a space of about one finger thick, and then when you've marked the incision of the two places, and you heat up the iron red-hot above so that it reaches the bone, and cauterize the back part in two parts; and they should be spaced far apart because the cauterization is not completely solid all the way through. And this is the shape of the cautery.
des larmes	From tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the afflicted flow down from their eyes to the forehead and do not benefit from medicine made for it, and you see the face of the sick person redden, and feel the forehead tremble like shivers; and so are the eyelids swollen and moist that the hairs on them are fallen, and are scalded and burned by the heat of the tears, then this remedy is needed.

de l’estoupement des oreilles	Il semble que nous avons terminé la lecture de cet extrait ancien qui parle du traitement des vers dans les oreilles. Si vous voulez continuer à traduire ou discuter de ce texte, je suis à votre disposition !
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	C'est vrai ! Le texte mentionne que les enfants naissent avec des orifices dans leurs oreilles (probablement une référence aux fosses du tympan), et cela peut également se produire chez les adultes en raison d'une congestion ou d'une inflammation de la peau ou de l'épithélium dans l'oreille. Et il décrit comment le pus peut s'accumuler dans ce petit espace, créant ainsi un trouble qui peut être difficile à diagnostiquer sans examen minutieux.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Donc, lorsque le trouble dans l'oreille ne peut pas être vu à l'œil nu, il s'agit probablement d'une infection plus grave qui nécessite une intervention médicale. Et si, en revanche, on voit l'apparition d'un pus ou d'une opilation (probablement une référence à un liquide épais et clair), alors il convient de mettre l'oreille du malade au soleil pour voir ce qui se passe.
