de la gresle	Of frost.
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come into papers of the eyes things that resemble frost in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "grandine", and it is an assembly of thick moisture on the paper above and below; the operation is such: first check if the grandine moves from one side to the other, which is a light thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape off each part lightly, then take it with tweezers, and remove.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot remove it without piercing the paper slightly, then do not harm the patient; and if the rupture is large, then sew it up with a suture, and cure it until it is sound; and if it is small, do nothing forcefully, because the ointments will repair it at once and join together flesh.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez. de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat or omentum (a fatty membrane in the abdominal cavity) of animals, likely used for medicinal purposes.
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is ingrained in the papers above, and this happens more often to children than to grown-ups, and it causes them great pain in their eyes, and they come down with catarrh in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because tears rush to their eyes; and so they go to bed on their faces immediately, and sleep on top, and have papers under their eyelids moistened by the inflowing discharge and appearance that covers the exinach which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your eyes with your thumbs and feel the exinach between them.

Then place it over the affected area; press with both hands from one side to the other so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle.

Then take a whole piece of cloth soaked in oil and wrap it between your shoulders at the back, and turn your hand to the right and left until it is spread out; and be careful not to add to the crack, that you do not reach all the way to the eye, that you injure it.

Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such people who burn themself in order to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then you treat them until they are healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to the eye as a hot swelling, then you should treat it with soothing plasters until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	the hairs of paper
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow on paper that are added to the natural ones and are inflamed, they cause harm and bring about ways of diseases such as accustomed tears and softening of the papers and albugine, so much so that it causes the destruction of themselves; and the cure is in four manners: or by cauterizing together fire, or by medicinal water according to what is written before or the chapter on cauterization, and it is done either by incision and stitching or by canes, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	It is necessary that you put the patient's head in your own hand, then turn the paper soaked in oil onto your left hand; if it has turned over, it's good; if not, put a needle on one thread of the paper and insert it into all the hairs that have grown there. And do this at the edge of the paper where the new hairs have grown next to the existing ones, and pull out one thread from the top of the entire paper, and turn it under the razor; then make an incision in the part below the paper, below the added hairs, all along the length of the tear, from the large tear to the small one. Then take out one thread and put a small patch of cotton and linen underneath the paper, then sign over the paper a shape like a myrtle sprig, and whatever shape you see the paper has taken, it is necessary that the figure be according to it.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it is necessary for someone to cut, make a great quantity of the paper according to what the paper is softened; then sew on all the padding above the two lines that you have signed, and start with a large seam up to small; and let one of the cuts be near the natural hairs in the thickness of a root, then put the cord into one of the two angles of the heart, then scrape off all of it; then assemble the two lips with a stitch from an awl on very fine wool thread, and dry the blood, and make the surplus of threads above the two knots on anything that sticks, as long as you see do this; and if not, don't take care, then leave the seam and the threads up to three days or four; then treat the wound without a seam from drying and constraining things, for the paper revives with the union of the wound and it, but the seam is dead (as said the ancients), and this work without fear; and if there is another manner: and it is that you sign the paper with a figure which is as much like the flower of myrtle, as we have told, on three cut-off cords according to the form which is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then take heed of those which ascend to the small veins equally according to the form which is thus:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you have no power to hold the forceps, and the thing is not entirely even, so take a needle with thread on it, and insert the point into the shape; and put one end of the thread next to the large nostril, and the other end next to the small one, and tie together with your hands the threads evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin above where you have marked, as we have said, then close the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, so calm it with ointment and similar soothing balm; and sometimes happen that the hair of the paper are converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure of the horns is thus: and it is that you turn the paper and make a slit in it according to what I have said, and then make 2 small canines by art, and 2 thin strings as long as the paper and the width of the spatula are; and take hold of the .ij. strings from each part where you hold the threads; then assemble one and the other subtly on top of what ascends from the paper of oil, and strain the two canines from both parts together; and leave it thus for some days, and the skin which has been strained will die and darken and peel, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it tarries, if the wound has some strength, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound is sewn up, and the paper has been lifted, and the hair cannot be felt anymore; and that is the form of the two sutures you will make according to this figure, and according to this length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	You take an exceedingly fine needle and insert one thread of silk, soft and fine; then tie the hairs and the needle together finely, making the length of the threads one palm long; then arrange on the skin one more thread of fine silk briefly, and tie the head of the thread to the knot; then put the patient's head in your hand; and place it by the sun so that the operation is illuminated, for this is a subtle and small operation. Then insert the needle into the entire length of the chase on the root of the hair attached, and make it pierce through quickly until you have drawn out the thread from above the natural hair; then draw out the thread up to the end of the skin on the paper with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the chase is treated and the hairs do not come out with it, you will pull out the thread from underneath all the thread that you have arranged, until the chase comes out through the hole above and you can see it by the sight of the eye; then you will pull out the thread and the chase, and close the eye and let the bandage stay closed for two or three days, so that the hair grows in its place and the skin heals; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the natural ones, and it should be raised with the one that you leave, until it is elongated and then raise it.
de la porriture de l’oil	Il semble que nous avons changé de sujet !
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this sickness called "aleacrati" or the whitening comes to the eye, it occurs in two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And occurs through a sudden wound, or incision, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the manner of treating it is that you cut apart the scab, and separate the lips of it, and put inside linen tents, and tie them until it heals; and it does not need you to use in its treatment things that dry up and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the sickness will come back worse than the first one; but I advise using soothing things, such as fenugreek; and the roots of water lily or althea, and flaxseed cooked, and anointing with unctuous liquid melted in any oil, and wrapping in a cloth, and treating it with that.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you take care not to let it close up again in the form it was before; and these works we have mentioned are no more than counter-remedies for this disease, so that it does not return in its former form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	the flesh (or tissue) that comes into the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is beneath what truly is called "axacrati", and it is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounds and cuts and cautery and similar things; and the method of doing this work is that you take a needle in which it has double thread, and pierce into the flesh, and make the needle perforate from left to right as far as straight, so that the threads come out on both sides of the flesh; then sew the skin above all the way around the needle, and tie with a string at the broadest part.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the paper returns according to what is needed, it's good; if not, then take a razor and place it in the cut, and turn the skin, and make two cuts on either side within the skin; and be the holes of the two cuts at the two angles of the incision that you sewed, and be made one angle so that when they are assembled, the shape is as much like the shape of a letter which has the name "I griesche"; then remove that skin, according to the size of its edges below, from what surrounds the paper; then join the two separated parts, and sew with a thread of linen; then perform the treatment of the medicaments that we said softening, and dressing, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or incision or cauterization, it is fitting that you make a plain incision under the papers, and follow what was said before. Then take a tente (a type of bandage) and separate the two layers of it, as I have said. And the operation should be done according to the shape of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and wise masters devise machines with all their might to make the figure return to its natural shape; and the sick person themselves, according to what seems fitting in terms of treatment and instruments, in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	the sudden movement of the paper
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this joining has been done in such a way that the paper on top is stuck with the white of the eye, and cannot move or perform its natural functions, then it is fitting to insert the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up. And bind it with bandages so that you sew what is damaged at the delicate thread, which should not be too rough nor too sharp, so that the sick person cannot suffer from the thread being too rough and hurting the eye; and your incision, from which you will remove this assembled part, should be made lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape. And all of this assembled part is healed, and there is no more liquid discharge in the eye, and it is elevated with a sweet liquid, and a colander; then place between the paper and the eye a linen bandage, and put on the eye a moist wool pad soaked in egg white; and after three days use a colander and things that clean out, until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the inflammation of the eye (from "l'ungle" which means "inflammation", "swelling")
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	It is known that the inflammation of the eye can occur in two ways: it can be nervous and resemble a hard dry scab, or another type that is not nervous but resembles frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and treated with pincers cannot be reduced; and both types of appearance begin near the large tear duct and grow little by little until they cover the entire eye, all the light and movement.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of making the incision is that the sick person puts their head in your lap, then you work with pincers to open up the eye. And take the paper and lift it up, then coagulate the inflammation with pincers of small double stitch, and hold it above. Then take a needle and insert one hair from a horse, cow or bull, and a strong thread, and fold back the point of the needle a little bit and insert it into the inflammation, and perforate all the way to the eye of the needle, and tie the inflammation with a thread and hold it above. And then remove all the hairs that are on the edge of the inflammation next to the eyelash, leaving just enough for the natural lash, so that through the incision the accustomed flow of tears does not come. And sometimes bind the inflammation only with string and thread, as we have said; then scrape away all the scabbed tissue from which is this form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the thread of the needle does not touch the tender tissue and break it, and that the eyelash is not perforated. And after the incision pour into the eye a little bit of burnt silk thread, and a collier made of litharge, and let it alone until the next day; then treat him with whatever is necessary until he is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the inflammation is not nervous and you cannot insert the needle, and the stitches cannot get in, this type of inflammation is often cured with medicines; and it grows as I have said in the division, and if you see it spreading, work on the eye of the sick person, and take a thread that is lightly sharpened to a point, according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And wipe the inflammation above with a subtle touch, and if you see that it does not decrease at all and the pus is pressing, distill from your mouth into the eye a collier made of litharge and red collier and burnt silk thread, and stop the eye until the next day; then start again the other treatment according to the same work, until it is completely removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no obstacle in the eye, such as a boil or an apostema (a type of abscess), then let it heal and first treat the hot apostema until it is healed; then start again with the same treatment, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the eyelash tissue is causing harm to the eye by great damage, then suspend it with a thread and remove a part of it, but not all, so that the flow of tears does not come; then distill into the eye red collier which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the tissue that grows on the eyelid (from "char" meaning "tissue", "growth", and "prunelle" meaning "eyelid")
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men's eyes once appear red cherry, and cover the pupil and hold steady above the papillae and turn to the outside, and seem like a balauster rose; and the work is that the patient puts his head into salted water, then works on the eyelids, and pulls out all that red flesh with suitable splinters, and sustains it at force; then cuts the first layer, and goes on cutting to the razor's edge until the end, and beware that you do not sully the eye in the work; and let the incision be somewhat like the spatulum we have said in the incision of the nail and the small forces by which one removes the sebaceous gland, as the form after this chapter shows it; and when the incision is completed and all the red flesh is removed, then apply the oil of silkworms or you distill crimson colliculus and similar corrosive medicines to the eye, and put on the eye outside cotton with egg yolk so that it may be sure of warm aposteme; and if there remains nothing and the blood rises above it, and you doubt warm aposteme, then leave the eye and cure the warm aposteme with soothing things for warm aposteme; then come back to your work until it is healed, and thus make what flesh has been put into the eye by this semblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But in any case, it is necessary that you alleviate the treatment of each weak eye, whether by natural means or accidental means with iron treatments; and do not insert your hand into any of these treatments until you see that this member has suffered from that treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the tears of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins are found which cover the eye, and they tolerate no work for sight, and weaken the eye forever.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary for the first that you look at the eye in which the red veins are; it must be free from other outer maladies except the red vein; then make the thread in this manner: instruct the patient to put their head into your hand, then suspend those threads all around with a fine thread doubled in this shape.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two threads by degrees in one knot according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	then one should apply force to those veins gently, and press the blood hour by hour after another, until you see remove those veins far from the eye; and be sure that you do not harm the eye with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at the hour of midday in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not miss what is happening in those veins; and when you have done this, then let green and red collyrium distill into the eye to corrupt what remains in the socket.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot squeeze out all of it in that hour, then make a poultice above the eye with soothing things for the pain of those eyes, and leave it on for some days until the pains are alleviated and be sure to apply heat so that an abscess does not form, then resume in this manner as before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye's fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	They call the hole a "arissati" fistula: when you cure it by cauterization and with hot medicine according to what I said before, and it is not healed, then there is trickery in that which you make incisions on top of the abscess, there where it should be dead, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you see the corruption and the blackness, then take it back with all the instruments with which this was done, that is the form; and it is called "aspre chief", and should be made of iron into one head sharp, and should be pointed like a lime as it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And put it back on the corroded part of the bone, then turn it between your fingers, and press your hand a little until you know that the corruption is removed; and do this several times, then restore the place with caustic medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the swelling is sewn up and flesh forms, and the body of the boil is sewn up and remains so for XL days, and it does not redevelop and is not inflamed, and no bad accident comes to it, then know that it is healed; if not, there is no other remedy except bringing the fistula back to the navel opening in this shape: and it is that you uncover from the bone a second time by iron, and by sharp medicines, and when it has been uncovered, take the forceps according to this shape, and the iron beak must be attenuated up to the head as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it against the bone next to the wound, and move your hand away from the eye of the needle, then turn the forceps until it pierces the bone and the patient feels it through the vein if they hold their hand on their neck; and then restore the joint with dry medicine, as I have instructed you, and when the flesh has grown back and hardened the place, then pour the liquid into the needle; this is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	La maladie des fistules de l'oeil...
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes appear to be open wide and there is no disturbance or diminishment, it is necessary that you instruct the patient; then clean them, then apply poultices with iron near the eye to bleed, then put on an eye compress made from a mixture of acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocolla; and then bind the eye up with bandages and cloths. The manner of the cloths is that you take soft cloths and double each one four times; then place one over the other as much as the eyes need; then strain by placing on top of it a hard bandage firmly, and repeat the poultices to bleed without causing pain; then remove the poultices and leave the eye bound tightly day and night, and if the compresses become moist, you must bind them tightly; then remove the compress after the day and the night, and if you see the eye improving, it is well; if not, then repeat the compresses and cloths and the poultice and the iron until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Translation:
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the veil of the eye gets disrupted, then it swells, and there comes forth a fluid like a grain of resin, and it is frightening to see; then if you cover it, the operation will be such that you prick an awl into the root of the lower part, up to the upper part, then prick another awl where there is one doubled thread from the eyelid; and make it perforate, and leave the first awl in its place; then close the top of the double thread and tie a part of the eye around it, and hold it tight, then extract the awl and put on an oilcloth soaked in egg whites; and leave it until the threads stick with the eye, then treat the eye with soothing things until the wound is healed; and whenever the wound is restrained by the stitches each part of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes are given a good appearance, then pierce it with a very fine awl that comes from the center of the eye, and cut out the moist albugo and lower the eyeball, and insert it right away; then pull it tight until it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	The bottom of the eye.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not far from being a boil which is assembled in the eye, resembling an arrow descending, and it's not water; and the manner of its appearance in the work is that you make the patient sit on a prepared seat and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and push so that you see the boil coming up to your eyes; then it will be stopped, and do not descend, and let the light be removed, and look at the patient's things as they usually are; and if it does not descend below, know that it is water, and if the descent of the boil is not prepared as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Sit the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and place it above the scarred tissue. Make a thread on the conjunctive with the scarred tissue and the crown, as long as the bowel issues; and when it has issued, distill in the eye hot water mixed with honey, or hot water of fenugreek that is boiled and mixed with honey, then be cured with another cure until they are healed.
des aigues de l’oil	A more specific part of the text!
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have the similar waters in the division, and what is needed to pierce; so work according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you sit the patient between your crossed hands, outside of the light from the sun, and the good eye should be strained very hard; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are left-handed, or in your right hand if they are right-handed; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are left-handed, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if they are right-handed; then place the point of the instrument near the crown by the thickness of a reed on that white part of the eye near the smaller tear, then push the instrument which is called "almagda" forcefully, and turn your hand so that it pierces into the white part of the eye, and feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be at the bottom of the measure of the space which is from the prune to the end of the blackness; and that is the crown of the eye; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the scarred tissue, then place the instrument just to the level where the water is, then express under a way after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the eyes bleed now, the patient sees before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if the eyes bleed again the second time, put pressure with the instrument, and when it is firmly in place and does not move, carefully extract the arrow turning your hand slowly and slowly; and then insert another thread of linen into the eye from within.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put on the outside a plug of linen or wet wool in rose oil and an abundance of egg white, and tie with the healthy eye.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and we who are of our time, put on a poultice with an abundance of egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter into the eye by its hardness, because there are such men who have very hard eyes, it is necessary that you take the instrument which is called "alberit", of whose form this is.
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And therefore pierce the conjunctiva only, and do not go too deeply, but make it subtle; then insert maybe [something], as we have said. And at the completion of the work, prepare for the patient the bed in a dark place, in which he sleeps on his back in a dark room; and he should be free from all movements, and take light food, and do not move his head nor to the right nor to the left, and let him stay tied according to his disposition just until the third day. Then release him in the same dark house, and test his sight, and make him look at some things, and then remove the bandage just until the seventh day; and it is not necessary that you do this now or after the incision, but rather that you delay it, because the eyes bleed quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When an abscess forms, instruct the patient to break open the pus in front of the seventh day, and address who soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, then break the eye vein and put on its face a bandage to cover any sore for one day, and be immediately in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then issue from the house and shout, and turn into his case; and know that no disciples should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Irach (a region in modern-day Iraq), who told us that in his peaceful land he made an incision with almagda, through which the eye's water escaped, but I have never seen anyone do this in our land, nor did I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps this is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the shapes of the forms of almagda, because whoever does not know them will see them, and they are made of pure gold.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the heads of these [almagda forms] are of this same subtlety, and their ends in three angled tips.
de la char sor le neis	of meat on the bone
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are times when various types of boil-like growths emerge, some of which resemble scorpions to the point of their feet; and if there are such that have swollen flesh with foul colour, and if there is swelling of bone with good colour.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	Therefore, for that boil which is swollen but not hardened, you should have the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; and close their nostrils, and burn an onion on those boils, and treat them with fire; then grasp what you can hold with a fine sharp spatula from one part, as long as you know that that boil has been completely opened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains any part that cannot be scraped off, then you should open the area with all one of the thin, sharp instruments lightly, until nothing remains. And if it is an abscess that bursts, cut out the scab as soon as possible; and if the abscess is malignant, hasten to cauterize it until the pain is alleviated and all the growths are removed, then pour oil or wine into the navel.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If the needle works and moisture comes up to the palate, know that it is clean; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is marrow in the bone above, to which the instruments do not come to cut: then you must insert a thread of linen somewhat thick, and well-knotted with fingers, with between each knot an interval of space as much or less; and put the patient's head on the needle at its greatest power, and draw through something odorant until it comes into the mouth from the nose; and many times do thus the children in school, and it is a light thing for him who wishes to do it; then take hold of the end that comes out through the nose with one hand, and the other end that comes out through the mouth with the other hand, and know one after the other in so far as they are on the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as much as you know that the new flesh has corrupted the skin, then pull out the pus, wipe away the blood, and moisten the thread with Egyptian balm, and put it back in its place just like before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corrode all the remaining skin; and then put on a poultice of some kind for several days until they are healed, and if they need dry medicines, use them; and that is the form of the instrument to purify the head, through which one distills oils and medicines.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it is of silver or of tin, resembling an open lantern, like a dog, and the conductor also; and if you see, make a closed lantern, and have the tools full to purge the head; and have one mandible at the chief to hold it while one heats the oil or some liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of meat on the bone
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there is a disease at the head of the bone which is called "telul", and it grows and becomes large so that it is visible as seen; and because of this it is necessary that you cut it out at the beginning, and have the surgeon remove all of it, then put on the place the cautery or burning medicine; and if one delays in cutting it out until it is large, beware lest it be hard, of foul color, of poor sense: do not touch it with iron because it is an enchanted tumor, for when you cut into it once, great evil comes to the patient; and if the tumor is of clean touch, not at all of foul color, and you see that you can remove all of it, then empty out the patient and the cut place senseless, and cure the place with dry and binding things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the bone is cut open and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solutions of corruption come into one of these working cartilages, it does little good, except in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to act as soon as possible when this happens in someone, if you observe that the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then attach the two lips together with a suture, then clean it until it is healed; and if the lips are already separated on one side or the other, it is necessary for you to scrape off all parts of their skin as long as they heal, then assemble the two lips together with a suture, and bind them tight, and sprinkle powdered dragon's blood, and burnt incense on top; and place on the powders a piece of plaster or another binding plaster, and let it set until it hardens by itself, then clean it with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of suturing is that you assemble the solution with:
des apostemes des levres	boils of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At times boils will erupt inside the lips as a hard abscess resembling grains of wheat, smaller and larger in size. Then you must turn the lips and split each one with a small cut, take hold of it with tweezers and scrape on both sides; then apply vinegar to the area after the incision until the pain is eased; and finally let the boil burst easily and cure the area with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the gum tissue
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a thickened mass of flesh appears above the gums, which they call "albulus"; if it is necessary that you grasp it with tweezers and cut at its root, and let the bleeding or pus come out; then put vinegar on the area to congeal, or other powders that dry and restrain; and if that mass of flesh returns after the incision, and many times appears, then cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not return after the cautery; these are the forms for cutting.
des sordens	of ulcers
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are found at the head of the teeth, inside the mouth between the gums, as rough and ugly scabs; and sometimes the tooth turns black and green and yellow, until the corruption reaches the gum, and it stinks; if it is necessary that you sit the ailing person in your hands, and his mouth should be in your sight, and remove the teeth or scabs that appear, until there is nothing left; and so do with the blackness, greenness, yellowness, and other discolorations, until they are gone; and if one removes what was at the first reason, it's good; if not, then start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything. And know that teeth need various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, because the scraper that is used to remove teeth from outside has other forms than those used to remove them between the teeth; and these forms and others should be with you prepared.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait until it's completely drained before removing it, because if not, there will be no excuse for failing to remove it; since it's a very hard substance that shouldn't be left behind.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the patient is bound by the cautery, it is necessary for you to be certain of the depth of the instrument.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	The patient often feels the pain to be from the tooth of Saint Anthony, and thinks it is being drained by the good tooth; and yet the pain does not depart because of this, until the bad tooth comes out, for we have already shown that to these saints; and when you are well certain of the depth of the instrument, it is necessary for you to burn around the tooth with a spatula very strong in order to protect the gums on all sides; then move it with your hands or with thin pincers at first pinch and pinch, until they are well loosened, then secure the pincers; and let the patient's eye be in your sight between your knees, and hold it steady so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extract the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not come out easily, then take one of these instruments and push it inside on each side lightly, and move it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	If the tooth is pierced and decayed, then you must fill it with cloth, at the place of the hole; and if it is strained gently with pliers, that it does not break when straining; and then carefully operate around the gum to unblock the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful that you do not break it, and leave a part of it, and tell the patient through the evilness of the root will cause greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not act in the same way as ignorant surgeons who because of their haste and boldness break the root sometimes, and do not provide what we have said would happen; but sometimes bring a great illness through the abscesses that remain, or through the root they break, as often happens to us; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the place with wine or with vinegar and with salt; and if there is a flow of blood which often happens, fill the place with vitriol powder; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the extractors, by which one first draws out teeth, are with long pointed tips and large handles, which do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And have large handles that do not bend when pulling, and be made of good iron well crafted, and have teeth to hold the mule.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains on the other side, you must put moistened cotton or a poultice on it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the place is softened, then I put in the forceps called "algefri", by which the head seems like a beak of a saw; and they should be made inside similarly to a file and that's their shape.

Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument is used if it cannot be broken, and you should know that many instruments of stone are; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise and subtle masters find their own instrument by themselves according to what their works and the disease show them, for there are such diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument on account of the diversity of causes and they should not break the bones or the other limbs unless it is necessary, if he searches for the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and uses gestures, of which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And they are large and well held to hold the bone so that it does not escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place of medicines suitable for this, and if there is putridity in the bone and it is small, then apply all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth appear not according to their natural body and the form is ugly, and especially in young maidens, it is necessary that you know if the tooth is newly grown after the tooth and is not in its right place and cannot be polished or filed: then scrape it; and if it is mixed with the tooth, take this instrument of which this is the shape, and resembles a small beak, and be made of iron sharp at the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the handle is short and short in your hand for the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it appears to be able to file it, take this file with a similar shape to which is the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like the file with which we make needles; and file the tooth short and short in your hand lightly, so that it does not move until it is sharp; then smooth it at the end to be perfectly flat, and if the teeth are too pointed and hurt the tongue, it is necessary to file the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not hurt the tongue nor corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	It seems like the text has ended abruptly. The phrase "quant li dent lochent" translates to "when the teeth are loose".
