Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth are loose due to falling or striking, and the patient cannot press on them without them dropping out, and you have treated them with binding medicines, but they do not hold; then they must be restrained with a thread of gold, because threads of silver become green and rot, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you want to guide the loose tooth, take the thread and put it doubled between the two healthy teeth, then insert the loose tooth between the healthy teeth, if there is one or more, until you have pulled them safely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then repeat the covering up as far as where you began, and hold your hand subtly and carefully, so that it does not move; and be sure to tie a ligature at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then take the wooden pegs of a thread and bend them in pincers, and assemble them, and point them between two healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not cut the tongue; and then leave it thus tight as long as it can stay, and if it loosens, or the threads break, then hold it with another string; if it stays and serves this way for a whole time period, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the direction of the two healthy teeth, and the two molars, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth falls out, it is put back in its place fresh by fresh, as we have said; and no one should intervene who is not wise and skilled, and at times a form of a cow's bone tooth is made, and it is placed in the location where the defect is, and it is held in place as we have said, and remains and serves thus for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	loose the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Whenever this thing comes from under the tongue or is a natural growth, that one is born thus; or by accident of a healed wound; and the works are such as you work on the mouth of the patient, and have their head in your healthy one, and lift up the tongue; then take the nervous thread from the back, so long as the tongue is released from its place, and if there is hardness or knot, and it's a sudden wound, then insert the lancet and take from behind that binding; and be sure that the wound is not too deep down for the artery which is underneath; and when you have done this, then lift up the head of cool rosewater and vinegar, or cold water, then put under the tongue a tent of linen; and let the patient spit each night, so that the clot cannot solidify.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood comes from the cut, put vinegar on the wound; and if the bleeding stops, treat it with the slow fire cautery, which is good for this; then cure him with another treatment until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see the ulcer to be colored or black or hard, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it at all, for it is a cancer; and if it is declining towards gangrene, and there is moisture, pour on the unguent, and make a thin paste from it, and deliver it from one part and another; and if the bleeding continues to your operation, put on vitriol poultice until it is stopped, then return to your operation until you have removed all pus; then lift up the hot iron and of ash, and cure with other treatments until they are healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	C'est un changement de sujet !
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes throats occur in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "hazelnuts"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it's a hard abscess of small sense and flesh color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also because of the bleeding; but let it be until it turns black, and then you will cut it, or it would break on its own; and if it is of white color again, and the root is subtle, prepare the instrument to scrape, but first look if the abscess has cooled down and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit before the sun, and his eyes should be in good sight, and the surgeon will open the mouth and take the patient's hand, and press the tongue down onto the instrument of this form; and it may be of silver or subtle bronze like a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against the whole instrument, and then see the abscess, if take the needle and stick it into the almond, and let the thread go above as far as you can; and don't leave anything of the threads with it, then cut it to the instrument, which is the shape, that seems like a hook; and although its head is curved, one end to the other, and are very sharp, and it's made of iron or lead.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	Je vois que les instructions sont progressives ! Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	Je vois que l'instruction est maintenant plus détaillée !
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was born inside the throat, that is to say, the small-sense abscess; and I had well closed all of the throat, so that the woman could not expire through the obstructed conduit, and could neither eat nor drink, and would have died if she stayed like that for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had been so swollen that it had burst out through both openings of the birth.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	Then I hastened at once, and inserted the instrument in one opening, then it burst out through it, and let out a large portion of pus; then I reinserted the other part into the other opening of the birth, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the instrument into the abscess, and cut off a part, and there came out from it only a little bit of blood; and so was unclogged the conduit of the throat of the woman, and she started now to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting away from that abscess for a long time; and the abscess kept growing again, and filled up the place that I had emptied, until it became very large; then I excised it and cauterized it inside the throat: thus it stopped growing; and I departed from those parts, and know only what God did with her after me.
de l’uve	Il semble que tu aies sauté une partie du texte pour ne mentionner que "de l'uve". Si tu veux continuer à discuter de ce qui précède, je serais heureux de poursuivre la discussion !
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the swelling descends to the eye and it is inflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it lies under a thick and round tumor, it is called "uve".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help, and you see that the boil abscess has been eased and it is subtle, then you must cut into it; and that which is round assembled and is not long; and it is bloody or of foul color or black, then you must refrain from cutting into it.

Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Then, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, concerning its shape and length, you must make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press the tongue with the instrument from which we have made a record beforehand; then push the needle into the eye, and draw out through, and cut at the two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cut too deeply that the superfluity which is beyond the natural term; for if you cut more than this, you wound at the voice and the parable; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear to be cut, you must use some trick for the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And it is that the patient puts his head in your vein, and then presses the tongue against the instrument which we have said in the chapter on cautery, and mixes with sharp water as, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and places the handle of this instrument, from which this shape comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And say the head has a hair or put on the medicine as the cheese of a spoon, and place the instrument all over the medicine on the eye; and the patient is lying on his side so that saliva and mucus flow from his mouth into the medicine inside, so that it does not go down to the throat and wound. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it on the eye for half an hour, as long as you see it darken and the irritation of the medicine is calmed; and if you wish, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument all over the cotton into the ear above, until the cotton dries on the eye. And do this often, as long as the cautery is perfect, then let it dry out, and go after four or five days. And if you need to start again the cauterization of the medicine, so start again, and after the cautery rinse around the eye with cotton soaked in butter, and clean up what is around the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and be cured with gargling until it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cauterization, if it is treated with fumigation in this manner: Take calendula, yarrow, origanum, rue, chamomile, and vervain, and assemble all or some of them in one pot, and I put ash there, and let it boil; and the pot should be well stuck with strong earth, and inside the pot have a wooden instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is to be of silver or lead, and one of the keys is placed in the mouth of the patient so long as the vapour ascends to the eye through the cord, so long as the eye is numbed; afterwards it often recovers, so long as the eye dries, and take care that you do not do this at the beginning of the hot abscess's appearing, for many things happen there; and do not do this unless at the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cord and put inside the head of the patient a strip of egg white, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the strip of egg white does not let the vapour harm the mouth, and it is good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has been done with the throat as dry as a fishbone or without anything; so it is necessary that you try what you see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see clearly the thing; and that which does not show itself and is closed in the throat, it is necessary that you make the patient vomit before the meat has been cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will be expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of pomegranate, or a root of lettuce, or .i. dry piece of bread; and tie to the sponge .i. thread, and then swallow it; and when it comes out, you will see it, and then you will know for sure; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take .i. instrument of cloth according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be curved at the top so that it can enter the throat more easily, and have the head raised upwards; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest the whole thing gets stuck, nor push the bone inside; and it is good that the patient puts the instrument in themselves, for this reason that they know whether the thing has been expelled; if they put it down, or it comes out at all with the instrument equally, as long as it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	This appears to be a title, "de la sansue de la gorge", which translates to "of the snot of the throat" in English.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	At any time is bloodletting the sanguine, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look into the throat of the patient at the sun, then that you press the tongue with the instrument which I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see pus, then scrape it off with a small spatula or fine tweezers that are good for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if these are not good, then take a horsehair cord and insert it into the throat of the patient; then stick the tip of the hot iron onto the end of the cord and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the illness befalls the patient every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take the full glass of cold water and open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and as soon as the pus feels the water, it will spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it does not spit as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asefetide, at the instrument that I have said in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will clear without spitting up.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the manner of the fumigation thus is that you take the pot in which there are glowing coals, and it being covered with a cloth pierced through in many places, and within this perforation the piece of the instrument; then throw your fumigation, and the patient puts the head of the reed in his mouth, and closes the mouth, so that the smoke does not come out but goes up to the nose; and now the sweat will fall, and if it does not fall, you repeat the fumigation many times; and make the patient suffer thirst, and eat bitter things and salts, and do not drink water; and then he must pass feces through this regimen.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	It seems that the text is describing a medieval medical instrument used to treat a condition. The description of the instrument is quite detailed and includes several features that were likely intended to make it effective for its purpose.
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many similar signs of abscess are, according to what the remembrance comes next from one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and shape; and there are two ways in which the one is like itself, and that which holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second manner is for the swellings which are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for abscesses of the head are other than those of the fundament, and abscesses of the jointed limb are other than those which occur in joints, and each one should have its own judgment in their work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses which should not be pierced, until the swelling is soft according to its completion; and those of such kind that it is necessary to pierce them when they are hard, and do not die according to their completion, as an abscess near a joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come near joints, and they are left until they are quite rotten around them, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of which it is a cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the principal limb, and if you delay the piercing until it is soft, it will harm the principal limb; or it is near the fundament, so when you pierce it while still soft; and it does not seem right to pierce a hardened abscess without digestion being completed, lest that which is near the fundament rot deep down and become a fistula, and be unable to heal in a long time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you know the work of piercing an abscess that has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain is alleviated, and the departure of fever, and the decrease in pain and redness, and the cessation of movement and tension at the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the puncture over or as close as possible to the place where the abscess has opened up, and where it protrudes; and that the puncture be long enough to reach the core of the abscess. And if the abscess is in the hands or feet, or near joints and nerves and arteries, then in all places equally, there is no need for a poultice.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in the fatty part, it is good to wait until you see that the perforation remains so that the digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it before that, the body of the pus will flow out from it, and it will be full of foul matter; and by chance the lips and the deep part of it may become hardened.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if to any abscess that is punctured according to the breadth of the body, according to what the member needs it.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary that you make small incisions in small abscesses, small openings; and in great abscesses, large openings, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if such an abscess requires cutting off the head, and covering; when it has become as dark as the dagger, and is softened, then you must do as one does for boils: and there are those that are split into three angles, and those that are cut like the leaf of myrtle, such as abscesses of the joints; and those where you make a round incision, and other cuts and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as a soft superficial abscess, it is necessary that you thoroughly pierce them; and it is necessary when the abscess is large and has accumulated great swelling, and you pierce them, do not pull out all the swelling in that hour, but pull out a part of it; then stop the abscess up to the next day, then pull out something from it again; do this by degrees over many times, until the swelling comes out completely; similarly if the patient is of weak virtue, or women bearing, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the spirits sometimes jump out with the issue of the swelling, which by chance the patient dies, and you are not aware.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your abscess, if the wound bursts open, and look to see if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it is a clean cut, then bind it up with tents made from linen or old cotton; and if it is a large abscess, and there are many ulcers, it is necessary that you stuff each one with a tent so that they come together in one place; and if you have found inside the abscess a part of the skin, and you have sewn it around, then it is necessary that you fill it up with old cotton or the rags of linen cloth without moisture, and tie it until the next day; then remove it, and cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs at your work, mix cold water with vinegar and moisten the cloth, and apply it to the place of bleeding many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, to be used on sound places; and if it is summer, and the place or abscess is very swollen, you must put on tents and moistened cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; and if it is winter, and the place is fleshy, you should put on damp cloths in water and oil, or in cold wine, until the third day, as we have said; and then loosen the abscess and drain and cure it, as is necessary, until they are healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: I have told you how one must proceed before treatments of abscesses, and here is the chapter.
des soros	swellings
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or the cure of a boil on the head comes from small abscesses, and they have the appearance that are in spider webs, as well as the down of a hen, and there are many similar appearances.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat and such places where there is moisture also like pus; and there are such places that are hard and stony to cut into, and there is no doubt if the instrument does not make it otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the works of cutting are such that you test with every instrument which is called "entromissoire", from which shape comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then make a hole in the long part on top.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is emptied, then scrape it clean without leaving any skin which contains that moisture, for it comes back again if you leave anything; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it's present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the dressing to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those will be cured who are staying at night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then start again with the lint, as before, on the second day, and the third, until you are well aware that it does not remain in the night; then treat the wound with ointment as is suitable, until it is clean.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains not swollen, cut it out according to this form, from long; and scrape off its crusts, and remove all scabs, and apply your whole cure of drawing forth pus from the cloth where it lies; and if the vein contradicts you, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do with the abscess if it is pus-filled, and of cutting and curing as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on top of the abscess that is filled with pus and moist, if it is easier, for they are full of blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if to some of these abscesses or on the head which do not have moisture, and among these abscesses that I showed you on the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had struck any of them, one would have made the wound as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	Other abscesses coming from the head or forehead, such as those that come to the heads of children and to the roots of ears, should always be opened up to their most dependent part, so that pus may exit; and they should be treated just as is necessary.
des scrophules	from swellings.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur in the neck and under the armpits and in the groin; and sometimes they come to other parts of the body; and are very swollen; and become intertwined with one another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly in its coat, just as the boil and the abscess of the head are, as we have said; and similar cases of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are abscesses that contain moisture, and there are malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In the one then that you see of good disposition towards treatment, and is similar in color to the flesh, and it swells from all sides but is not red at the neck or at the artery or at the conduit, and it is not deep; so it behooves you to cut it off above, and scorch each part, and sew the two lips of the skin with stitches, if you have need of them, just as we have said in abscesses of the head; and let the poultice be wet and wet, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, nor touch the tendinous sinew nor incise, lest your hand escape, and see too far ahead, that you do not cut what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	If you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, put vitriol broths or certain powders that prevent bleeding in the wound, and compress the wound; and leave it so until the abscess is relieved, and the wound becomes softened, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood is stopped, if it returns to your work, leave it until you have completed it; then inquire by your due sign whether any small scrophulae remain, if so cut and scrape them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has in the root of the scrophula a large vein, then you must not cut that scrophula at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang down without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton steeped in Egyptian oil, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut out the whole scrophula, then it is necessary that you sew together the two lips of the wound, and close them now; since there is no longer any superfluity because of the size of the scrophula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you understand how to cut out the root of it, and drain its pus, and close it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrophulas that hold superfluity, pierce it where the pus comes out; and pierce it in the same way as the one mentioned before, from within, then apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that they corrupt what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well cleansed, then apply an ointment cure with a layer of fat, until it is healed.
de squinance	Il semble que nous ayons atteint la fin de ce texte. Le style et le vocabulaire utilisés suggèrent qu'il s'agit d'un manuel médical médiéval, peut-être écrit en français ou dans une langue romane similaire. Les instructions pour traiter des plaies et des scrophules sont détaillées et semblent avoir été écrites par un praticien de la médecine du Moyen Âge. Si vous souhaitez poursuivre, je serais heureux de continuer à traduire ou à commenter ce texte !
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet. Il est maintenant question de la "tailleure de la gorge", qui pourrait faire référence à une procédure chirurgicale ou médicale ancienne.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	Those who have scabies must have the incision in the throat called "epiglote" removed; and this should not be done by someone else because all the veins and the pulse of the patient are hot in those with an abscess on the tongue, or in the throat, or in both jaws.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the pulse, it is necessary to cover the epiglote to avoid the peril that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Then it is necessary, when we want to cut the epiglottis, that we cut it below three circles or four with a small incision through them, between the two circles or because of the size of the incision by itself, not in the cartilage; and those places are suitable for the section of the epiglottis since there is no flesh, and the vessels are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is cowardly, then it is necessary that he stretches the skin of the throat to all the edges, then cuts it so far as it reaches the chin; and stop the blood vessels from bleeding, if you see anything, and then close the wound with a bandage, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the cutting of the vein at the chin which spurts forth through the place that is broken, and by the failure of speech; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which we doubt strangulation, assemble the two lips of the wound of the skin, and sew it all together except for the cartilage; then administer medications that cause flesh to grow, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	I dare say that we should not do this just so long as the throat is entirely stuffed up, and the patient is judged to be on death's door, and the pulse is faint.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis for what the patient cannot swallow, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is saved from death; and because of this command the ancients to leave the wound open as long as the evil of the illness has passed, and it passes in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young woman took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the canals of the womb; and I was summoned to cure her, and I found her just as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it, and I knew well that she had not tied down or guided the throat, and the vein was issuing forth through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed to her side, and stitched the wound, and cured her so that she was healed; and nothing happened to the young woman except that she turned red in the face, and returned to her normal condition; therefore I say that there should be no fear when cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of a big throat.
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "hernia of the throat", and it is a great abscess in a dark color, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or natural one has no instrument.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental one is in two ways, of which one is like fatty swellings, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is fear, and it should not be operated on with hot irons unless it is small, and prove and search thoroughly for all instruments: if you find it just like I described as fatty swelling, and cannot be pulled in any way, then cut it, just as one cuts fatty swellings, and take care of the whole area, if there is none, and search well everywhere, and cure it as it should be, until it is perfectly healed.
des nous	of the fatty tumors.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways for us that I will say all the likenesses; and now it is fitting that I tell all the difference which is between us and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that an abscess is hot and feverish, holding its temperature until the suppuration has passed, and the putrefaction has been completed; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the nodule there is neither heat nor fever nor pain, and it swells up, which is its own sac and is according to the colour of the body, and begins also like a boil, and becomes big; and they are in two likenesses, either fatty or moist, and many colours are such as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the fatty tumor, that you probe and investigate it first with all the instruments which are called "entromissories", according to its shape, either a capstan or what comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the manner of incising the abscesses of nodules is that you take the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and bend your double-pointed tool back and forth until you know that the instrument has pierced the core, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the thing inside, and be careful so it does not burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes through the skin, whatever color it may be, then do so as I said for other abscesses; and if after draining it there is no more moisture, know that it is fat, then do so in a cross shape, and take it with forceps, and scrape off lightly from each part and go to the core where it lies that you can pull it out whole with the needle; and if you cannot pull it out whole, then pull it apart piece by piece until nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there remains nothing, then the patient will come back many times; and if a small piece remains, and the blood irritates it, fill in the wound with corrosive powders sharp as knives, and bind the wound, and put on soothing things to the abscess warm, and cure it with other treatments until it is healed; and if the tumor is large, cut off the two lips of the wound, and cure it with those who harm the flesh.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the pain is contrary or otherwise bothers you, then hurry and apply the place with vinegar broth, and let it stay for two or three days, until the wound suppurates, and the ebullition of blood subsides; then come back to cut out what remains of the tumor.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Behold the forms of entromised instruments, and there are three kinds: great and medium and small; and among them there are three squares called "albaret", and one called "breb", and among them there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, to encircle abscesses of fistula; and they are also like needles with which we cauterize sponges, and they are made of citrine bronze, or iron, or silver, and the yellow ones are most valuable, and the black ones are more tested to encircle the edges of fistula; and there are three kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the holes.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The forms of lancets are of many shapes, such as you see here: great, medium, and small; and there are lancets with two handles in three manners also; and there are lancets with three handles, and they are in three manners also; and there are lancets with two handles, and single-handled lancets, and they are in three manners; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The chief of these which we do is cutting, and there are some that cut no more than from one side, whose skin we flay, so that we do not bleed the vein or nerve; and among the introducers are the alemeles responded in linen, so that the patient does not feel them when opening abscesses; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one should use no more than in a well-known place, such as legs, arms, breasts, armpits, and similar places; and sometimes we make another small instrument, resembling flayed pieces of cloth, in the shape of which we drain blood.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and one places it sometimes at the place that heals after incision of veins and arteries, and they are made in this great shape.
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	At times the breasts of some men swell when they begin to be corrupted, so that they seem like women's breasts; and they remain swollen and ugly, and whoever wants to cure them must do it according to this shape from point b to point g.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scrape off the fat, and fill the wound with medicated salve dripping from a siphon, then sew together the two lips of the wound at costura, and care for it until it is healed; and if the nipple leans downwards, and is swollen due to its size just like in women, make two small incisions above it, by two similar cuts; so that one contains the other at the end of both, so that the larger line holds the smaller according to this shape, from this line .b. until the line .g.; then scrape off the skin which is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and do what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to the bleeding of blood, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it mellows out the remaining fat, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	The abscesses of the armpits.
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come under the armpits are types of hard scrofula or abscesses with horns, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be scraped according to this shape, from line b to line g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the whole pouch in the abscess is emptied, then fill the wound with old cotton, and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat it with ointment suitable for this purpose, until it is completely healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is of a similar nature to scrofula, then make it in the same way as we have said for scrofula incisions, and if the wound forms a pouch again, then apply cauterization as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	The rupture of an artery.
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin on top is sewn together, there are often abscesses; and it also happens that the vein swells up and forms an abscess; and if you know how to tell when it's due to the artery, then the abscess is long inside deep; and when you feel it with your fingers, you feel it somewhat loosely; and when it's due to the vein, then it appears to be swollen on the outside; and it's foolishness to scrape this abscess, especially when it's under the armpits and shoulders and in many other places, and is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary to scrape the fire cautery, and also that which is on the head needs to be scraped, and in him who is swollen from the artery make a hole through the skin longwise; then work the incision at the stitches, and part the artery carefully from the threads, until it is uncovered; then put an awl beneath one end, and make it pierce up to the other side, and bind the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I have instructed you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then pierce the place between the two threads with a probe until the blood issues which is there, and loosen the abscess; then apply the dressing that one makes from boiled bow, as long as the thread falls away; then treat those wounds with suitable ointment, until they are healed; and if the abscess is due to an incision of the vein, it is necessary that you mark on your hand what you can take from the abscess all over the skin, then put the awl beneath the place that you hold in your hand, and make it pierce, and tie a double thread, so that you can pull it out from the other side; then bind the abscess, as I have told you, or the thread of one of two parts at the two corners of the thread; and if you doubt that the threads will not come out, then rebend another awl over all the thread through all the incision of the first awl, and bind the threads in four places; then scrape the abscess until the superfluities issue, then scrape the superfluity of the skin and leave what is bound; then put on a damp cloth soaked in wine and oil, and apply treatments of tents and ointments as long as it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	The abscesses of the nerves.
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Also like abscesses that come in the artery and vein, there are abscesses of nerves when they are injured or overworked, and similar causes.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	It happens most often in the joints and shoulders and everywhere where there are joints; and it is a grievous abscess, and its color seems like the color of flesh, and it occurs in various dispositions without pain; and when you restrain it firmly, the patient feels pain, but not deep within the body, but below the skin; and it can move freely from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor above nor below, and that which is in joints should not be opened with iron: perhaps there would be a contraction; and he who is in the head or on the forehead, make a poultice of sputum.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, you should seize it with forceps and cut out its root; and if it is large, suspend it to the navel, and peel off the skin, then scrape away and reassemble the wound to the suture, and cure him until he is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	The large hanging abscesses.
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At any time it occurs in the belly and not elsewhere the swelling, and it is a disease which is called "fungus" by its resemblance to mushrooms, and it has fine roots and thick stems; and there are small and very large ones; and I have seen one man who had two in his belly that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a thin root, and were already burst open, and were dripping with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them and found that one weighed 18 ounces and the other 6 pounds; and the work of the incision is such that you look to see if the patient is moist, and the color of the tumor is white and moist and has a fine root; if it cuts with a spatula so large, and be present in your cautery by fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the surgeon comes many times excessive bleeding of blood, and if the blood flows out, then hasten to cauterize; and if you see the patient trembling and fearful of the iron incision, then take a well-made flax thread and tie the artery as we have said, and let it be two days; and then restrain it, and cease not to strain the flax thread until it closes the artery, and cut through by sense work; and if the roots are large, then fear to touch even for the belly, but you can well touch half of it, then cauterize so that it does not recur; then treat the wound, and beware that you do not touch the cartilage which is of fresh color and poor sensation and milk-white appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	Because it's an enchanted abscess, and I'll come to the treatment of ulcers next.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the pouch is full.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterizing a wound or an abscess incision and is on the belly and in some of the intestines, as it happens with other ruptures, or blood flowing from veins or arteries according to what has been said before, or from inflammation; and if this is due to the rupture of the intestine and by the exit of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and is apparent with various exits.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is due to the discharge of the intestine, then it is more complex, and when you press it with your fingers, it springs back, and returns, and perhaps it is constricted, and greatly enlarges at the entrance of the bath and for strong labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it's because of moisture, it's a light thing, and you know well when you press it with your hand, it doesn't harden; and if it's because of blood, then it appears by these signs the abscess is large and hard, and is bound according to quantity; and if it's because of windiness, then it is soft to the touch, and the procedure is that you look to see whether the appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	It is necessary for you to leave the wound alone.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, because of the artery and vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is due to the intestine or bowel, it is necessary for you to command the patient to draw his intestines out and extend them straight, then mark with a sign all around the bowel; then command him to lie down soon between your hands, then go around the place that you have marked completely, then leave the upper half of the abscess in its entirety up to the great ligament; then tie it around with a strong thread or a cord made from strong silk firmly, and let the two ends be loose; then work on the upper half of the abscess extended over the thread, and put your index finger inside, and seek the intestine; if you find it caught in the thread, then release it, and push the intestine back into the belly; and if you find the bowel, then grasp it with the ligament, and cut away the superfluity; and if the artery or vein makes it contrary, then go carefully around them, then come back to your work and take two needles, and insert two strong threads, and insert the two needles through what you have made in a cross that you make pierce; then strain the abscess in four places over the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the place as long as it takes for it to heal, and cut out the dead flesh on its own; or you can cut it when it is softened and healed, then cure the abscess as is necessary, and let it go as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place as is necessary, and sew up the wound.
dou chancre	The chapter on ulcers.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the previous section about the signs of ulcers, and how to work with medicines, and how to avoid surgical treatment.
