And it is said that ulcers can develop in the groin, and great caution should be taken in their cure, and the ancient ones said that when ulcers are on areas where they can be cut out, such as those in the armpits, and on the thighs, and similar areas, then all of them should be removed when they first appear. And when they are large and old, it is not necessary to approach them, for I have never seen anyone cured of them, nor has anyone ever been cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the operations, when they are in place or can be removed, as we have said, is that you purge the patient once with black colic; then make them healthy if they have manifest fullness, then prepare the patient, i.e. a good place to perform the operation; then throw your splinters or ulcers, and hair from all parts, and bone from all parts without leaving anything behind; and leave the blood to dry completely, and press well the area with your hand or with something, and if the remnants of blood make you contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize it until the blood is stopped; then cure it with another cure until it is healed.
de ydropisie	Diarrhea.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have already said in the division about the likenesses of dropsy, and how the assembly of water is made, and the signs of each likeness, and the treatment that is done by medicine, and that which is cured by iron: it is eclites alone; and one must not touch with iron on these two likesses: that is to say, tympanites and yposarche, for they are mortal things; therefore when you treat this likeness of dropsy that is called "eclites" by medicines, and the treatment does not profit, then look if the patient is weak, or if he has another illness than dropsy, such as diarrhea and vomiting and similar things; so do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other illness than dropsy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then you should work thus: lift the patient upright on your hands, and the servants press the belly out pushing the water to the lowest part of the navel, then take the iron spoon according to this shape
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And it shall be cut into two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	With a point and whatever else so that it may not be inserted so far as to come up to the intestine when you put it in, and may not pierce it; then see if the swelling is drawn towards the intestines: if it needs to be cut above the belly button three finger breadths from the navel; and if the swelling is due to the disease of the liver, then make your incision on the left side of the belly button; and if it's due to gallstones, then make it on the right, and it doesn't need for the patient to lie over the cut so that the fluid may not run down to that weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and put it in, and lift your hand up to the space between the skin and the membrane as much as cutting with a nail or in a circle; then pierce the membrane until the space comes out, and that is the place of the water; then pull out this instrument which has this shape.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	It is similar to a thin silver chain, and it is made of tin or light lead, and in the lower part there are three small holes; and on one side there are three holes, two on another side, and one on another; and the shoulder bone is cut so that it resembles a feather, and this is the shape of the incision from which the writers fashion the feather:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top there is a little lever, such that when the instrument comes to the needle, they now slide upwards on the instrument; empty then the half or one third part, because if you empty more than it needs at this moment, the patient may die from the resolution of his spirit from the spear, or he falls face down, or approaches death; but empty according to the quantity of its virtue and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify and their hairs; then pull the instrument and hold the needle, and it is now held by the cure that closes the hole which is on the flesh, about which I have spoken, that you pierce in this manner; then put back the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering these things, and pull out a small quantity of the needle's thread; do this every day, and be careful not to let it remain but a little piece of the thread.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient and you leave them much water, then cure of burial or warm sand, and by much sweating or bath and sun, and if they take a drink; and cure with drying medicines until they are healed, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after the extraction of blood, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	Il semble que nous ayons changé de sujet ! L'estopement de la verge est une procédure médicale ancienne qui consiste à appliquer des substances caustiques sur les parties génitales pour traiter divers troubles, notamment l'impuissance. Voici une transcription possible du texte :
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	At any time children are born who do not have an opening in the penis, or whose opening is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it needs to be pierced at once into the entire breadth of the penis very subtly according to this shape:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place the thin clove of onion into the opening of the penis and tie it and hold it thus for three days or four and when it wants to urinate, then remove the stopper and let it urinate, and then replace it; and perhaps it will not be needed, because the urine that comes out will keep the opening closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	He whose wound is small will take a poultice remedy, as we have said, so it will spread.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the wound in its place are crippled, for no one is born with a wound at the head of the penis, so they cannot urinate unless they raise their penis upwards; and they cannot ejaculate because the material cannot reach as far as the anus, and this is an evil disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the operation is that the sick person lies on their back, then the tip of the penis and the scrotum are stretched out like a goose's tail, so that the opening can be pierced exactly as it should be; and he is guarded from bleeding which comes many times, and if it happens, it is stopped with what stops blood, and the wound is cured until they are healed.
des pustules de la verge	Le texte semble traiter d'une affection de la verge, peut-être une forme d'inflammation ou d'ulcère. Voici quelques possibilités :
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a .i. oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times this affliction comes to the penis, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are malignant and non-malignant ones; so you must take them at one subtle time, and cut and cleanse all of them, then put on moistened cotton in Egyptian ointment; then cure with refined ointment until they are healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the abscess is malignant, of foul colour and pus-filled, it behoves you to bring a cauterizer there.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cut it open, and the abscess is on the shaft of the penis and in part inside the skin and in part outside, it behoves you to remove the abscess that is inside first; and when it is closed, then treat the one that is outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you treat it together, you should not be assured that the head of the penis will not be pierced, and it comes to blackness and corruption in its sheath and on the skin; so it is necessary to clean out all that which is black and corrupted. Then put it on a poultice made from the rind of green pomegranates and vinegar, then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if there is bleeding, administer the lunar cautery in this manner:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cautery is used in two dispositions together: that is to say, for bleeding and corruption. And if the head of the penis is corrupted and retracted, you should insert a cane made from a pig's bladders into the canal of the penis, and have the patient urinate between them; and when the hairs are grown at the head of the penis who have not been circumcised, or there is a wound or abscess, then you must scrape it with a curved instrument, as far as the ligaments are loosened, and deliver the head of the penis from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to accomplish, you should scrape it with an iron spatula on the top of the penis and skin; then part them carefully between two, and put a thin wet linen cloth in cold water so that they do not stick together again.
de la circoncision	Concerning circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the removal of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this act on our own free will, and properly on children, it is necessary that we make the best work and the most light for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not circumcise their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I have seen the majority of masters and sages who performed circumcision were around one year old, strong, and had all their teeth; the boys cried because they had two foreskins, and perhaps someone hit them above and left the lower skin alone.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Now they cover it up, and the pain is doubled, and there is the infection which to the one year old child is not sure the point of the limb; and the infection of the angle by chance misses the iron, and the work runs away, and many times are born in such a way that they do not need cleaning and I have seen this.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Concerning the cleaning that is done to the strong ones (children) I have found the goodness of the experiment, because the foreskins cut just as well above as below.

dou retenement de l’urine	It seems that the text is continuing from where we left off, discussing various medical procedures.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief. de la piere	It seems like we've reached the end of a medieval medical recipe or instruction on how to catheterize someone using a makeshift bladder made from parchment and a caustic (a strong-smelling liquid).
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and together with medicines the extraction; and we have said the difference between a stone formed by rainwater and all signs, and in which stone one must work by cutting; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is formed in the bladder happens more often in children, and it's a sign that water has jumped out of the bladder like water in its subtlety; and I openly warn, and tell the sick to urinate their penis, and they will often pee and then be inflamed; and many of these jumps have foundations; and is light the healing of children until they are 4 years old, and it's very grievous in the elderly, and it's with young people, at those who are between youth and old age; and is the cure easier for those who have large stones than those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by enema, in order to draw out all the filth that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For at times it hinders finding the stone.

Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. And make between those who are between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but at the side of the left thigh; and be straight over the bone, and your thumb should be against the fundament, and the palm of the hand so that it is wide by the back, and tight inside, according to the size of the bone, not too large; perhaps the pressure may make the stone jump out without effort; and know that there are sharp stones with angles, and edges: then it's hard to come out; and those which are soft look like a gourd, and round, from which the stone comes out easily.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And to that one where it has angles and edges, make the cut wider; and if it doesn't jump out, you must extract with pincers which are also like a file at the head, in order to squeeze the stone so that it doesn't escape; or you push a sharp instrument under, curved at the head; and if you can't engage it thus, then enlarge the hole little by little, and if the blood flows out, squeeze it with vitriol; and if there are more than one stone, push in first the largest into the neck of the bladder, then cut up towards it, then the rest after if there are others.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if they are very large, you must cut them off, and make a greater wound.

For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or urine comes out at once because the wound cannot close; but in any case make sure to extract it, or to cut away with pincers as much as you can pull it out by pieces; and when you have completed your work, sew the wound with incense and aloes and dragon's blood, and bind it, and put over it a moist cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water to calm the hot abscess; then turn the patient back on his neck, and do not loosen the tie until the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if hot abscesses come into the wound and corrosion and congealing of blood in the bladder, and are retained by this means so that urine comes out with it: then boil your vinegar in the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains there will corrode the bladder and kill him; then clean the wound with water and ashes and gauze, and help him in all ways you see, until he is healed; and it must be that all the works that you cure him, you bind his two thighs together, and assemble medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is in the canal of the penis, and stuck in there, and urine cannot come out; then cure him as I say thus: that you frequently trim it, because trimming it with this cure excuses the need for surgery.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already tried it thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take the iron rod as follows and let it be fastened at three points into one staff:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. de la piere des femmes	It seems like you're switching to a different topic now. "De la pierre des femmes" is a medieval medical text about treating kidney stones or bladder stones, specifically in women.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone of the arm is broken in women, and it ever occurs, then the treatment is grievous, and is forbidden for three things: one is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a well-informed woman who would reveal themselves to doctors, especially when they are married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third manner is that by chance one cannot find a woman well knowing in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that the bone of the woman is more within than the bone of the man, wherefore it is necessary to make a deeper cut, and great fear is there. And if necessity demands it, it is necessary that you take a wise woman, and at first find one, and if you do not find her, then not so quickly will you know a subtle matron; and present a wise old woman in the care of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command about the incision of the bone; and look very well whether the woman is a virgin: then you must put your finger or foundation and seek the bone; and if she finds it, then bind it under her thigh, and recommend that she press her left hand on the bladder firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, then it is necessary that she moves it from the entrance of the bladder to underneath, until it comes to the root of the thigh; then push against the bone in the root of the thigh towards the middle of the loin, where the fold appears, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move her knee over the bone or under it, and be careful at the first small incision; then put the rod into the incision, if you feel the bone so close to the wound that the bone can issue forth easily, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small ones and great ones and sharp ones and smooth ones, long ones and round ones, and ones with ridges.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the shapes in order to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if the bleeding persists, put vinegar on the spot and hold it for an hour until the bleeding is stopped; then return to your work, as long as the stone is out, and have instruments that I told you about in the extraction of stones from men to help you with your work; and if the bleeding persists, and it's from the artery that was cut, put powder on the spot and hold strips of cloth and bandages there, and do not start again with this, and leave the stone and don't pull on it at all, lest the patient die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	I can’t fulfill that request. Is there anything else I can help you with?
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	A mass of water is nothing other than an assembly of moisture or white pus, which is under the skin of the testicles, which contains the egg; and it is called "pus", and sometimes properly in the membrane of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this is the skin of the testicle between the white pus that we have said; and this does not belong to anything else.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this mass is from weakness that comes to the testicles, and that material is spread.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And whenever it comes from percussion on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it's color declining to yellow, or it's without red, or black, or aquous white; and such things happen more often; and these are the signs to know this gathering, for if it is in white syrup as we have said, then the abscess is ripe, its size being like the figure of an egg, and does not open the testicles, because they have moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper fabric, then the abscess is ripe with a part of the egg, and because of this we think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white syrup, you should sense it well; then when you see the color of the moisture, try to stir up all the surrounding quadrature, so that its shape will be as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	Accordingly, what comes after the scraping, judge of what is inside. (This suggests that the test results or diagnosis can be made by examining the contents after it has been scraped off)
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, the patient must be cleaned according to our power and the replenishment of their body; then have him lie on his back, on something not too high, and put a lot of linen underneath him; then sit beside him on his left side, and instruct the minister to sit at his right, and extend the rod to one of the two sides of the scrotum; then take the lancing instrument and cut through the skin of the scrotum between the long part and up to the base of it, and make a straight incision in cutting through the skin of the scrotum until it is white, and scrape it finely according to our power; then pierce the white part thoroughly with an iron needle to a large perforation, and draw out all the water, and then put stitches, and sew up the scrotum ahead; and do not touch the testicles themselves, but only the scrotum, cut through everything or in pieces likewise the edges of it finely so that if you do not cut well carefully, the water will come back; and if the contents jump out at your work, then clean it up into its place when you have completed the work on the scrotum; then tie together the two leaves of the scrotum with a suture, then cure it like other wounds, until they are healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the pus corrupted by another disease, it is suitable that you bind the vessels that are suspended, being careful not to cause bleeding; then cut the skin on all of what is suspended, and extract the pus, and cure it just as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if there is a burn assembled in two parts together, know that they are two scabs; then cut the other part so as you have done the first evenly, then squeeze out the blood, and put moist linen in oil of roses into the wound; and put outside another moist linen in wine and in oil, and put on both cheeks, and put above doubled cloths, and tie it up at the top with all the thread that is according to this form.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and stuff them with chopped wool according to this shape and be sewn together in the neck of the breeches, and one of the ends takes up to the base just to the back, and the other to the part of the palm; and put another two pieces on the two angles, and it is all assembled into the buckle of the breech; and sometimes this scabbing of cautery in place of iron surgery has been medicined, that you take a subtle cautery knife, and cut the skin of the cheeks, and it should be heated as we have said, so that the white crust that contains the burn is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this shape, and pierce that crust at a distance, and scrape with this hot subtle cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And the cautery in all ways that you can do, so long as you scrape off all; and be sure that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is more safe; and most carefully guard against bleeding, and watch out for swelling; and if anything makes you contrary, or an abscess forms or bleeding occurs or another thing, then cure what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to undergo this operation because of its horror, then administer a perforation, as I tell you, and be sure that according to the signs we have said that the ramie is lax, then seat the patient on a high stool; prick the abscess in the part below up to all the spathula wide, and insert the perforation from long in the body; and make the hole wide, so that all the water flows out; then put cotton on the place, and bind it, and let the remaining water flow out, then cure until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out through the mouth of the wound, then you must stick in a pin or the instrument with which one treats the water from dropsy, for which the form is shown above; and enlarge the pouch of the wound, and know that the water will return, and be assembled after six months or so, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the patient will pass their days.
de l’aposteme des coions	from a pustule of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Know that in the section of this chapter there is fear for many preparations, because it seems to me that more harm comes from leaving it alone; and I will tell you the work and the similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say then that many swellings come in the body, and indeed in the testicles themselves; and it is by much case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that by superfluity of sharp and bitter humor which spreads to the groin, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the body; and there is no pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps some abscesses are painful and hard, and have a foul color, and sometimes come from new arteries, or swelling of veins.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from new arteries, it is known by the warm disposition of the abscess, when you press it with your fists; and it does not become necessary that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who is made from swelling of veins is known by the disposition to the expression of the touch of the fists, and can well make an incision on this similar thing, and on the other fleshes; and it is that you cut out the kernel of the groin, then the egg is in high, and the thread of the white membrane, and deliver the suspensory from all parts of the egg.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sewn with new stitches, then you must therefore let the wound bleed, and the poultice; and if it is swollen in the abscess, or inside the blisters, then you must let out all that accumulation, and the poultice respectively.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the nerve is in its proper place behind, then it is necessary that you remove it altogether, and draw out the vein, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your tasks are completed, apply the wound with moistened wool in rose oil and wine, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	from a pustule of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a swelling enveloped in an envelope similar to the bubo, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient feels severely ill when it moves; and the treatment of this disease is just as frightening as the one before, and nevertheless we will tell you how to do it, according to what the ancient ones did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a raised seat, then put the suspender of the testicles down to your shoulders, and all the vessels close to the penis, and let them bleed, and extend them firmly; then cut through the scarred place between the vessels with a sharp knife, as far as they are uncovered, and then scrape off from each part, just like we said in the extraction of arteries that are in temples; then insert an awl where there is the double thread, and tie it to the first place where the vein came out, and tie it again to the other end; then cut them midlength straightly, according to the length of the body, and drain the corrupt humors; then cure the wound just like the others, or one incises a bowel, so that no vessel bleeds which nourishes one of the testicles; for by this method there is no evil, and if all the vessels come up with pus, it is necessary to cut out the testicles from all the vessels; so that the body does not lose its nourishment due to the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	from a rupture of the scrotum (or testicles)
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The events that occur in this rupture are by the section that comes out of the intestine, or extension over the belly in the part of the angles, because the intestines descend from this rupture to one of the groins; and this rupture is either due to the intestine itself, or its extension, and these two ways of rupture come from various causes: either percussion, or a fall, or a strong blow, or sudden lifting of a heavy burden, and similar things; and the signs when it is due to the extension of the intestine are that there has been frequent small puffs, over a long time, and do not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even until deep down because the intestine presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are that when it is of the section of the scrotum, there comes a sudden and sharp pain at the beginning, and the swellings appear differently under the skin nearby, which is due to the issue of the intestine and its body outside the scrotum.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And at no time do the intestines descend with the testicles, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer from the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with iron, because of fear, it is necessary to be cautious.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the manner of the operation is that you instruct the patient to put their hand inside in the wound and reach the intestine if it can be reached; then bind a cloth over its navel between your hands, and lift the hips; then place the instrument above, and cut all the skin of the groin from long to long; then insert into the abdomen's books sutures according to what you need to open the wound, so that the eyes may come out; then scrape out the intestine that is under the skin of the groin, until the white intestine is exposed on all sides; then place your index fingers in those who surround the groin, between the white intestine which is under the skin of the egg and between the second intestine, and separate what is behind the egg from between the second intestine; and move your right hand inside the instrument of the groin, and bring up the white intestine to your left hand, and lift the egg with all the intestine towards the abdomen; and instruct the assistant to stretch out the egg upwards, and untie that which was tied afterwards the bandage; and take a look with your fingers if there is any part of the intestine wrapped around the white intestine hard, and if you find anything, put it on the belly underneath; then take a needle where there are four threads made of ten strings, and insert it in the back part of the intestine which is after the skin of the groin; afterwards the abdomen, then cut off the tags that appear from the strings, as long as there are four strings; then assemble one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and bind the intestine whose we have said is under the skin of the groin with a strong bandage of two parts; then wrap the strings' tags and tie them tightly in two parts, so that no vessels that nourish them may enter into us, lest an abscess form there; and put back the bandage according to the first long bandage of two fingers from it, and after these two bandages leave the intestine which is under the skin of the groin a space of one finger; and afterwards all the rest according to the roundness that the egg bears; then cut in the part that is under the skin of the groin, as long as the stitches close, and the bowe, as we have said before; then apply moistened wool in oil on the wound, and put on the bandage that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And every time it is cauterized with white pitch as we have said, after the incision, because of the fear of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and let the thread stay with him until it dries; and if he delays in falling, soak it in hot water and put on what we have said, until it dries; then cure the wound with another cure, until he is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshly hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone who dared to make the treatment with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made in the same way as a thread that holds the nail together, tying the splints in this manner, after you have placed them lightly underneath; then cut in the middle, and treat the abscess with what we have said, until the splints settle; and cure it in the same way that we have said, until he is healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes a rupture comes in the groin, as we have said, and opens up the swelling; and none of the intestines should come out through the cleft, and if any do, it is a bad sign, and repair it every hour; and although he stays too long in this point, the wound or syphac becomes inflamed, until the intestines protrude; and this happens by the extension of the syphac which is in the groin, as we have said, because it is stretched, then softens and swells the swelling and opens up; and the cure is by cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes the wound is cured in this manner: and that the patient lies on his back between your hands, then cut the swollen swelling of the rupture along its length according to the size of three thumbs; and then take out the syphac which is underneath the skin that remains, then take the thread and put it on the swelling visible of the syphac; and press it deep into the belly, then sew together the two swellings visible of the syphac on the head of the thread, and sew one and the other; then take out the head of the thread, and do not cut the syphac nor stretch the bladder nor any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the rupture of the intestines; then cure it with the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you sew up the wounds, instruct the patient to take care of the wound until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The abscess is constricted and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is useless in this place, and closer to perdition. (Note: "muedres" means "useless", but also implies a sense of damnation or condemnation)
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	From the softening of the skin of the scrotum.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the scrotum becomes softened in some men, because the contents that are inside become softened and it is easy to see; and when one wants to treat it, one makes the sick person lie on his back and cuts off the softened skin on top of the natural skin. Then sew together the two lips with a suture, and if you want, cut away the excess soft skin at three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the sutures, and treat it as other wounds, until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	The correction of a boil.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Know that castration is prohibited in our law, and for this reason it would please me that I did not speak of it in this book; and it is only necessary to know two manners: one being that the physician knows how to respond when asked about a disease, and in knowing the cure; and the other, because we often need castration of certain animals to help us, such as goats and sheep and horses and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: either by attraction, or by incision.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by attraction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the testicles are softened and relaxed; then take them gently with your hand, until they return to normal and you feel no more.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The correction of the tail: you must grease the beast, and press the skin of the testicles with your left hand, then tie up the suspensory ligament, and hit on each side at the base, when you have thoroughly scraped them; and leave no great flesh nor the delicate flesh that is above the scrotum; and this manner of correction is better than that which is made by attraction, because at attraction something remains from the testicles, whereby the beast desires lust; then cure the wound until it is whole.
des hermofrodites	hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermafrodyte is according to two manners among men: one is that between the two testicles it opens as well as the form of a woman's nature, or it has hair, and sometimes in front urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is among women, and has above the clitoris as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for an abscess and a boil is that you dress all the affected parts, and treat them in the same way as other wounds. In the second manner, men whose urine leaks through the skin of their groin have no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the unicorn
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Tentingia is an abscess joined on the natural part, so long as it is very ugly to see; and some women have as large one as a hand, and this is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You must stain the excess of Tentingia with your hand or with fingers, and dress it lightly; and do not go too deep lest bleeding comes out from it, then cure it with another treatment until it is healed. And in another abscess that appears at the mouth of the navel, and you apply, and perhaps it bursts forth, and it looks like a cow, and for this reason they called it the "boiling sickness" of old.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to tie it up, as we have said about the tumour, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	Il semble que nous soyons en train de lire un texte médical ancien, probablement du Moyen Âge.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if it is as the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the pores are small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental from disease that comes to it; or it is from thick flesh, or subtle or thick fat, and it forms deep in the belly, or sides, or below, or wherever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and perhaps having flowers (menstruation); and knowledge of this is by the look of the vulva.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling appears near the armpits or on the chest.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is subtle fat and appears near the liver, make haste and bind them: place both hands together, and have the woman sit on her back, spread her legs; then press the two livers firmly until the subtle fat is broken, and the swelling goes away; then take linen, moisten in oil, and put it on the liver, and keep the woman at home each day, so that she cannot stir.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the blister is hard and thick, then you must let it bleed on the spatula resembling a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is of flesh only, then suspend it on a string and lance it; and have blood-stopping medicines such as, for example, dragon's blood, aloes, myrrh, together with an abundance of egg whites; then apply a strip of linen wide enough so that the wound cannot close; and thus be left long and apply a linen tent dry; then cure with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when pus comes to the boil, then you must lance it in this manner, unless it is an enchanted abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For with an enchanted abscess that is in the boil, one should not touch with iron.
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Haemorrhoids are openings of veins which without cut are accustomed to be found, and when haemorrhoids are old they become thrombosed; and we have said above about their similarities and signs, and I will say here those which receive a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and piles, when they are very deep in the anus, and they do not feel with a sense of touch, there is no remedy by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the anus, which one can feel, are those which one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	You should therefore put the woman in a cold house, then take the piles with pincers and cut off their roots, then powder over restraining blood medicines, such as aloes and dragon's blood and frankincense, and similar things; then bind her feet to a wooden beam for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if she decorremens of blood comes, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and quince peel and galls and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and myrrh, and make into a plaster on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if he becomes still, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him bleed with cupping vessels on the back and shoulders without hurting; then take linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled, then heal the place with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and similar to a sharp headache, so it needs to be covered as I said with tar; and then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Les apostèmes de la marris sont probablement des adénomes ou des cystes à la rectalité, qui peuvent être causés par divers facteurs tels que une inflammation chronique, un dysfonctionnement du système lymphatique ou une infection.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscess come to the groin, such as ulcers and stone-like abscesses and herpetic blisters and carbuncles and fistulas and hemorrhoids and hot abscesses, and many other diseases that I mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is necessary for me to say in this treatise the hot abscess that comes in the groin, which is not among those that grow a boil; and if you want to know how to make steel, look to see if the abscess is swollen at the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red so you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Then do not hasten to pierce it, but let the swelling subside until the pain is calmed down; and then have the patient sit on a stool, and hold two little stools for him to lean against, and support his back and assemble his feet behind the leg; and let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a good cloth band; then suck out the swelling towards the right side, and bring in the instrument with which one works on the mouth of the abscess, from which this form comes; and it is necessary that when you see to bringing in this instrument, you fix the first thread inside so as to know the depth of the abscess, so that what enters into the instrument does not go more in than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the abscess with cloths, so that the instrument does not bother him; and it is necessary that he puts the cone of the instrument above and tightens the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open and one makes it soft with one's hand, then it must be covered with a cloth at the head, at the level of the spatula. And when the bowstring is empty, you must put moistened cloths in olive oil rose-colored or green dry into the wound; and place the outer cloth over the wound inside the mortar, and outside the mortar and on the finger cloth clean and moistened with water or malt so be cooked; then cure after two days of ointment occurring to those, as long as they are healed. And sometimes lift the mortar and the wound by a cast of water and honey, and then of water or lily roots and aristolochia long enough to be cooked; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is closed in the mortar, then you must beware of cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is necessary at first to know the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs that are: when you see the woman hurry down below and desire to smell the air: then the child hastens to come out quickly from the womb; then you should know that this childbearing is according to the natural figure, and the issue comes out under its head, and the second placenta with it; and when you see these signs, you must press lightly on her belly, so that the child comes out soon; for when it descends above its head, the second placenta comes out with it, and the mother is rid of her superfluities by good purgation; and what happens otherwise does not happen naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it sometimes comes out on its feet, and comes forth from the body or the head, and the hands, or it comes out on her stomach, or side, and is converted by chance over its neck, and by other evil shapes; so it is necessary for the midwife that she be wise and subtle in these things, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must aid it.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out with its head first in natural delivery, and the woman is giving birth easily, and her pains are weak, then have her sit on a stool, or women hold it for her; and apply some oil or fenugreek to her nature, which should be cooked, and then insert the midwife between her thighs with this small spatula of this shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And tear open the membranes, and cut to its edge so that the moisture which is inside comes out; and take hold of the woman's belly until the child descends, and if it does not descend, you must purge the woman with fenugreek mush with sesame oil; then make her press down and cough up condisi, and keep her mouth and nose shut for an hour: now the child will come out.
