Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the hands come out too far, you must reset them gently bit by bit; and if they cannot enter, place the woman on a stool, and lift her feet up high; then lower the stool to the ground, and keep hold of the woman so she does not stand up; and if the hands cannot enter and the child dies, cut the hands with the knife that is placed ahead of you, and take out the infant, and reset them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the infant comes to its feet, you should push it upwards; and then turn it back and forth little by little until it is even; then take hold of the feet and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps just up to its hips, you should command it to stop and make it stretch out its legs; if it is forced, it will have the will of God.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he doesn't go forward as we said, then turn him a little bit at a time until he is in accordance with the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it is easily fixed.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't come out as we have said, then take mandrake root, and oil of sassafras, and boiled gum, and pound all together in a mortar; and put on the woman's natural moisture inside and outside this ointment, then make her sit in hot water up to under the ribs; and when it is moistened underneath, then place the mirror girdle on her, and put it on, and let her stay for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her stretch out and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly touch her belly, because the infant now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child from between her legs.
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the infant comes in this form, if I put my hands gently on it; then bind its neck and let its feet hang down, and be placed on the bed so that they are bent; and fold its hands gently and then take them off its stomach, and remove the cushions underneath, until it is lowered down; and if the infant does not cry, take its feet and move them back, then move the stomach up, then I put my hands in; and see the small child folded and gentle; and command the woman to grasp it until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the issue of the child that comes forth, which is hanging down one arm.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring the hand back: if one cannot bring it back, make the woman stand up and go; if she cannot get up, lay her on the bed and straighten her legs; then administer the remedy that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, make her sit on the stool, then try to bring the hand back; and see the child according to its natural shape, and make it take a breath, and command her to grasp until the infant emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the issue of the child from around its neck, and it has stretched out its hands, and its face is turned towards its mother's back.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the patient hold his hand, then turn it slowly and slowly, and let it rest lightly; and when it is even, so place on it the natural mustard-like ointment of aloes and oil, as we have said, then instruct him to move it slowly and slowly; and when you will have done this, so make him sit on the seat, and instruct him to hold himself steady; and make him stretch.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in this same manner for the entire second birth.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way to the second stage, then cut the membrane with your nail, until the moisture is drained; and if the umbilical cord goes up on its face and onto its neck, so cut the umbilical cord close to the mouth, that it not be retained, and let the child die; then push the child inside, as much as you have put it, as it should be, and instruct the woman to take hold of herself once: then it will come out lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins.
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes three or four are born at once; and this is not a strange thing, and it happens often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Dui are strange things, and do not live, if they have no name; I know these, which multiply, and are severed by the spleen that divides them, which is connected to the belly; and sometimes issue just naturally like us all sons, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they issue grievously, then the cure is as we have said, and the belly is subtle, and makes what it does quickly and lightly; and make thus as it tends towards health.
de plusors enfans	of many children.
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the womb I or II or III or IV or V or VI or VII, or more than fifteen, and are all formed in shape of a child by the measurement of the wise creator, and it is necessary that the belly knows everything, for perchance similar things happen to him; so do according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman after the child is dead or in the womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to intervene by hand; so it is necessary that you know if the woman has a good constitution, and whether she has had an accident or fears death; so it is necessary that the woman be placed on her back, and her head inclined downwards, and her legs lifted; and the patient should have a poultice of 2 parts, or she should be tied to the bed if she is not treated for the descent of the child; then rub the mouth of the mother with moist oil mixed with musk, aloes, fenugreek, and flaxseed, then anoint the hands of the birth attendant with these oils and mixtures; then insert the fingers lightly into the poultice, then wait if the child is descending onto its head; if so, place the fingers in her eyes or neck or mouth or throat or under the chin or on the chest or near the sides, and if the descent is on the feet, place the fingers or pin them and tie them back to the body's midsection; and it is necessary that you place the poultice in your right hand, and put the pad between the palms of your left hand, and insert the fingers lightly into one of those places that we have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the poultice:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find the other incision, or the third one if you need it, so that the extraction is equal; and then stretch it equally in moving from one side to the other, so that the incisions are spaced so as to hold them, just like this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if there remains a part, then anoint the ball with some of his own oil, and insert them in that part, and pull the other part; and if it does not remain at all, then place this incision or higher up, and do so until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and he cannot bring it back for the straining, then you must wrap a cloth on top so that everything comes out; then bind at the jointure of the sole or at the ankle, and thus you should do the same in the other hand, and both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's shoulder is large and it is stiff in the outlet, or it has a sharp point assembled, then you must push the spatulum spinous between your fingers, and make the point and draw out the tip; or you remove it with the instrument which is called "almidach", by means of whose form comes with instruments or chapter that follows this one; and thus do the same if the child has a natural large shoulder; and then pull out the bones on the pincers, and if the bone jumps out and holds in forceps, so it is split, until the moistors which is in the pit outlet; and if it cannot come out, you must cut through pieces with the force that you can; and if it is inflamed in the belly or under the ribs, then you must make a hole until the moistors comes.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the child is above its feet, so it is easy to pull out and the tendons lead to the mouth of the womb are easy.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stiff in the belly or pit, then you must draw it out with the cloth enveloped on your hand; and make the belly or pit, until the moistors which is inside comes out; and if the other members are cut away, and the shoulder remains, then push the ball of your fist into its depth, and pull out the tip; and when you put one or two in, and pull it out, and the mouth of the marris is narrowed due to hot abscess which has come there, then you do not need to work on it, but rather apply moist and greasy things; and anoint with ointments, and make a poultice of softening and moistening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the infant is on its side and you can put it equal, so arrange it as we have said in a living child; and if one cannot, so carry it by pieces, and do not leave anything of the afterbirth.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if the swelling comes from an abscess that comes in the armpit; and if there is discharge of blood comes, it should be put in cold water constricting, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose womb contained a dead child, then she became pregnant with another on top of it, and rejected the death of the other.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After long time it came to him some abscesses in the mouth, and swelled so that it opened, and began to great pusulence.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to heal him, and I thought for long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on him plaster of strong attraction, and came out a bone, and after some days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was greatly amazed, because his belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	So I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I washed the wound, and with great care took out pieces of bone, until the woman was in a much better state; and the woman lived for a long time in this way, and she had always a lump of flesh from the place; and I have never recorded this chapter except that, when the master finds an unusual thing, he knows how to treat it.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to return the marrow to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	This afterwards comes the form of the purse, to which we give the books; and at two turnings on the two sides of the two strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the combs are more subtle than the forceps, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the wood should be 2 fingers wide, and the margin of the trees it should be, and a half-palm long; and between the two hammers there should be two joints of the same wood, which are strengthened in one and the other, half a palm long or somewhat more; and these two joints are put in the mouth of the abscess to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, to its resemblance more subtle and more light, is made of ebony wood or beech, according to the likeness of pincers; and has two handles two inches long, and two of width; and when you see open the uterus with all the instrument, then have the woman sit on the bed, her feet spread and her legs wide open, put the two handles together in the uterus, and hold the head of the instrument under between her thighs; then work your hand over all the instrument, as you did with pincers equally, according to the quantity that you see open the mouth of the uterus, until the patient makes what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all mounted and their likenesses multiplied; and when the craftsmen have prepared them, so much more speedy is the work, and higher the houses for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not despise the instrument, then do not fail to prepare it, for it is not excusable in its necessity.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the secondine is retained at childbirth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to retain her breath, and then have her sneeze with condensation, and hold your hands to her mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, take this herb, and make a pit or cover on it, and I put herbs that can open the mouth of the gallbladder, as chamomile, rue, anise, camomile, cassilaugine, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or poured over water above the fire; then put a string or pit on the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the gallbladder, and tie it so that the vapors come inside the gallbladder; then make it sweat, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the secondine spits up quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not completely healed, command the patient to moisten her left hand with sesame oil or with muscilage of aloes, and then insert it into the gallbladder, and withdraw the second probe; and when she has found it, take hold of it and stretch it straight out little by little, so that the gallbladder does not burst during extraction; but it must be moved slightly to the right and left, and then pull.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the mare is tightly constricted, we have said the cure for hiccups, and fumigation with herbs; and if she does not get better from all that we have said, then be careful not to follow further; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the mare, you tie to the navel of the woman, then fumigate with tefrarmaceutical ointment; if she will relieve her and set her back on track, and come to good health. But nonetheless, when she hiccups again, a foul odor comes up into the stomach and head, and harms the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So it is necessary to do fumigations suitable for her: none of the old men have proved that fumigation with watercress and dried figs does not work.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one fumigates the woman to retain the flowers and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is similar to a canker, and put the head of it finely into its nature, and the hairs broad on the fire; and be the fumigation above the coals, and the scab so that it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the fundament
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet had their fundament pierced, but it has been stopped up by a subtle silk thread: so then the nurse should make it pierce this silk thread at its proper time, and not with a sharp spatula, and guard the bandage so that it does not touch; then put on moist linen in vinegar and oil, then apply ointment as long as they are healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will stop up, so put or pierce a bandage of linen, and let it be left on for a long time, and have it taken out when the child wants to go into chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And as soon as this stoppage comes suddenly of an ulcer or apostema; it behoves to cover that suddenness: if it is cured, as we have said of the linen bandage.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula in the fundament (i.e. anal fistula)
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the fundament are nodulation, and those that come above the fundament or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, it works, and brings more moisture, a pale or subtle pus, and sometimes these fistulas persist; and they are known by these signs: either purging or vomiting or flatulence when the patient makes an evacuation, and perhaps coughing up a worm.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if one has fistulas that pierce just to the bladder, and just to the middle of the penis, and reach as far as the junction of the thigh, and as far as the knee.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula to be patent at the fundament, and not patent: and it is that you prick your finger on the fundament, and insert a fine needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then I insert a thin probe of linen or a horsehair, as long as you feel the probe or hair on your finger; and if you don't feel it, and there doesn't come a discharge of pus or wind or blood, as we have said: know that it does not penetrate; therefore do not hasten to treat.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is bursting through to the bladder or to the passage of urine, it will shoot out the urine, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just up to the joint of the thigh, then the probe comes out at its place; if there is no twisting and the invention of pain around it, then it means that it goes down quickly, and there's no cure by medicine or binding with ointment; and in these patent fistulas there is no strong cure except surgery, and the foolishness of foolish physicians who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not pierced by steel and is not old, there is hope for healing with iron, as I have tried it, and the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his hips, and has his hips inclined towards his belly; then apply a splint of lead or of wood if there is tortuosity, so long as you know when the splint comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the fundament, then you must insert your index finger into it, if it is pierced by the splint at that point; and be discovered where you feel between your thumb and skin or flesh, then know that it is pierced; if there is no trouble with it, then one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is always said that one can well heal some people, but rarely so; and the help that one does there, if it is to cauterize the cautery finely according to the width of the fistula, as is said before; and put it all hot into the fistula, until it comes near the fundament; and do this two or three times, as long as you know that those charred bits are burned, which are similar to a bird's feather; and then cure with damp cloths in burrow, until those charred bits come out; then cure with ointment containing sharp stuff and consolidating.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it so, namely cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent [or abscess] bursts in and does not puncture to the bottom which is at the foundation, and between your fist and the tent there is a thick layer of flesh or skin, and you see the fistula towards the covering from the heat; then cut off from the beginning of the fistula, and push ahead the tent, and apply the cautery afterwards, as long as it reaches to the top of the tent; and the tent will be delivered, and dry out; then cleanse those foul skins that look like a bird's feather, and let nothing remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the skin is too tight and cuts between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or a medicinal poultice to make it more pliable.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the cautery of fire combines two good things: namely, the scorching of foul skin and the drying out of blood and moisture; then treat moist boils in barley or cheese batter, as long as the place discharges pus, and sends forth the charred skin into the pus; then treat the wound with ointments that soften hardened flesh, and are dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, then it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes all the way to the fundament and is far from the body, then insert your finger into it and investigate this thing.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tumor, and between two is the web or the scab or skin, where it is close to piercing, so there is no doubt except faith and hope, by the administration of one of the three ways: or you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it down to the bottom, or if you can put tents and cure it as first; and do not go too deep in advance, that you do not cut the tenement which holds the foundation, and come the excrescences by the sense unwillingly; then cure it, as we have said; by chance it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean up, since it is cut close to the foundation, or by tent or other appointed instrument; then cleanse that fleshy part which is in the wound, as long as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to leave the fistula in the part behind the foundation: if it were a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And at any time there are fistulas in this manner: and it is when you pokes the tent inside the fistula, and it is on one side close to the foundation near the skin above, so take a perforated needle with a point at the tip according to this shape:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I put 1 twisted thread into 2, and insert the probe as far as the thread is in the fistula all along.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread of that perforation, so that you poke your thumb or foundation; and twist the head of the thread, and join the two holes together, and hold one to the other, and leave it for a day or two; and hold it again, as long as the threads are stuck between them and dripping; then treat the wound until it is sewn up and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then make it to pierce in all ways that you can, if it is not too deep inside.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because it does not need to be pierced so deeply into the wound, and then heal it, as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spine-like instrument with which one makes the fistula is quite sharp on one side and notched; and on the other side it is not, because of this one does not catch those things that one must not catch at all, as you see here:
des emorroydes	the blood vessels
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Evulsions are according to two manners: or they are inside the fundament, just like grain of resin, and there are small ones and great ones, and in court always blood, and sometimes one or more, and are outside the fundament and at the chief of the fundament; but those that are outside so have a lot of moisture, and in court always a drop of clear water or a drop of blood, and have the color of the body; and the cure of those who have them inside the fundament, is that you command the patient to spit for to let go in chambers, until the fundament comes out, and appears the root; if it hurts him, and it cannot be held by forceps, take it on your finger, then cut off at its roots; and if the skin cannot hold because of their moistors, take them on a cloth, or a cotton, or on a piece of felt; and extract with your hands, then cut, and powder over some hot powders that are in place of cautery; or you cauterize them just as it is said in the chapter of cautery, then cure with other cures until they be healed; and if the fundament cannot come out, then cleanse the patient with a sharp and bitter purgative to wash what is inside the fundament, so that it can come out openly; when the patient feels pain, and the root comes out from the fundament, it is easy treatment; and it is that you take them on your finger or with forceps, and cut, then cure just as we have said, until they be healed, and he fears incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you bring the thread in this manner: take twisted thread, and put it on a needle, and then draw the thread up and make the needle pierce on the other side, and turn the two ends of the thread under the needle, and make them be of equal length; and bind the thread firmly, then tie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do thus with all the others, and leave it for a while to let the superfluity of blood drain; then put on the bottom a linen cloth moistened in rose oil or cerote, and put it on the bottom, and instruct the patient to rest; and then let him be until he has ceased bleeding, and when they have stopped, then cure them with ointment and other treatment, until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	of the drying up of the fistula or foundation.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there has been a drying up of fistula in the intestine, and due to natural constraint, and when the illness is old and medicine is not effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary that you scrape off the top layer of a boil or on your fingernail the scab above, which does not let it moisten; then cure them until they are hardened as is proper; and if it cannot harden, then begin again to scrape more strongly than before, until it heals completely, and is scabbed over; then cure them until they are healed.
dou fremit	of the fistula (or abscess) in the intestine.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	A termite is a small appearance located outside the body, and it goes deep into the interior; and at some time the frost finds it, and one feels it just like dead movement, and comes to the entire body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose or a strong pheasant feather, and place that quill on the termite so that it circles the termite all around; then turn your hand over to cover the entire quill all around the termite, and push it deep, and extract the termite from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see fit, then make it of a thread of silver or iron in this shape, and be subtle under it and drawing on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it may stay at the tip, and press hard. And if you see fit, then cauterize the furuncle, as it is written in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of an enema.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes one makes an enema of silver or vinegar, or melted tin or cloth, and sometimes one makes those small and large instruments, according to which they are made for them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Then the ones that are made for use in the treatment of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The shape of a small and large enema is as follows: the top is wide, or the belly is tied in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there is a hernia where the belly is tied, as you see, and the navel is pierced from inside; and has two holes on one side and one on the other; and the belly is placed on medicines from an animal bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is a space of one finger between each hole, then fill these holes with a strong thread of twisted yarn in the shape of X or about that, and gather the belly as a goat; and when the medicine is inside, tie it up with a strong thread before an instrument from a thread, then use a suppository; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot nor too cold, and anoint the top of the poultice with oil or almond oil, or a similar thing, then insert it lightly into him; then grasp the poultice with both hands together until he is completely dry, then remove the poultice, and lift up the patient's legs to the height, and if the medicine wishes to come out, so bind it as long as possible; and if he sleeps one night entirely, so is greater aid.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you purge with the enema for the disease of intestinal obstruction, and the medicine hastens to come out, then repeat it as long as the patient is not healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at their root or abscess, so be the poultice as subtle as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle poultice on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds.
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds; and now we will speak of the treatments for hands and medicines, according to their fulfillment.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the place or location where they are made, and of what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things through which wounds are made are by striking with stone, and cutting with sword or knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar things; or that are done according to the places of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or on the head, or the breast, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds of the head, because the remembrance will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, be careful if it is from a fall of stone or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is great, and you doubt a little of hot abscess: so make him heal immediately with a cephalic salve; even if there comes pus from the wound, and let the patient drink wine and thick meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to heal, so that his food be diminished, and he do not drink wine, nor eat meat; and put on the wound a cloth, if a hot abscess comes, wetted in rosed oil alone, or in vinigrette oil; and if there is no hot abscess, so put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it has not been moved by air, powder which I will say about later; and if the burn has moved it, so put on some ointments until he be healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like a cut from a sword and similar things, and the lips of the wound cannot be joined together by stitches, then join them together with a suture, just as I will say about belly wounds in the chapter on suturing.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone and suppurates, and holds only by a small amount, cut it out; then cure the wound with medicine, and replace hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat thick meat, such as roasted testicles and bread, as well as chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find skin rotting, and it is not touching the bone, cut out all the rot, and pour out pus, then cure it; and if it has an artery in the wound or vein, do not cut without caution, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie off the artery, and if you cannot loosen it, tie it with a thread; and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light, and it is that you put in this powder that closes the wound even when the fire has dried it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; and live calce three parts, and grind it finely, and apply the wound with it, and hold it firmly, until it dries well and joins all its own blood; and then bind it tightly, and let it alone without loosing, if it does not swell; for one does not remove medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one makes this powder solely of sal ammoniac, when there is no incense or dragon's blood, but the fire has dried the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the ulcer has become infected by worms, just as in this state, do not put on it this powder; but apply some digested ointments, or balls of barley flour made with water and honey, so that they discharge pus; then cure with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you afterwards about fractures of the skull.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but if the nerves of the neck or an artery are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the nerves, then there should be no other treatment except leaving the cure and not putting anything constricting on it, because it hurts the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but if you are skilled in medicine, such as a wash made from rose oil and vinegar, and a wash also made from apple cider vinegar, and other herbs like this, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then sew it up and bind it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and high and full of pus, then pierce or lower down; and if the artery is cut and there comes bleeding out, then stop it, and bind it up, and cauterize as necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the tube is guarded by which the meat goes, then sew up the wound on the skin of the neck, but do not touch the throat itself, but rather put it back in its natural shape; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for some days, and then cure with ointments that have been made so that they are clean until they are healed; and if the wound has pressed into the bone, then search out; and if there are pieces of bone, then extract them all if you can, but leave those that you cannot take, and let the wound become inflamed, and discharging, and adhering to its exit; and if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and an abscess (fistula), then treat it as I have said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or knife.
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's a blow from a lance or a knife, and the wound is deep, then look to see if there are convulsions beside the wound in the patient: know then that the wound is mortal; and if it's not deep, and it's fresh with all its blood, don't put powder on it at the first hour, nor bind it for the blood that doesn't clot in depth, and will return to the heart, and kill the patient; but put attractive ointment on it, and tie it twice a day; and if you don't have ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to suck out excess moisture, and make the patient sleep above the wound three days, or four, or more; so there won't come spasms, nor male trembling of the heart, nor strange convulsions; and when you see good dispositions, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure it then with tents and other treatments, as long as it is healing; and if it cannot heal, and work, then know that there is a fistula; so treat it as one must.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is a cut of sword or knife and it's simple, or worse, on the back, then treat it with the cure that is before; if it is large, sew it up; and if it is small, apply powder; and if it has splinters in the bone and they are loosened, scrape out the wound, and remove any foreign bodies if there are any; and if there aren't any, let the wound fester, for this will help the extraction; and of other wounds on other limbs make the judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly.
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupturing of the belly is great and middle-sized and small; from the large wound sometimes a intestine or part of an intestine comes out, because of which the introduction of them is bad; and sewing up is more difficult, and at times it's worse for the smaller wound than the larger one, so we put more force into the intestines when putting them back in, if we don't put them in hot against hot, because the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, and they go back together better, and therefore it's worth more to reset the intestine to its place rather than other two. And know that the tearing of the belly is according to four manners: the two common sewings occur in the sewing up of the belly, and the sewing up of other wounds of the body and the two other proper sewings are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more proper with the sewing up of the belly, and I will say each one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines is protruding, and there's no need to intervene, it can be done in one of two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner: moisten a sponge or a wool cloth in hot water only, or cook it in boiling water with cypress and spikenard, and hold the intestine until the swelling is gone; and sometimes make this happen by restraining it, and be careful that it not burst to deflate.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestine with water or boil the bandages that are cooked, because by these means the opening is helped to the point of a thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch in the wound with the instrument with which we cut hemorrhoids; and the first treatment is careful not to cut the vein, for there must be no cutting without great necessity; and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut inside in the curve and outwards no, and see here the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is stretched out, and the intestines leap forth, then return them to their natural place in their proper location, if you are able, because that is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is large, and it is in the lower part under the belly, then you should have the patient lie on his back, and put his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part under the belly, then put his head and chest higher than the lower parts, and also similarly for a wound of the belly that is in one of the two parts, place the injured part so that it is higher than the other; and thus you should attend to what I say about big and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	Make the patient dress in their clothing, then take a thread or a yarn that covers all the wound with your hand, and bring together the edges; and this is the common way of stitching, and is to take one needle or more, according to the size of the wound's breadth, then leave a half inch at the head of the wound, and insert a needle where it has good strong thread; and pierce the two holes in the skin with the two holes of the siphac, which is under the skin inside, until you make them pierce from that part, and bring together the two ends of the siphac, then tie four times; then strain one double thread around the needle from both parts, then bring together the two edges of the wound properly, and then leave a half inch, and insert another needle; then tie the thread as you have done the first needle, and do not stop doing this with the needles, until all the wound is tied up; and be the needles various, between thin and thick, for the thin needles cover all the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot well enter: therefore it is necessary that they are varied; and it is not necessary to thrust the needles too far into the flesh and skin, lest they tear and open the wound in front of the suture; then pierce the ends of the needles, so that they do not prick the patient at night, and I put tents or cloths on the ends of the needles for good keeping, and leave them until the wound is sewn up; and this way of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, because one needle suffices, the second suture is common, and is that you bring together the two holes in the skin and the two holes in the siphac together on a needle where there is strong thread; and when you have pierced these four holes altogether, then remove the needle from the part where you began, as one sews clothes; and leave a half inch between each stitch, this stitch the men know, and I sewed up a wound that had in his stomach, who was hurt with a knife, which wound was more than a palm broad, and the intestines were well two palms long, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to him the intestine after it had been twenty-four hours further, and the wound was sewn up just in fifteen days, and he healed, and was cured.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the physician had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where you could not find any, nor any medicine; and I placed clean cotton on top of the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was cured.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and attach it to the outer part up to the inner part; when it has pierced straight through in a straight line, then take the top thread of the suture or the needle that you attached and make it pierce from the inner part out to the outer part; and the understanding of this stitch is that you sew just like tailors do with furs, and that you leave once the suture on one side and pick it up on the other, until the entire stitch is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second manner of suturing, which the Greeks call properly, is such as anyone does, who join together the two parts naturally assembled, and apply one end of the silk to the other end in this way: put a needle or point of thread nearby, and make it pierce only that place, and leave the two ends of the silk; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the outside part up to the inside, at the two ends of the silk; then make it pierce one and the other from the outside part up to the inside in two other holes of the thread that are on the other side; and this is the proper manner of suturing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	The Greeks call this phrase and anyone testifies to it, that the belly should be sewn with two needles, where there is thread in each; and one should put one needle from one side, and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who sew shoes; and know that when an incision is made inside the belly, then the suturing is more difficult than at other places of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as those of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, just like the fire has moved it, then return to the intestines, and the gut; then put on the powder of white chalk, and if the fire has moved it, then put on any ointment that is available, until the wound is closed; and sew up the skin, and the flesh; then cure the wound as with others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then put on, immediately when it begins to close, old cotton and stir it two times a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you do not need other medicine in most dispositions when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not become common infection of the main members, it is necessary that you moisten light wool in tempered hot oil or in rosella oil, and put it around the armpits, and under the shoulders; and if it feels pain or irritation in the bowels, and this often happens, then cleanse with black wine tea enemas, and similarly if the irritation comes just to the intestines; and perforate within, and know that when it is the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines that are called "jeun" cannot heal when they are injured, and this is because of the fragility of their veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and the approach of its nature to the intestines.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gutting thread springs from the wound, replace it in the same way as the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and become black or dark, you must bind the part that is black, so that bleeding does not occur there, for it has veins and arteries; then tie what is between the thread, and hang the two ends from the lower part of the wound until the gutting thread falls out, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the rupture of the belly.
