Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn and the wound is small, it can be restored in some men, because I have seen a man wounded with a lance to his belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it was sewn up and became a fistula, and there were discharge and flatulence coming from it; I applied treatment according to what I knew, and did not cease to refine it until he was healed, and the place sealed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewed, I doubted that the patient would be ill in his belly; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, he must be tied in this manner: take a great fistula, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the fistula has opened the mouth, put it on the two lips, so that they hold its mouth shut; and then knock his head, and this holds so well that he cannot untie it, then put another fistula after in this manner as before, until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief is inflamed in the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, and one can tie the intestine with a thin thread that has been cauterized from an animal's intestine in this manner: take the end of this thread from the intestine that is very well drained, and then tie it at the head of this thread with a fine linen thread twisted together; then insert the thread into the needle, and sew the intestine, and pull it back through the sewing, and this manner of stitching with fistula is not far off from the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, just when it is in one of the lower intestines, there is no remedy or cure, except subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or whatever kind it may be.
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that every wound or abscess, when it festers, is called universally "fistula", and indeed when it becomes thickened and runs over.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the verdant nodation lacking soft and pale flesh, or where one does not feel pain, and it is also thickened like a bird's feather; and sometimes it runs clear pus, and sometimes thick; sometimes little, and sometimes enough; and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that every wound which is not healed, and there is no meat, it is caused by one of the nine reasons: it is to say, by the scarcity of blood or body fluid; or because of its malice; or because there is hard flesh inside and above the lips, that does not allow new flesh to grow; or there is too much pus; or the place is rotten, and the material is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the treatment; or because the corruption is a manner of plague; or because the property of the region is slow digestion, and slow healing, and it gets worse by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these reasons, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now it is necessary for me to let you know the treatment of a fistula that is done by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas occur in all members of the body; for they come to the large veins and arteries and nerves or to the scrotum or intestine or bladder or to some of the ribs or to the spine of the back or to any joint of the hands or feet; and thus to the principal part of the member, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this manner are grievous to treat, and there is no remedy except for labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come exactly to the place that I said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you recognize it, then take a tent of tin or iron, if the fistula is straight, cut it; and if the fistula is twisted, search for a subtle tent of cloth, for cloth bends easily around twists; and if the fistula has many perforations and you cannot well search it with tents, then cleanse it by way of one of the perforations, for moisture runs quickly from one perforation to another, and purifies it; then cut the abscess as far as your skill allows, that you know if there are bones or nerves, and it is deeply embedded, and ask the patient well about the pain they feel when pressing with your hand, and in what place they feel it; and when you truly know where it is, and if it is away from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I told you, then close it according to what I told you, and remove the false discharge and corrupted flesh that are within; and then cure it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply rooted in the right place, it is necessary that you cut deep into it, as long as you can, then put moistened tents of medicine there, and insert them up to the head of the fistula, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then apply unguents to fresh flesh, until they are healed; and if they are not healed by this, then cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the fistula, close it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves do not hurt the main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean it out until all the corruption is removed, then cure with things that make flesh so long as they are healed; and if they are not healed, and return to their previous state, know that you have not gone far enough: uncover and scrape down until you reach the bottom, and remove all the corruption, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too deep, and you cannot come near it: then there is no remedy but to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it out with pincers, pull it out with an instrument suitable for this, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, do not leave any one of them; and if the moisture opposes you, and there is no error or fear, cut and scrape away the flesh, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, so put a thing inducing rotting on the wound, and leave it until the surrounding flesh is rotten around the bones, and then they will have more easily broken; and if it is a large bone, such as of leg or thigh, so clean only the corruption as long as the blackness is entirely removed, then repair the wound; and if there is a great part of it corrupted, and comes just to the touch of the bone; so you must scrape and cover all up to the corruption, and then heal it until it is sewn; and I will tell you of an abscess that occurred in a man's leg, so take example and aid in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man around thirty years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came inside the body, so much so that the materials came to the leg, and he had a large abscess, and there was no reason outside to open it; but the doctors worked foolishly so much on top of it that the abscess opened, and they drained out a lot of material, and it became a fistula, and there were many openings that all poured forth and moistened from the body; and many doctors applied treatment around two years, and there was no wise man in the art of hands, until I was called to it, and saw his leg and the medicines with which they treated him, and what poured out through the openings was a large amount of pus; and the young man's body became red, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these cavities, and then searched all the cavities, and found that one came against the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurried and dug into one of the cavities until I uncovered a part of the bone, and it was corrupted and pierced, and the corruption came up to the inner bone; I removed what appeared of the corrupted bone, and believed that there was no other corruption except for what I had taken out; and I began to heal the wound with soothing medicines over a long time, but it could not bind together; and then I repeated, and found the bone as before, and discovered the continued corruption in the bone, and removed it, and thought of joining the place; but I did not succeed until I dug around a palm's length into the bone, and pulled out all its marrow, then healed him with medicines; and he was healed and bound quickly, and there was no need to continue the work except for the weakness of the patient, which could not bear it, and because of the fear of death that I had from him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir. Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, you must do it thus: take a linen thread, and stretch it at the head of the bone that appears, and command someone to hold it up; and put another linen string, thicker than the first thread, and tie it on top of the skin which is above the bone, and pull down the corrupt skin beneath, and uncover the skin on the place where you want to see, so that the sawing does not hurt the skin; and take a tongs or a board under the bone to cover the corrupt skin; and you must sow as long as you can see and feel the corruption, and sew again another time.

Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess of the groin.
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Carbuncle is an abscess that arises under the armpit of the hand, or the foot, or perhaps it arises in other places; and when it has grown old, and one does not take care of it, then a large abscess forms, and it pours and discharges pus until it runs along the root of the boil, and perhaps all the way through; and comes the corrosion right up to the bone, so that it causes stinking pain, and the head of the fistula is wide, and its color is black.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés. Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cautery is a great help if the bone is sound and the boil is healthy; and if the boil presses into the flesh, begins to prick and tear it, then you must put hot oil under the boil that pricks the flesh, pour it up high, and cut out that subtle and delicate flesh, and apply on the remaining flesh medicines that burn and corrode in order to remove all of it; then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the ulcer is in the bone, cut it out and take care, for as long as the bone is corrupted within it, it cannot heal; and if you see the two bones corroding, cut them off just like it was said before, then cure them until they are healed; and if it is infected, boil it, and put a poultice on it, and it feels great pain, so it behooves you to cure it first; then cut the ligament above the spur with a crosswise incision, and be careful that the blade does not come up to the flesh which is under the ligament, for the patient would feel too much pain; and if it happens, put something on top that soothes.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of deafness in the hand,
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The bones that are born in the hands of some men by chance are entirely fleshy, and by chance there is a piece where there are bones, and sometimes it has a ligament, and one of them is born at the root of the joint, or the birth is in certain nooks of the bones.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with any defect in the navel does not move, and he who is born at the jointure of the navel, perhaps moves; the height of one who is fat so is light, in such a manner: measure him in his root from an arm's breadth.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who arises in the root of the joint is difficult to cure, if you are not skilled enough to cut it.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who was born with or has a hernia at the rear navel, it is necessary that you cut off the flesh around it as far as the bone first, then cut the bone to a suitable thread according to him, then care for it until he is healed.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The swellings that come on the fingers together come from birth, or from a blow, or from burning with fire, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	It is necessary that you cut the suture, so that it may be repaired according to its natural forms; then put between two tents or dampened cloths in rose oil, so they do not close; or you put between two pieces of thin linen, until the place is sewn up, as it is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If swellings come to any of his fingers with the palm, then cut off that swelling as it is necessary.
des vils	the evil ones
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	They are swollen and inflamed veins full of melancholic superfluities that come to many members of the body; and there are more in the legs of those who walk on foot and work and carry loads than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	It is therefore necessary that you administer to them sometimes cleansing with vinegar, and then purify them with basilicum.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The cure of iron is in two manners: one is to cut them and bleed the black blood; and the other manner is that you open the vein and drain it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The cutting is in this manner: first heat the leg with a hot iron very strongly until the main vein is subtleized, then tie the patient's leg from above the knee down to the part below the kneecap; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, with a large blade, then elevate and bleed out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can suffer; and then tie it, and command him that he eat bland food mixed with dark vinegar; and resume the evacuation and bleeding when the veins are full, and cause harm to the patient.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The limbs of the patient are prepared in this manner: wash the leg if there is much hair, then soak it in water and let the veins swell with hot iron until they turn red, and inflame the veins; and if you do not have a basin, heat it on the fire, and then apply a long lance to the main vein of the knee or in the part below the ankle; then scrape the skin around the vein, and strip away the vein from each side until one feels it; and it will be seen red and black, and when it goes into the skin it seems like a white string; then put back the flesh beneath so that it rises above the skin, and then soak it in water, and apply another ligature on top of three fingers; then scrape away the skin over the vein until one feels it, and lift it up as you have done, and apply another ligature as you did first; then apply another bandage or more if needed, then lift it up, and tie it to a wooden stick, and then apply it to the next bandage, just like you did first; then apply another bandage, and lift it up, and tie it; and take out the vein in length after length until it is all free, then apply another ligature; and if you cannot pull it out and raise it, put a needle through the entire thread that is very tightly doubled, and tie it, and insert it beneath the thread, and turn your hand this way and that until something comes out; and be sure it does not cut, for if it cuts, one cannot draw or lift it, and it will harm the patient; and when you have drawn it all out, apply damp wool in vinegar and rose oil to the place of the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and coiled together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must cut it obliquely, but do not cover it; and treat it in the way that we have previously said.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The form of the iron that is used to cut the vein should be curved and not sharp, lest it pierce the vein; and it is a thick curvature, for if it were fine, it would puncture the vein, but let it be thick as we have said, and this is its shape:
de la voinne civile	of the common vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is located in the legs, in the warm parts where there are no herbs or tree, and in dry earth; and it may arise elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens because of the corruption that comes from under the skin, just as serpents and worms come out inside the body between the flesh and the skin.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein so are that it comes in the leg a very great inflammation, then the place changes and the vein begins to come out, just as a root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein opens up, then it's necessary that you wrap around a piece of linen cloth of one and a half to two hands deep, and a node, and leave the linen cloth on the leg, and every time it points out at the far end, so wrap it around the linen cloth, and the node; and if it is too long, then cut off a part, and wrap up the remaining part, and do not cut off in its root, until it comes out completely; for if you cut it, then it goes into the flesh, and brings abscess and corruption to the place, and makes a bad disease; therefore it's necessary that it be treated bit by bit until the end, and none of it remains in the body; and at times this vein when it is treated two palms long, or ten, and once an hour came to me, from which it issued ten palms long, and when you cut it, then a hole or a pit opens up, and perforate until the bottom, so that everything comes out; and the material inside becomes empty, and apply medicines against corruption each day, then it cures just like abscesses.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And at this point there are many rainfalls of blood, and indeed when it bursts into the joint of the foot or the foot itself, or there is a lot of pus, and from which it runs rainfalls; then cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	the worms that are born between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This illness is called in our land "bovine disease", because it has occurred many times among oxen, and is a small worm that is born between skin and flesh, and goes throughout the body ascending and descending, and the person feels it well from member to member, until it bursts through the skin where it goes, and runs out; and it is infested with corruption of some humors, such as worms and serpents and fleas and hookworms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it goes through the body, and it rises to the head, and it comes into the eye, by chance it enters, and destroys the eye; and this has occurred many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it healed and drawn out, there is no certainty that it will cure itself; so you must bind the area above and below with a strong and tight ligature. Then strike up and draw it out, and if the worm is deeply embedded in the flesh and you cannot find it, cauterize it with fire on top until it rots; and the greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said. And if you see it approaching or its head near the eye, then press under it a small loop, then strike up, and draw it out. It also behooves you to use cleansing of body medicines with dissolvent properties for bad humors and to keep him from spoiled meat which causes putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to some members, and it can move from member to member; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to a sick woman, and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise as quickly as an insect on the shoulder, just like living silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and settled in the shoulder, and then shortly after it ran throughout the body, until it came into the other arm; then she told me that it would come back around the body, so I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was greatly amazed at how it moved from member to member, for I had never seen this illness in that manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I had always thought that the pain would move from one place to another well, but I did not see it so in the woman; and I thought that this was because the woman's body was dry, and her veins were uncovered, and for this reason the swelling appeared constrained; and they do not appear so according to this reason in those who are plump, and have moist bodies and closed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to curing this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens as we have said, then bind above and below hastily, and then lance on top so that the swelling is forced back into its place; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it with your own eyes, then cure it from those who induce swellings, such as fetid pills, and scorpion pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	from arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The fleas are diverse, according to their appearances and the places on the body where they bite.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of theirs is that there are those with large points, and small ones, and barbed ones, and pointed ones; and those with two angles, and those with shafts, and those with pieces; and that which shoots into any member does so in two ways: either it shoots in the principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, womb, reins, intestines, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it falls into any place of these members, and the sign of death that I will tell you hereafter, appear to you: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for many die afterwards in various dispositions; and when this evil sign does not appear to you, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out, and cure the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits it and pierces the bone, and shoots out the dura mater which is above the brain, is when scotomia and sodor and esvertin and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and mixture of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there are fluids coming from the nostrils, or the ears; and perhaps the speech and voice are lost; and shoots out a white moist wound like pus, and also like the rotting of flesh; and if these signs appear to you, then beware of the cure, and pull out the arrow if it is not in.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign of the arrow when it pierces the heart are that it is close to the left breast, and feels as if it were stuck in a hard thing, not an empty one; and perhaps the arrow moves as the hairs do, and there is black bloody discharge, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: know then without doubt that the patient will die.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the signs of the flea bite that never affects the womb is that pus bursts forth from the wound, and the throat swells, and the sick person changes color, and gasps deeply and seeks cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the flea bites in the covering of the belly (i.e. the abdominal wall), it is near the small ribs; and there is great anguish and great pain, and gasping; and all the muscles of the shoulders are convulsed.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the flea bites in the stomach, perhaps something of undigested meat will come out from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the flea bites in the belly, and it bursts through the intestines right away, then there is no hope of a cure, nor of extracting the flea.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the flea bites in the bladder, and the urine bursts out and comes forth, and the sick person feels a very painful sensation: know that the wound is mortal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and arms and throat and shoulders and adjacent parts and spine of the back and feet and calves and similar ones, are safe according to various dispositions. (i.e. the flea bite is usually not fatal in these areas)
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the flea is in the nerve or artery and it is venomous, as I will tell you that happened to me, because you are doing the same thing. (i.e. this text is a personal account by someone who has been bitten by a venomous flea)
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to the wife of a nobleman that an arrow struck her in the eye near the root of the nose: I tried it, and pulled it from the other side under the fat of the ear, and she was healed without any harm.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I drew out an arrow that had struck a boy in the fat of his eye under the eyebrow, and the arrow was bent back, and could only be pulled out by the tip towards the bowstring, and the arrow was as large as a Turkish archer's, made entirely of light iron without ears; the boy was healed, and no bad accident came to him.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And extract an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and the arrow was Arabic with ears: I filed the barbs, and made it so fine that I drew it out, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And extract an arrow from the home of a man, who had it stuck in his belly, and thought he would die; and then that thirty days had passed, his condition did not change; I cut into the arrow, and bound it, and drew it out, and had no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you want to extract an arrow that fell on the back of a man, and the wound was sewn up above; and the arrow remained inside him, and did not change his natural disposition, nor found any harm in any of his natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And you see another man, to whom an arrow fell in his face, and the wound was sewn up; and it remained thus without suffering great pain; and many others similar things.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And extract an arrow from the home of the prince of kings, which was stuck in his neck, and was slightly leaning towards the right side; and the arrow was completely lodged. I was summoned to the cure after it had been stuck for 3 days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I searched all around it with a fine cloth and didn't feel anything; and he felt a sting and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow I put on the place a plaster attractive and digestive, so that the place wouldn't swell; and the place of the arrow appeared.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster again for many days, and the wound was resolved once more, and the patient remained so long that he felt the arrow one day within his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I apply a medicinal astringent liquid to the wound by hand for several days until it is fully open; and I tested it; and felt the head of the arrow which was drying out at the place; then I inserted into the opening of the wound with that medicinal astringent liquid so that the head of the arrow appeared visibly; and passed well in a period of about 4 months; and then burst the wound so that I put forceps on it, from one side and from the other, and it could not come out; then I did not cease to subtlety and to ingeniously invent instruments, until I caught it the first day with good forceps, according to what its shape will appear at the end of this chapter, so that I could take it out and restore the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the wise men judged that the nasal cartilage could not be restored; I then restored it, and the wound was sewn up, and the patient was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care on what I do not say; for books cannot take in everything. But wise and skilled masters can gather well from a small thing, and from that which is present and failing, find new work, and new equipment, at the descent of strange things which happen in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows do not emerge from limbs or are stuck in them except in two ways: either through the place where they enter, or on the other side; and those that exit through the place where they entered are arrows entering fleshy parts, and may jump out at some time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not jump out now, then leave it so that the flesh around it is putrid and the issue becomes clear; and similarly if it is stuck in the bone and cannot exit, leave it thus for some days, and move it every day; and then it will jump out, and if it does not jump out, pierce around it with a very fine needle, so that the area around it is widened, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the arrow is stuck in the bone of the head and goes up to one of the stomachs of the brain, and any of the accidents that I have said are apparent to the patient: do not pull it out at all, but leave it until it becomes even after some days, for if the arrow comes close to the skull, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the bone itself and does not come close to the skull, and the patient remains for some days without a bad accident, then it may be extracted.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very fixed in there and cannot come out further, I administer tar to the area, as I have told you; then cure the wound until it is healed. (i.e. this suggests that even if a flea has burrowed deep into the bone or flesh, treatment with tar may help to loosen its grip and allow for healing)
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is reset in its place in the body and it cannot be seen, search for it thoroughly throughout the whole tent; and if you feel it, extract it with any suitable instrument. And if you are unable because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, then let the wound be large; and extract the arrow if you can, and if the arrow has ears to which they hold, cut away the flesh that is stuck in them from both sides as far as you can, and then break or bend the ears of the arrow until you can pull it out; and take care well that you do not break the arrow, lest you make the extraction more difficult.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it at once, then leave it until the area around is corrupted, and then pull it out, because the extraction will be facilitated. (i.e. this suggests that sometimes, letting the wound or area around the flea become more inflamed or corrupted can make removal easier)
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding is contrary, so administer what we have said of the treatment in its chapter; and beware of incision to the nerve and vein, and note how you can draw out the arrow without peril, soon or late, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the form he was when the arrow struck him, for this is the greatest help that it is, and if you cannot, so put him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if it pierces any part of it, or the skin is swollen in place where you can see or feel the point clearly: cut then above, so long as the pincers can take hold, and then pull it out: if now it springs out.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then turn your hand around carefully, so that it enters the bone and enlarges it, and then pull it out. (i.e. this suggests that if a flea has burrowed into the bone, you should use a gentle but firm motion to coax it out by creating a larger opening in the bone)
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, so leave it and then resume the extraction until it comes out; and if the shaft of the arrow is in it, so insert the entire shaft; and if the shaft slips, and you see administering fire, so administer the instrument pointed, so that the point of the arrow enters into the hair of the instrument; and then push forward, and if the arrowhead is stuck, so insert the instrument with entering point, to ease out the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is stuck, it is necessary that you cut all the flesh around where the poison is, if you can, then heal the wound as it seems proper.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the chest or belly or bladder or rib or side, and it is close, and you can cut on top, if you do cut; and be careful not to cut the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then dress the wound, if necessary; and cure it as long as it is sound.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the tongs used to pull out fleas are similar to the beak of a bird, and see this form: (i.e. this suggests that the tool or instrument used to remove fleas is shaped like a bird's beak, possibly indicating its ability to grasp or pierce the flea's body)
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And they come in many sizes: large, small, and medium, according to the size of the flea. (i.e. this suggests that the tool or instrument used to remove fleas comes in different sizes to accommodate various types and sizes of fleas)
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the arrowhead is also like the feather of a bird, to hit at the point of the arrow, as here is the shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of pincers for pushing and testing if this is so:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the tendons of common muscles
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	Of the veins from which one gets well are XXXI, of which there are XVI on the head, that is to say: two pulses which are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and the two arteries which are in the two temples appearing; and the two veins that are in the two eyelids, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the neck; and the two jugulars which are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the lips, on top of the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and the two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The common veins that we commonly save are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and they call the simple people "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "basilic", and it is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call the simple people "vein of the heart"; and the basilic itself is on the right side, and they call the simple folk "vein of the belly", and it is above the armpit, and that one from which we save, which appears manifestly over the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saphenous vein is the vein that is between the little finger and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and at the foot are three veins: one is under the fold of the left side elbow, and the second popliteal which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "saphenous", that is on the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg are three veins under those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of the veins that are behind the ears is said to help the cathartics in the past, and the migraine; and the quality of the vein bleeding, as I tell you, is that you lift the patient's head and rub the place where the veins are with a rough cloth; then tie the patient's neck with a screw so that the two veins appear behind the ears in two dependent places from the head: which is to your good, and where you feel the pulse under your arm, make it sign; then take the lancet and push it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand all along the vein upwards and strike and cut well through the skin and the vein in two; make the blood come out as much as you see; then stop and bind it so that it is healed.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding from the two arteries that are in the two temples, is worth to emigrate a long time, and is accustomed to be made an old style, and a habitual eye wash, and in the vessel of sharp tears for the eyes; and the quality of the bleeder so is as I say: and it is that the patient tightens his neck, until the two veins are apparent clearly; and feels the hair under your chin, and then signs to get up; then lift the key over the vein on high at your index finger, and push the lancet underneath, and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, as you have done in the other two veins, and make a bandage of blood according to your necessity; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then tie it firmly, and let it stay until it is healed; and we have spoken already about their amputation and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein from the forehead is worth as much as the bleeding of the cephalic vein in ancient face diseases and migraines and rashes; and its quality is that the patient twists his neck so hard that the vein appears; then take the instrument which is called "fosseur", whose form is this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And put the point on the vein, and press with your hand, or something else, and let two bloods come out according to what you see; then tie the patient's neck, and bind the vein so that it is closed and there is no bleeding at all.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not necessary that the bruises are too sharp; and the incision crosswise, because the bone is close, and perhaps break the bruise when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of the two veins that are in the armpits helps the eyes, and the itch, and the redness, and the yellowing in the eye, and the diseases of the face; and the quality of their blood is that the patient tightens his neck by twisting with a rope, as before; then let it bleed, and be the bleeding of a width twice as long as the thread, not very wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the bruise is subtle, perhaps it will break through; then make sure to close the blood vessel, so long as you need to, and then tie on cotton, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein of the neck is worth against ague, and sudden fever, and diseases of the face, such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient tightens his neck, then strangles his neck with your left hand, and take the fine thread long, and place it in the gap between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open well there, and the blood will start to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then bind it one night, because it is very quickly restored; and this is the shape of the thread:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The salve of two threads helps to constrict the vein, and at the beginning of suturing, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corrosion, and in herpes, and in swellings; and the quality of the salve is that the patient binds his neck under one thread and the other, as we have said; and let the master be on top of the patient's head, and the patient sit on a seat, then salve the vein of the long piece somewhat widely, then tie off the blood temperately, or as much as necessary; then make another part in the other vein, then release the ligature, and hold the veins moderately, so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until morning, when the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The salve of books (or possibly "the writings of salves")
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The cutting of the veins on top of the lips helps against bleeding in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and splits in the lips, and around the nose.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the vein is to have the patient sit in front of you, and strain his neck as I said; then turn the lip, and look at the two veins, one being on the right lip and the other on the left, and they are recognized by the fact that they are black, and by the small dark blood vessels around them: cut both of them, and if you do not recognize them, and you have doubt, then cut the largest of each side, and do the same for the two veins above and below, because it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the vein under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The vein under the tongue is helpful after the vein of the forehead, and it is for the narrowing of the throat, and diseases of the eye, and diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the surgeon is that the patient sits between his hands in front of the sun, and raises the tongue, and looks underneath on each side for a black vein: cut then both and do not go too deep, for under them are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the throat, from which one commonly extracts blood, are cleansed according to two manners: either they prick at all with a flame of myrrh, wide and large, or an olive oil subtle as a surgeon's knife, and it is called "anesil"; and they are wide and subtle according to the wideness and narrowness of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the myrtle leaf is very well-known, and is wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the veins that are thick and full of evident blood, and that contain much blood and trouble; and this is the form of the olive oil flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate to cut, and is for cutting subtle veins, where there is subtle and yellowish blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The vein of the basilic, which is one of these veins, helps in illnesses that are below the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the belly; and it is necessary for the surgeon to bleed him carefully, and beware of the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he strikes the artery, and a flow of blood comes forth, then it is necessary to cauterize, as I have said; and he should not prick with the flame, but cut like "anesil".
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic vein does not open obviously, it is necessary to extract it, and replace it with another one; or you want some of its branches removed, or you clean around it in the arm: it opens obviously; and the wound at the base becomes inflamed, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of the wound, it is necessary then that you extract the arm, so that you touch the place until you feel the pulse; then mark the place of incision, and then bind the arm, and open the vein at the base which becomes inflamed; and be careful not to strike in the artery when you see the place swollen, for it is the artery: withdraw then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it come out high like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and fine, know that it is blood of the artery: hurry then, and put your finger on long, then take away your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; bind the arm, and leave it, and do not move the patient; and be afraid for him, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the bleeding is not stopped, and you are summoned, and there is no medicine present, then cut the artery if it appears, because the head will recede; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a peel of fig tree bark, and make it into a poultice, and take one half and tie well just above the other joint; if the blood stops, that's fine; if not, then treat with the powders which stop bleeding; and the hemostasis is not very serious in many dispositions for the small size of the wound, and the strength of the arm tendon.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.
