The juice of the vein in medium so helps to treat bleeding from the head above and body below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it behooves the surgeon to be careful for the nerve which lies below, and if he probes too deeply and finds the nerve, and it swells up and the bloodletting becomes serious, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve appears many times, and since in some men it is so subtle that it does not appear, then you must remove the vein from the instrument without touching the nerve, and withdraw the nerve to your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there are veins between the two nerves, then tear them long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding of the cephalic vein so helps, that it draws blood from the head and helps the eyes; and it is necessary to bleed with a flamed olive or a flamed myrtle, for it is the most safe of all the veins, because it has no nerves nor arteries underneath.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	In any case, it is necessary to seek the lightest place and do not hurt anything if one fails the first time, and try again; and by chance some men's joints swell when one fails the first time, but it does not cause harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cutting is according to your thought. (This sentence seems to be a conclusion or a summary, indicating that the decision to cut the vein is ultimately up to the person performing the operation.)
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is not done except to preserve health, and to ward off illnesses from coming; and the bleeding should be made in one of the three veins that are or cut: that is to say, cephalic, facial, and basilic; and it should be bled at the beginning of spring, summer, and after eating in autumn and winter when the sign of fullness appears; and it should be bled on the first day or the third after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The physician who administers the remedy to the sick has no fixed time determined for treatment, but rather whenever it is necessary by day or night in all hours and at all times; and it does not seem right to treat children until they are 14 years old, nor a pregnant woman more than three quarters of a month up to seven.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should old people who are over 60 years old be cut. (This sentence suggests that surgical procedures may not be suitable for older individuals, possibly due to decreased physical resilience or increased risk of complications.)
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone wants to be treated, in whatever way it may be, they should have the intestines cleansed with a light clyster if he has many bad humors retained, so that the veins do not draw out superfluous substances harmful to the main members; nor does one get cured who is too full of meats, or drunk, as long as he remains so, or dropsy; and be careful not to treat after a passion of colic, vomiting, and purging of the belly, and frequenting women, and travail, watching and sleeping, and all such vices, either by virtue of arms or of body; then subtilize the humors, if the blood is thick, by meats and drinks and medicines, if you have the power; then enter into a bath, if nothing prevents it, to subtilize the blood, and cure of the vein around the third part of the belly, as we said; and guard that day from travail, and pain, and lust, and similar things; and be joyous and happy, and let the physician be higher than he whom you treat, and wet the arm two or three times, then twist the thread above moderately, for when it is too tight or loose, the blood cannot flow out; and then moisten the physician's hand with the flame of an old oil, then put his hand on the right side over that vein below the place where one wants to treat, so that the vein does not become inflamed and split open upon striking.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	There are veins that flow like strings to the surgeon, and there are those that are filled with windiness, so that when one puts a flame on them, they withdraw from the flame and cannot be opened; and thus it is with some of these; and if the vein bursts open, the wound is too narrow, therefore the surgeon should be advised in such things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein closes at the first time, that's good; but if not, then try again shortly below or above that place where you started, as long as the swelling is not increased. (This sentence suggests a strategy for handling cases where the initial attempt to cut the vein does not succeed, by reattempting the procedure in a slightly different location.)
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the swelling is inflamed and the patient fears, let it be left for one or two days and do not bind up the arm: perhaps a festering abscess will form; do not let him enter the bath, then resume the treatment if he pleases; and if the wound is small, or the vein runs shallowly, and you doubt that it does not flow so much blood as you see, place your entire flame into this very same opening; and make a poultice promptly, thus as long as the swelling is inflamed; for such things have happened many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the swelling filled with fluid, do not begin to lance it again, and put some linseed oil on top of it, because it lightens the body from blood, and is moist in this place where the oil lies; and thus administer the linseed oil in each lancing that you lance the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same thing does to treacle and poppy milk, when you put it on top of the swelling; so subtly let the abscess come out and burst when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess that has come many times, just when it is not well closed again after that time or the opening of the vein is small, then be in haste and put on the place a moist sponge in water and with vinegar a little warm, and hold it for an hour; and you must do this after the blood has stopped flowing from the vein, and if there remains at the place after some days any discoloration or greenish color, it does not harm; and if you see fit, put on something of aloes or myrrh dissolved in rosewater, camphor, or similar things.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times the abscess and inflammation has occurred at the cut of the Basilic vein: so put then your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the touch of the hand, that is the bad appearance. (This sentence seems to be describing a specific medical condition where an abscess or inflammation occurs at the site of surgery, and advising the use of physical examination as a way to diagnose this condition.)
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not put anything on it from what we have said, because perhaps it cuts without bleeding of the artery; but make one dry poultice to harden the place, then let it be cured by another treatment, until it is healed. (This sentence seems to be advising caution and suggesting an alternative approach when dealing with a specific type of injury or condition, possibly involving the use of a dry poultice to help control bleeding and promote healing.)
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And consider each blood separately according to its quantity and color. (This sentence seems to be emphasizing the importance of careful observation and consideration when evaluating different types of bleeding or hemorrhaging.)
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow out until it becomes red; and if you see that it is thick, let it flow until it thins out; and if it is too hot, let it cool down. (This sentence seems to be advising a gentle and gradual approach when treating bleeding or hemorrhaging, with the goal of achieving a balanced and healthy state.)
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for the person who is weak and frail, and needs bleeding with bloodletting, that one make a larger wound, and let the flaps be wide; and for the weak one, do the opposite, and have to heal slowly and often, and one should heal in cutting across, not by piercing; and this manner of healing is safe from bleeding out of blood and cutting into nerves, and it's worth more than a long incision or a wide one.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for the person to whom the body fails in healing, it is necessary to give a damp compress soaked in apple juice; if they are overheated, then apply the bleeding three or four times; and if they have a cold complexion, then moisten the compress with a sweet syrup, or with an aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chickpeas, and a well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he spits up at the vein, after issuing of much blood, then it is necessary that he drinks a broth made of meat, and a fragrant subtle syrup, and uses the other things that we have said in the chapter on fainting, for the evacuation of blood.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to vent his arm and heal another time, it is fitting, when he is weakened by much surgery, that he heals bit by bit, according to the quantity of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to vent his arm after the first surgery, and he has a strong pulse, heals himself in seven hours after the first surgery, or after nine hours.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to heal from another place, should heal on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is much blood inside the body that is already heated up, and causes fever; so it is necessary to draw out a great quantity, and widen the opening until it bleeds into a basin; then you should reward all the conditions of a vein, and put your hand on his pulse when he is bleeding, so that death does not come instead of bleeding, and this often happens when the leech is negligent; and it is not necessary when you see to untie the arm, and let blood for the second time, and the opening is closed, that you press strongly up; nor if it is crooked, that you stretch out his arm quickly, for that would be bad; but leave it until he bleeds for a second time; or you prick at the point of the flame, as long as the congealed blood is issuing from the vein into a basin, and put on a piece of silk soaked in water, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vomit is stopped, leave him alone and do not restrain him, until the swelling has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to let out blood again, then he heals in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arm are healed instead of the veins in the head because they are composed differently.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the manner of the cure is such that the patient places their hand in hot water until the abscess becomes red; then it must be bound moderately so that the vein appears well; then the abscess must now be cut through, not long or wide, and the incision must be large, and it must be cleansed well near the joint of the hand, and if pus cannot come out, then place the hand in hot water, and let the pus remain in the water until you have enough; and if it is cold, then do not plunge the hand into hot water again, for it is put more in winter than in summer; and this cure for the abscess is safer than all other abscesses, because there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The cure for the inflammation of the right hand is worth as much as all diseases of the liver, and this is how it is done: strain the hand and place it in hot water until the abscess is swollen if you can see it; and if you cut the abscess crosswise, and you take everything out completely, then nothing will be hurt; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are under all the muscles bare of flesh, and then place the hand back in hot water if the pus is congealed in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have let out blood as much as is necessary for you, then put oil and thread on the vein to sew it up quickly, and do so with each person.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The healing of the spleen in the left hand is worth for the disease of the mumps, and do everything just as I told you for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blemish of the shoulder joint is worth for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the liver, and retention of flowers, and disease of the reins, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of its treatment is that the patient puts his foot in hot water and rubs on it until it peels, and binds above the joint of the foot; and the vein is at the ankle, and over the leg go many veins; treat then the largest vein, or one at the ankle, which is worth more.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, it will ward off the worms that are underneath, and the juice will go through as in cutting; and let the inflammation cease.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the swelling cannot come out, then put the foot in water and leave the affected area well drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the treatment fails the first time, it is repeated a second time above a poultice, because the place is salty; nor should you doubt of nerve, as we have said, and thus treat the shoulder of the other foot similarly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The swelling of sciatica is on the knee of force (or strength), and its juice heals the pain of the back when it's very hot.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of his urine is such that the patient enters into a bath, and extracts on top of the ankle four turns while twisting, for otherwise the vein will not appear; and if it appears, then clean the urine in every way that you can, and crosswise; and be careful that you collect it, for the place is clean, and it has been well received by many men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find it, then clean any blood that appears on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make as much flow of blood as you see, and then untie the bandage, and put on a pad and bind it in place; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of venesections
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made from horns, or copper, or glass; and cupping is done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this venesection which is without wounding is in two manners: either it is with full force, or with little force; and the venesection that is done by wounding and extraction of blood is done on 14 places of the body, of which one is entirely in the top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others in the sides of the neck; and the venesection under the chin; and the venesections on the shoulders; and the venesections above the buttocks; and the venesections on the arms; and the venesections on the legs; and the venesections on the ankles; and this venesection does not treat blood, but only small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and for this reason it has no great effect, just like a vein treatment; and it must not be administered, nor with full force nor little force, in any disease that comes from repletion, until all the body is emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of sickness it is necessary to bleed, or for habit, so we bring them to bleed each hour in the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between, and each time; for there are such that, when they need to be bled, they have a heavy head; and those who find repletion and redness in their face, and in their head, and in their neck, and darkness around their eyes; and those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, and have fled the tongue, and are bleeding; and there are such that dream, and see by bad blood and injury and death and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially since it is in the month of March, we will command them to be cupped after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bloodletting from the neck so helps against the greiteness of the head that comes to the eyes, and it is not necessary that this be after the evacuation of all the body's blood; and this bleeding is in place of the cephalic bloodletting, and it is not fitting for those who have a cold complexion to use it, or who have quartan fever, for this does them great harm; and because of this, it is not fitting for the elderly to use it, nor for those who have head diseases that are cold.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become forgetful, and therefore it is advisable to place the cup more down towards the back of the head in order to avoid forgetfulness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation through the neck is in place of the natural humor of the head and of the belly; and therefore it is worth it for the constriction of the bowels, and the rupture of the canal of the womb, and for all ailments, and for repletion; and it needs to be pressed, because if it holds too tightly, then it obstructs or perverts the stomach and the heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The venesections at the two costal arches of the neck are worth for the pains of the head, and for dimness, and for migraine, and for strangulation, and for the pain of the roots of the teeth, and it is in place of the humor of the belly; and you must command the surgeon that he extend his hand to make it, so that he does not compress the artery, and draw out blood in short measure.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The sweatings on the chin are worth for diseases of the mouth and gum corruption, and similar ailments that are in the mouth; and it is in place of the healing of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The sweatings on the shoulders are worth for diseases that come from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The venesections of the sides are worth as much as the three veins of the arm, for they draw blood from these large veins; and command the surgeon that he must not cut too deeply, for the place is bare of flesh, and lies near nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass that is on the buttocks is worth for hemorrhoids of the fundament and diseases beneath it. And the cup should be large and made of lead, so that it can thoroughly drain. And if it were subtle, it would probably break and cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The cupping glasses on the legs clearly heal (or remove) the blood from the entire body, and are worth for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and gallbladder, and they cleanse the pores. They are in place of the two saphenous veins and the two ankles. And however, after long use, they weaken the body and bring on paleness in many dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to put on the cupping glass is that you first put it empty, and then suck temperately, and place it hastily, and move it evenly, and do not stop doing so until you see the area turn red and swollen, and appear the color of blood; then insert (the needle), and re-place the cupping glasses, and pay attention to the condition of the body, for there are some who have a lot of flesh, and clear pores: it is necessary to prick only once, and it is necessary to make large and somewhat deep wounds, and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, it is necessary to prick twice: the first time to thin out the way of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, it is necessary to prick a third time; and when we want to draw out the blood little by little, we only need to do it once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, then we recommend often; and if the blood is thick, then prick deep, and the ends should be pierced suddenly, and it concerns he who has hard skin and rough, and who have large pores, that you anoint the places of the cups with oily appetitive and dissolutive oil: whether it's in autumn, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or oil from the seed of cucurbit; and if it's in winter, with hawthorn oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the superfluities are thick and cold, take bitter almond oil, or balm oil, or anise oil, and similar ones.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the person to whom one applies medicine has tender skin and large pores, then it does not concern putting on oil, but it concerns washing afterwards with rosewater, or cold water, or water of mulberry, or cucumber water, or water of pear tree, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have too much moisture, should rise from ash, or water of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have gross surplus liquids are lifted by old wine, or by vinegar of honey, or by a decoction of wormwood or camomile, or by similar things; and it is not necessary to bandage with a poultice in front of the bath or after the bath, but an hour or two later; and he must not sleep afterwards, but rather be awake, when he should be pouluced and when he is pouluced.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And take care of those who are sick and choleric, and their blood is too bitter and inflamed; then it is necessary that he takes cold things, such as green apples and endives and lettuce in a sauce, and similar things; and mutton broth, and beef flesh that is moist.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, then take syrup of honey, and medium-smelling wine, which is between old and new, and mutton broth, and mutton juice and young birds and chickens; and the day that he will be pouluced, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men sometimes treacle or musk before the poulticing, or after, in order to comfort the main members; and thin out the blood, but it does not need to be drunk by those who are hot.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The apertures that are made with an iron blade are those that are placed on the liver, and on the spleen, and on podagra, and on the belly and the navel and the hips and the thigh, for these members do not endure being pierced there; and it is done only to draw blood from member to member, as we place on the shoulders when the fever subsides; in order to remove viscosity that is in the member, as we put a blister on the belly and on the navel to reduce the swelling; and to remove pain, when there is inflammation or stone, it removes by its attractive virtue by chance the inflammation, or dislodges the stone from its place; and thus does it when it is placed on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained effusion of fluid; and these blisters are administered empty only to suck; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes full of hot vinegar, as in the disease of the pleurisy; and in such a manner one fills the blister with warm water alone, or with water in which herbs have been cooked that are beneficial for this purpose.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the cupping glass administered with fire is this:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The instrument must be two palms and a half in breadth, and have the edge on the outside around the middle a small notch, as to thrust a needle, and it should be of brass, smooth before so that it does not hurt the patient when putting it on the member; and there must be in the middle a rod transverse of brass or iron, to put a candle enclosed, and they should be both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for children's poultices are different from old people's, and thin ones from fat ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must put this poultice on the member: take a candle of wax or ointment and put it inside the poultice at the end of the rod which is inside the poultice, so that the light is at the bottom of the poultice so as not to burn the patient; and then place it on the member, and you must have the poultice over the notch that we said, so that when one wants, if there goes vapor, remove the poultice; and take the ointment again as before, and start again often, if you need.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping device which is administered in the disease of pleurisy at all times, there is no rod nor tube, and it is not administered except when it is full of water, and it is placed on the member only; and this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Cups are not administered except on members where you cannot put cups for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and on flesh-free joints, such as toe or knee, and other similar ones. And the quality of the patient is this: when you find cups that are in sweet clean water without sedimentation, take them; and soak one cup in sweet water, until they become familiar and have nothing inside; and then let it be cut open by a vein and a cup, then scrub the member until it is red, and put on the cups; and when they are full, and have swelled, if it is a place where you can put a cup, put it there, for it will be worth much afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the seat of a boil, and then with hot water, very well, and then apply it; and if the boil heals too slowly after the blood has been drawn out, then soak a linen cloth in cold water, and put on it, until the pus is stanched; and if the pus is multiplied, then put on vitriol or gall or similar things, until it is stanched; or you place a mixture of peeled green peas on the boil, and let them be heated against the boil, which will now stop bleeding; and if you need more, take other poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the poultices do not want to take hold, then rub the seat of fresh blood on it, or you stick a needle in so that the pus comes out, and then put them on, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up; and when you see that they are dripping, then powder over a pinch of aloes and burnt silk or ashes, which will now stop.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the beginning of the Book of Bruises.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and are a restoration for bruising and purging.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that foolish men gaze upon this chapter, which they have never seen in any of the ancient books or letters; and for this reason is the science estranged in our land, for I have never found one good; and I know nothing except through the science of the ancient books, where I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and abridged at the end, and shown clearly the forms of instruments that are brought forth, just as I have done in these two chapters preceding.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we say the prologue of this book, which sums up the words and chapters where the wise person puts their understanding, and remains on the truth, so that those who are proven know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when breakage or dislocation or torsion or crushing comes to someone, it is necessary for you to hasten in healing the patient from one side and the other, unless some thing prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or drunkenness, or old age; or if the time is not very hot, or too cold; and if they have a cold choleric temperament, that is to say, cold juices, and meat of bird and goat, and do not drink wine, nor eat greasy meats, and do not fill oneself too much with flesh foods which fill the veins with blood, until you are certain of hot aposteme or spreading of matter in the member; then let the patient recover quickly under your first-hand governance as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bone begins to heal, it is necessary that you feed the patient with foods that make thick nourishment, or they have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and eggs, and peas, and beef, and fish fresh and fat wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with good nourishment the wound heals faster and sooner the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you should know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well reattached or soldered according to their nature because of the drying of the limbs, nor those also who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but do not care, reset on the fractured bone large splints which have been seasoned and joined the limb together, so that it strengthens itself such as it was before; and do not take away from its work, and therefore it must be fed with thick meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that bruises are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the bruise of the head is different from the bruise of the thigh or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of a bruise.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are bruises that turn into swellings, and others that become incisions, such as the cut of a pen nib for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a bruise with an open wound, and a bruise that has a small crack or fissure all over it.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And it should have its own device and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what comes back into place; and it is known that there is a break in the bone by what is twisted or apart, and it sounds well by pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or sound at the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no break; but it can well have twisting, or fissure, or small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	So it is not necessary to move the joint with your hand, but put on remedies that come later, and then gently tighten it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in a bow shape, and are the two parts disjointed, they should be placed at an equal point now, just as abscesses of hot water come; and if abscesses of hot water come, let them remain any day, until the abscess is calmed; then put it level with the joint that you can handle lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of this one is more light than the restorations of those where there are pieces; then bind it, as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and it is extended by two parts, whether it is an arm or a foot, or on your hand it is a small member, or of two strings, or of one string and your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, then you should bind back together with all sorts of appliances the additions in their places as best you can, and guard that through your work there does not come to the patient injury or pain; and join well the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And if it feels not well to the touch, as if it were not well, then dress it beautifully and do not tighten it too much, nor press it like those who bring hot aposthems and contractions to the member, as we have said many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is positioned correctly, instruct the patient to keep it still so it does not move, whether in sleeping or waking, turning or any other manner; and be sure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet in place, and you must put it in such a position that it feels no pain; and be careful that it is put back straight, so that twisting does not occur when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is as I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken members are diverse in smallness and greatness and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar ones: you must wrap them in a soft and subtle linen cloth; and those that are large, such as thighs and calves: you must wrap them in a wide and strong thread, for the wide threads encircle the entire great limb and hold it equally from all sides, so that there is no looseness. Then tie around gentle bindings, three or four times according to the limb, and grip with your hand a knot on the whole thread, then go above the break and hold it less tightly, so that the break will be slightly apart from the break; and soften the thread somewhat and somewhat, until you take a large part of the healthy place, then take the other thread and turn around again above the broken limb; then go back to the lower part of the break and hold it moderately, neither too tight nor too loosely, as we have said in the first lesson above; then put between the threads cloth or linen bindings, until they are entirely even; then tie everything up with a bandage, and then put your straps well made on top, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If there is an abscess or swelling, then put on something soothing the swelling hot, and which extracts the swelling, and let it be thus for some days; then attach to it a poultice of moistered cloth that has been scarified in half, as wide as a large cane strip, or made from wood used to make skewers, or palm fronds, and they should be according to this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the poultice which one puts on the break is a little thicker and larger than the others; and be as long as it is necessary for the member of smallness or largeness; then attach to the poultices in the same way as you did at the first dressing, then tie above a cord moderately, just like at the first dressing on the break; the tighter it is, the more so; and it must be that the cord be medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and they should be of soft linen; for if the cords are thick, as I have seen in the works of fools who do their bandages with twisted linen threads, and this is a great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it must not have between each poultice less than two fingers' breadth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is hurt by the threads of the strings after the straining in their healthy places, then put under them poultices of linen, or torn flannel, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the fracture, and the ligament is broken, I will say the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not need to strain with strings all the broken members on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	When the members are large, there is no need to apply ointments too quickly, unless after 5 days or 7, or more according to your safety of abscess overheating; and behold here the manner of ancient plasters for restoring breakage, dislocation, and twisting: and it is that you take flour that is held by the walls of the mill, and mix with plenty of egg, and put this concoction, neither too clear nor too thick, and use it, and it is the common method of the plaster restoring breakage to many dispositions, and indeed for women and small children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another manner of poultice restoring fractures, dislocations, and torsions: take 3 parts of asafoetida, gourds, and mugwort, 10 parts; myrrh and aloes, 5 parts; alecithin, 8 parts; and make a powder of them, and mix with a lot of egg yolk. If the complexion of the person is hot, use this poultice, for it has good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is worth to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another manner of ointment that is worth for twisting: take musk and costus, about 10 drachmas; myrrh and aloes, about 9 drachmas; acaica, 6 drachmas; Armenian balm, 10 drachmas, and grind well, and mix with water or plenty of egg, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to plaster joints and bones that have been dislocated from their places, and calm the pain occurring, and the fracture: take new linen, and soak it in oil and cooked grease, and put on the place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These plasters do not restore [the bone], but they are good for calming a hot abscess, and properly removing the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another manner of poultice that restores broken bones: take dry leaves of a fig tree and earthworm leaves, and grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to plaster to restore the breaking of the bone and to reduce the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of balm, camomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one; and crush, and mix with vinegar, and if the member is heated, then mix with moisted water of coriander or of water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster more strong than the first one, when a hard abscess comes at the restoration of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of viper's grapevine, and seeds of flax, balm, marigold, and savory, and flowers of violets and chamomile, all in equal parts; and grind, and mix with vinegar of salt, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Hippocrates writes that when restoring a broken member, one should not apply on it something more than wax made of candle wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two states: neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should apply on the broken member things dry but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another manner of poultice that is worth for lesions and pain: take mugwort and sheep's wool or bird feathers that have been soaked in vinegar, and ground ivy, all in equal parts, and grind them together, and make a poultice with it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen the dressing a little afterwards, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has the bone moved from its place; if it does not loosen by hand for many days. And if pain comes to the place, or itching, without rest or swelling, hasten and loosen it, and remove the poultice now; and take a light cloth, and a wet sea sponge, and dip in water, and lift the place, until the itching ceases, and the pain is calmed; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, dampened in water or rose oil, and tie up with a bandage, so that you are sure of hot abscesses; and calm the inflammation of the limb, and have removed the pain, then repeat the gentle binding, and a little poultice, and do not pull it too tightly as before; and bind until they are healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the hot swelling and redness and pain and inflammation have been completely removed, and you need to apply poultice and binding again, then repeat it, just as you did first in the same way.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member any of what we have said, then do not untie it until after three days or four or five or seven; and sometimes leave it twenty days, as is seen, so that the swelling decreases and approaches the flesh on top; at which point it becomes more swollen than before, and its flesh grows more thick, just as I said before; and if you see the place drying out more than necessary, know that there can be no swelling; then take away hot water compresses from it, every time you untie it, and drop one part of vinegar in it: by this work, therefore, the swelling is prevented from the member, and correct quickly what foolish people do, who left the member twisted incorrectly: this is bad, and it is a fearful operation, and I see nothing else but that it should be released and done correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Il semble que le texte se termine ici et passe à une nouvelle section intitulée "Des diverses manières de brisure". Je vais essayer de continuer à traduire :
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many ways of breakings are, and diverse figures, and the causes are specified; for there are breakings that are made by percussion of a sword, and the arm breaks all the bone right down to sifac which is under the bone, so that it does this just as an axe or wood fust does; and because of this it is called this way of breaking "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone from above without piercing it, and is called this manner of breaking "absolute"; and the wound of these two breakings is great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is struck with an axe, or split, or fist of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it is a breaking that pierces, which approaches just to the skin that is under the bone, or it is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that is reunited in the bone as subtle as an ant's claw, and the crack is small, and because of this it is called this break "capillaire"; and if the wound that is made or by striking with stone, or by falling, or by something similar, and makes enter the piece of the bone downward, and the place is hollowed out so that as furnace-makers do when they strike up on the furnaces, thus it enters the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to children who have soft bones in the head, such as a child's; and it occurs in all these ways of breaking that small fragments are separated like these; and I will speak of them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all manners of breakings by the signs above them, and the inquiry that has been done, and by the corrupt flesh that is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary sign is known by this: when one has uncovered the bone and rubs it lightly with a cloth, if the break opens black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care to avoid accidents that can befall the patient, and if you see no evil accident, such as vomiting blood, loss of understanding, swelling, paralysis, fever, or if the limbs become pale and red, and other similar signs in various conditions, then he cannot heal with any doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming accident and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the wound first comes to you, and it's in winter, then it is proper to remove the bone before the 14th day of the moon that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hasten to remove the bone before the 7th day, so that the skin under the bone may not become corrupted, and the accidents which we have spoken of may come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the break of the bone comes just to the skin that covers the brain, then you must split the broken part thus: and you take hold of the head of the patient in pain, and uncover over the bone in all ways that you can, and on the appearance of the wound more softly than you can, and if a bleeding of blood appears to reveal the bone or a suppurating abscess, then the aid of those who need it is, and you must fill the place with dampened cloths in olive oil; and make the wound rest as long as the suppurating abscess is calmed, and be assured of stopping the bleeding; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done in two ways of work: one way is that you cut at the narrow tailing before, and this is the form
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I apply another stricture more larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have a number of diverse strictures, some narrow and others wide, pointed and made of iron; and work on them lightly, so as not to cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and strong, it should be pierced around it, so that you may apply strictures with awls, not too deep so as not to pierce through the bone of the head, and it should have above the point a border or one circle, which does not let the point pass beyond the bone; and you should have several, so that each one comes back to its place on the edge of the bone, so that you may have awls for all the heads; and this is the form of the three methods of awls:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is that you place one awl on the bone and turn it with your hands until you know the bone is pierced; then put the awl elsewhere a little bit later, and do this all around, then cut with the nippers the space of the bone which is between the piercings, and do this as finely and lightly as you can, as we have said, so that you bring out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have such as pincers, tongs; and be careful not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
