When the break of the bone is restored and after healing remains weak and fragile in the member, this happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was tied too tightly, and not tied as it should be; or because there were too many ligaments, and the nourishment could not reach the member; or due to excessive inflammation; or due to too great movements, not in its proper time; or because it has too little blood in its body, so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you feed the sick person and make their body tender, as long as there is plenty of blood in them; and have them take baths, and give them joy and comfort; then put poultices on the member, so that the poultice attracts a great nourishment, and draws out the inflammation with an absorbent cloth, as long as the nourishment comes to the member, and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	of the deformed member after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the member is twisted after healing, and the broken bone is exposed, and the shape of the member is ugly, even so it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish people who say that you should break the limb all over again, and many foolish men have done this in our land; and this practice is blamed, and comes to great harm, and perhaps death. However, if the nodules and twisting are fresh, it is necessary that they be drawn out with hot water or cooked soothing herbs, such as leaves of valerian, roots, and melilotus, and similar things; and make a soft plaster, such as well-made dyacquilon, and take the pulp of valerian, and mix it with goose fat or oil of sesame, and make a plaster on top; or take fatty figs, and grind them with collyrium powder, and similar medicines that soften the joint.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the swelling is removed by constant and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And bring the member to gentle movement every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is hardened and turned to stone, so that it needs to be removed with an iron instrument, then you should cover just up to the bone with a small, sharp incision, and put a poultice and a salve in the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	It begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocations occur when a joint moves out of its place, why it cannot move, and the limb is misaligned, and the patient feels great pain and great injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When a dislocation occurs to anyone, if you must now bring it back to its original place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the swelling will become inflamed, and by chance it will be set on fire at the swollen place; therefore, do not move it until it is swollen: often comes the pain and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, have the patient relieved first, then let him go, as long as the abscess has been calmed; then warm the member with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and cure each member just as the treatment will come to its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from head to toe.
des mandibules	of the jawbone
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	What happens when the jawbones are dislocated and they are dislocated in two ways: or they are slightly out of place and a bit softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang towards the chest, and cut off the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot hold it, nor can it close its mouth, and envelops its tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns to place by itself in a few days.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must reset it promptly, and do not delay; and in such a way that the attendants can hold the patient's head, and insert the mirror into its pouch with one of their hands at the root of the jaw dislocation inside the mouth, if the dislocation is in two parts; and the other hand should be outside to make it equal; and instruct the patient to relax his jaws, and move them in every way.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the attendant puts it back together evenly, so that it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw returns is difficult, namely if it are the two jaws together, then heat them with hot water and oil, until they are rinsed lightly; and do not wait for the return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment, and the patient's mouth is closed well with a softened salve, so put on damp cloths in a cerote made from rose oil and wax, then bind it lightly with soft threads; and let the patient sleep on his back, and his jaws be between two cushions, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor does he make any effort to eat, but takes light food, until the pains are gone, and the jawbones are sewn together; and then gnaw whatever he wants lightly, and do not stir himself to open the mouth while eating and drinking, as long as the jawbone is well sown and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be returned to place within an hour and are not converted back to their normal state, it will lead to fever and bad habits, and possibly diarrhea, and perhaps vomiting of cold, clear fluid.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see these symptoms, then know that it is a bad sign, and understand that the person who experiences them will die in 8 days.
de la forcelle	This appears to be a title or heading, possibly indicating the start of a new section in the text.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The dislocation (li forcele) cannot be reduced from the side towards the spine within its usual course, and is never reduced to the outside, and one can easily feel it.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back often, and stretches out his arms; and then presses strongly with your palm at the joint, and it will come back; then put on the poultice and bandage, and secure it; and the shoulder which is near the armpit cannot dislocate; if not, and if it dislocates once, so reset it to its place, as we have said; then put on the poultice and bandage, and secure it, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed; and in the same way is restored the shoulder of the scapula when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	This appears to be a title or heading, indicating the start of a new section in the text about shoulder dislocations.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: 
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they have a blow or fracture, and the shoulder becomes swollen with a hot abscess, and they think that it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So it is necessary to examine it thoroughly, until you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when they are downwards towards the armpit, and make a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among their diversity evident; and you will find a pit at the head of the shoulder, and beneath the armpit at the touch of the head of the shoulder, just as if it were an ulcer; and the patient cannot bring his hand to his side, nor move in any movement; and also, if it is dislocated upwards, it is not hidden, because you find it manifestly at the touch; and this type of dislocation is not otherwise than to reduce when it is new, or if the child is diseased.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister lifts the patient's hand up, then places his palms under the collarbone, and lifts the joint with force upwards to its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, then places it down; and it will come back quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in three days, then it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and the assistant should apply a warm and soothing poultice, such as a decoction of alfalfa, fenugreek, and mallow in water, and it should be applied; then have the patient lie on their back, and put a linen cloth under the armpit, not too soft or too hard, then put the weight on the heel above the cloth, and lift the head of the shoulder gently, and pull the hand of the patient; and another assistant should tie down the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward; that shoulder comes back right away, and if you see it when it is reduced in this manner: then you have someone present who is greater than the patient, and they should be to the side, and push the patient's shoulder under the armpit, and lift the armpit up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and another assistant should pull the patient's hand downward towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, he can lift with him some heavy thing, and the dislocation returns immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And he is also rammed out in another manner: and this is by inserting a long stick into the ground, whose end is as sharp as a pike, and neither too thick nor too thin; then it should be placed under the patient, so that it touches him softly on the hip, and the joint will return to its place quickly. Then he should extend his hand downwards from the other side form a fist, and the joint will return to its place quickly. And if it does not want to come back for all these things we have said, do this cure: take a stick of two arms long and four fingers wide, whose end is sharp enough to enter deep into the armpit, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then tie a cloth over the top of the stick so that it won't hurt the patient, and place it under the collarbone of the patient; then stretch your arm across the length of the stick, and tie the other end to the stick at the elbow, and also tie the wrist of the hand, then place the arm on a wooden beam about as wide as a large plow, and have the hands hanging down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint will come back immediately.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is back in place, however it may be done, it is necessary that you put under the collarbone a spear of wool, then apply an ointment made from mill powder with incense and egg white all over the shoulder and around it; then tighten the bandage under the collarbone gently, and turn the string on the ointment, and wrap the hand around the neck, and let the hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that they be moved carefully little by little, as soon as the limbs are comfortable, because they will heal more quickly; and then move them again after five or seven days, and if it is firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come in, or for another reason, then you must apply cauters to three pores, as it is written before the chapter on cauters.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it loosens after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift his arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation which is near the chest, and the shoulders, or backside, is caused by sudden impulse, and stretching of hands, and it administers another injury; and cure them until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes stiffness to the member, and delayed motion, then the patient should bathe many times, until that stiffness is alleviated, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the hip
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the hip is dislocated to points, and returns to points; and it is dislocated from all parts, and even in front and back, and the dislocation is not regained, for one sees it well and feels it well; and dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the knife to the sick person with the cord, so you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is swollen, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it's necessary that you rub it gently while the swelling comes down, for if the swelling came down, it would be painful to move it back; and perhaps it cannot be moved back entirely, especially when it is in the back; it's worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and perhaps death may come from it.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is this, when it can be moved back like that, you extend his hand with yours; and his arm is stretched out, and his hands on the hip around, over, and under, and push the joint to its sockets together, or to the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he doubles his hand to his other hand, and pushes the joint back with the root of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and it happens that two people extend the arm, and bind it with two bandages, so that it does not move in extension; then turn the arm from each side, then wrap a double, long, and wide cloth around it; and when the physician has joined the joint to his hand, he anoints it with some oil to soften the joint, then inserts the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in place, he puts on dry plaster with egg yolk, binds it firmly, and lets the arm hang at the neck of the patient for some days, then releases it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, they should remove the bandage and leave it so. And if you see that the joint doesn't hold well, repeat the poultice and the bandage, and let it be for a while, until it's firmly put back, then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels grief after the reset of the joint, and it moves, then bathe him and scrub gently, and press so that it is alleviated; or you put on the joint a poultice of thick sheep fat, then leave for a day and a night, then take off, and let him enter the bath; and when he sweats, scrub the joint temperately, then put the poultice back, and then enter the bath; and thus do it two or three times until he is healed; and if you see fit, then put on warm moist cow dung with butter, and press on it; so it will return to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The text appears to be a medieval medical text describing the treatment for a shoulder joint dislocation.
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The articulation of the hand is dislocated, and the return is slight, more than other articulations Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place hastily, in the same manner as it was dislocated, so that there may be swelling or hot abscess at the joint.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the reset is that you put the sick hand on a table, and stretch out the fingers of the hand, and the thumb should be placed even, thus as if he places his palm on the appearance of the joint, and press so that it returns to its place. Nevertheless, it is necessary that you look if it is well in place; then put the patient's back of their hand on a table for extension and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the hand, then the patient places their back on their hand on the table, and the surgeon places their hand above the appearance of the joint.

de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and slow, nor hard; and use at first soothing poultices warm, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, then set the limb right now to its place, so that the warm poultice may come there; and when the limb is in its place, administer soothing poultices warm, and cure the wound, as it is fitting, with drying ointments; and if with the dislocation there is a break, and small bones are loose, then take them out, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and beware of entering into a path of fear, according to what I have said, for that will mislead you according to your Creator, and because of the ignorance of your hand and body.
Amen	So be it
